Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
6 min
Definition of Fiqh and Usul al-Fiqh
Opening definitions of fiqh and usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain how each qualifier distinguishes it from other types of knowledge.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of subsidiary legal rulings derived by reflection and deduction — not conjecture, not one ruling, not revelation.

This lesson unpacks the foundational definition of fiqh and usul al-fiqh as presented in the opening of Noor al-Anwar. The author carefully limits fiqh to a specific type of knowledge, excluding conjecture, isolated rulings, non-legal matters, and direct revelation. Understanding these exclusions is critical for distinguishing fiqh from other Islamic sciences and for grasping the scope of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of defining fiqh first
Recognize that 'usul al-fiqh' is a genitive construction (idafa); one must understand fiqh (the mudaf ilayh) before usul.
The author explicitly states this order.
2
Parse the linguistic definition
Find the linguistic meaning of fiqh as 'understanding', with Quranic evidence from Surah Hud.
The verse shows the word in context.
3
List the five qualifiers of the technical definition
Identify each term: ilm, jumla, shar'iyya, furu'iyya, nazar wa istidlal.
Each qualifier serves a specific exclusion.
4
Pair each qualifier with its exclusion
Match ilm with conjecture, jumla with one/two rulings, shar'iyya with non-legal, furu'iyya with usul, nazar wa istidlal with revelation.
This is the core analytical move.
5
Define usul al-fiqh
Understand that usul al-fiqh are the evidences (adilla) from which fiqh rulings are derived.
The term 'asl' indicates dependency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم حامداً ومصلياً أما بعد فأقول حق على كل ما حاول تحصيل علم من العلوم أن يتصور معناً أولاً بالحد أو الرسم ليكون على بصيرة فيما يطلبه وأن يعرف موضوعه (وهو الشيء الذي يبحث في ذلك العلم عن أحواله العارضة (له تمييزاً له عن غيره، وما هو الغاية المقصودة من تحصيله حتى لا يكون سعيه عبثاً. وما مسائله لتصوّر ،طلبها وما منه استمداده لصحة إسناده عند روم إليه هو من مضاف هو الأصول ومضاف معنى عنه البحث فيه من الأحوال التي هي تحقيقه إليه وأن يتصور مباديه التي لا بد من سبق معرفتها فيه لإمكان البناء عليها. أما مفهوم أصول الفقه فأقول : أن قول القائل أصول الفقه قول مؤلف الفقه، ولا سبيل إلى معرفة المضاف قبل معرفة المضاف إليه، فلذا تذكر تعريف الفقه أولاً ثم الأصول ثانياً. أما الفقه ففي اللغة عبارة عن الفهم (كما في قوله تعالى: مَا نَفْقَهُ كَثِيراً مِمَّا تَقُولُ (هود: (۹۱) أي لا نفهم وفي عرف المتشرعين الفقه مخصوص بالعلم الحاصل بجملة من الأحكام الشرعية الفروعية بالنظر والاستدلال فالعلم احتراز عن الظن بالأحكام الشرعية فإنه وإن تجوز بالطلاق اسم الفقه عليه في العرف العامي لكنه ليس فقها في العرف اللغوي والأصولي وقولنا بجملة من الأحكام إلخ احتراز عن العلم بالحكم الواحد والاثنين فإنه لا يسمى في عرفهم ،فقها وقولنا الشرعية احتراز عما ليس بشرعي كالأمور العقلية والحسية، وقولنا الفروعية احتراز عن العلم بكون أنواع الأدلة حججاً فإنه ليس فقها في العرف الأصولي، وقولنا: بالنظر والاستدلال احتراز عن علم الله تعالى بذلك وعلم جبرائيل والنبي عليه فيما علمه بالوحي فإن علمهم بذلك لا يكون فقهاً في العرف الأصولي، إذ ليس طريق العلم في حقهم بذلك النظر والاستدلال . وأما أصول الفقه فاعلم أن أصل كل شيء هو ما يستند تحقق ذلك الشيء إليه، فأصول الفقه أدلة الفقه. هي
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praising and sending blessings. To proceed, I say: It is incumbent upon everyone who seeks to acquire a science to first conceptualize its meaning by a definition or description to be insightful in what he seeks, and to know its subject (which is the thing in which that science investigates its accidental states to distinguish it from others), and what is the ultimate goal of acquiring it so that his effort is not in vain, and its issues to conceptualize them, and from what it is derived to validate its attribution when seeking... [unclear]. So understand the concept of usul al-fiqh: I say that the statement 'usul al-fiqh' is a genitive construction, and there is no way to know the mudaf before knowing the mudaf ilayh. Therefore, we first mention the definition of fiqh, then usul. As for fiqh linguistically, it means understanding (as in the verse of Allah: 'We do not understand much of what you say' (Hud: 91), i.e., we do not understand). In the terminology of the legists, fiqh is specific to knowledge obtained of a body of subsidiary legal rulings through reflection and deduction. So 'knowledge' excludes conjecture about legal rulings, for even if the name fiqh is metaphorically applied to it in common usage, it is not fiqh in linguistic and usuli terminology. Our saying 'a body of rulings' excludes knowledge of one or two rulings, for that is not called fiqh in their terminology. Our saying 'legal' excludes what is not legal, such as intellectual and sensory matters. Our saying 'subsidiary' excludes knowledge of the types of evidences being proofs, for that is not fiqh in usuli terminology. Our saying 'through reflection and deduction' excludes the knowledge of Allah Almighty of that, the knowledge of Jibril and the Prophet, peace be upon him, of what he knew through revelation, for their knowledge is not fiqh in usuli terminology, since the path of knowledge for them is not reflection and deduction. As for usul al-fiqh, know that the 'asl' of everything is that upon which the existence of that thing depends. So usul al-fiqh are the evidences of fiqh.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the book. It begins with the basmalah and then states the importance of first defining a science before studying it. The author explains that to understand 'usul al-fiqh', one must first define 'fiqh' because the term is a genitive construct (idafa). He then provides a detailed definition of fiqh: linguistically it means understanding, citing Quran 11:91. In the terminology of the legists (i.e., the scholars of Islamic law), fiqh is defined as knowledge (al-ilm) of a body (jumla) of subsidiary (furu'iyya) legal (shar'iyya) rulings (ahkam) derived through reflection and deduction (nazar wa istidlal). The author explains each qualifier: 'knowledge' excludes mere conjecture; 'a body' excludes knowing only one or two rulings; 'legal' excludes non-legal matters like rational or sensory issues; 'subsidiary' excludes knowledge of the evidences themselves (which is usul al-fiqh); 'through reflection and deduction' excludes the knowledge of Allah, angels, and prophets who receive revelation directly. Finally, the author defines usul al-fiqh: the 'asl' of something is that on which it depends, so usul al-fiqh are the evidences (adilla) of fiqh. This is a foundational definition in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): In the terminology of the legists, al-fiqh is knowledge of a body of subsidiary legal rulings derived through reflection and deduction.
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The evidences of fiqh, i.e., the sources and methods by which legal rulings are derived.
العلم (al-ilm): Knowledge as opposed to conjecture; certain knowledge.
النظر والاستدلال (al-nazar wa al-istidlal): Reflection and deduction, the method of deriving rulings from evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is excluded from the definition of fiqh according to the passage?
A) Knowledge of a body of rulings
B) Knowledge of one or two rulings
C) Knowledge derived from revelation by prophets
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is defined as knowledge of a body of subsidiary legal rulings derived through reflection and deduction; usul al-fiqh are the evidences from which fiqh is derived.

Defining al-Sirat al-Mustaqim: The Middle Path in Shari'ah and Aqidah
Defining the straight path as the middle way between extremes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-sirat al-mustaqim as the moderate path between extremes and apply this definition to identify the Hanafi position in both legal and theological issues.

Core Idea
The straight path is the middle way between excess and negligence in both law and belief.

In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi definition of al-sirat al-mustaqim—the straight path. This is not a vague concept but a precise legal and theological principle: it is the moderate path between extremes, embodied in the Shari'ah of Muhammad and the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah. By understanding this definition, you will see how Hanafi usul grounds rulings and creed in a balanced, evidence-based middle ground.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dimensions
The definition operates in two domains: Shari'ah (practical law) and aqidah (creed). Each has its own sets of extremes.
2
Analyze extremes in previous religions
In Shari'ah, the religion of Moses contained excess (severe penalties) and the religion of Jesus contained negligence (permissiveness). The Shari'ah of Muhammad avoids both.
Examples: cutting off impurity (Moses) vs permitting wine (Jesus).
3
Analyze extremes in theology
In aqidah, note the three pairs: Jabr vs Qadr (compulsion vs free will), Rafd vs Khuruj (excessive love vs hatred of Ali), and Tashbih vs Ta'til (anthropomorphism vs negation).
Each pair represents an extreme; Ahl al-Sunnah takes the middle position.
4
Derive the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position on any issue can often be understood as the moderate path that avoids the extremes. Use this as a tool to evaluate positions in fiqh and usul.
For example, the permissibility of wine for non-Muslims reflects a moderate stance between absolute prohibition and absolute permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1. معنى الصراط المستقيم والصراط المستقيم: هو الصراط الذي يكون على الشارع العام ويسلكه كل واحد من غير أن يكون فيه التفات إلى شعب اليمين والشمال وهو الذي يكون معتدلا بين الإفراط جانبها ا الله أي الشدة والتفريط وهذا صادق على شريعة محمد ، لأنها متوسطة بين الإفراط الذي في دين أي اليسر والسهولة موسی عليه، والتفريط الذي في دين عيسى عليه، وعلى عقائد السنة والجماعة، فإنها متوسطة بين الجبر والقدر، وبين الرفض والخروج، وبين التشبيه والتعطيل الذي في غيرها، في دين موسى كقرض موضع النجاسة، وأداء المال في الزكاة وقتل النفس في التوبة. (القمر) في دين عيسى: كتحليل الخمر قال في "نتائج الأفكار" ناقلاً عن "غاية البيان": إن الخمر والخنزير كانا حلالين في الأمم الماضية، وكذلك في حق هذه الأمة في ابتداء الإسلام، وورد الخطاب بالحرمة خاصا في حق المسلمين فكانا حرامين عليهم وبقيا حلالاً على الكفار كنكاح المشركات كان حلالاً في حق الناس كافة، ثم ورد التحريم خاصا في حق المسلمين فبقي حلالاً في حق الكفار ، ألا ترى إلى خطاب الله تعالى للمؤمنين في سورة المائدة بقوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِنَّمَا الْخَمْرُ وَالْمَيْسِرُ وَالْأَنْصَابُ وَالْأَزْلَامُ رِجْسٌ مِنْ عَمَلِ الشَّيْطَانِ فَاجْتَنِبُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تُفْلِحُونَ (المائدة: ٩٠)، والمؤمن هو الذي يفلح، وقال تعالى: حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمُ الْمَيْتَةُ وَالدَّمُ وَلَحْمُ الْخِنْزِيرِ (المائدة:3) انتهى. (القمر) وعلى عقائد إلخ: معطوف على قوله : على شريعة إلخ. (القمر) بين الجبر والقدر الجبرية قالوا: إن العبد جماد لا قدرة له أصلاً لا خالقةً ولا كاسبةً، ويرد عليهم بطلان الثواب والعقاب والقدرية قالوا: إن للعبد قدرة خالقة ويرده قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ (الصافات:٩٦) وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم القدرية محوس هذه الأمة، لأفعاله، وأهل السنة والجماعة قالوا إن للعبد قدرة كاسبة لا خالقة وأدلة الفرق في المبسوطات (القمر) وبين الرفض إلخ الروافض رفضوا أكثر الصحابة وأنكروا إمامة الشيخين والمسح على الخفين، وسبوا معاوية وأحزابه فهم أفرطوا في محبة عليه، والخوارج فرطوا في محبته حتى خرجوا عن الطريقة القويمة وحاربوا مع عليه وشتموا أصهاره الا الله وأهل السنة والجماعة كفوا اللسان وأيقنوا بأن الصحابة كلهم عدول الأمة وخيارها والأدلة في علم الكلام (القمر) التشبيه والتعطيل المشبهة شبهوا الله تعالى بالخلق وأثبتوا له الجسمية، فغلاتهم أصروا على التجسم الصرف وغير الغلاة قالوا: إنه جسم لا كالأجسام من دم ولحم لا كاللحوم والمعطلة قالوا: بكونه تعالى معطلاً كما قال الحكماء إنه صدر منه تعالى عقل أول ثم منه عقل ثان، ثم وثم إلى العقل العاشر، وهو العقل الفعال وعليه نظام العالم، وأهل السنة والجماعة قالوا إنه تعالى منزه عن الجهة والجسمية ونواصي المخلوقات بيده تعالى يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد. (القمر) الذي إلخ صفة لكل من الجبر والقدر إلى التعطيل (القمر) في غيرها : أي في غير عقائد السنة والجماعة.(القمر)
1. Meaning of the straight path. And the straight path: it is the path that is on the public road and everyone travels it without turning to the branches of right and left, and it is that which is moderate between excess (on one side) and negligence (on the other). And this applies to the Shari'ah of Muhammad because it is intermediate between the excess in the religion of Moses (severity) and the negligence in the religion of Jesus (ease). And it applies to the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, because they are intermediate between Jabr (compulsion) and Qadr (free will), between Rafd (rejection) and Khuruj (secession), and between Tashbih (anthropomorphism) and Ta'til (negation). In the religion of Moses: e.g., cutting off the place of impurity, paying wealth in zakat, killing oneself in repentance. (al-Qamar) In the religion of Jesus: e.g., permitting wine. He said in Nata'ij al-Afkar quoting from Ghayat al-Bayan: Indeed, wine and pork were lawful in past nations, and also for this ummah at the beginning of Islam. Then the address of prohibition came specifically for Muslims, so they became prohibited for them and remained lawful for disbelievers, like marrying polytheist women was lawful for all people, then prohibition came specifically for Muslims, so it remained lawful for disbelievers. Do you not see the address of Allah to the believers in Surat al-Ma'idah: 'O you who have believed, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone alters [to other than Allah], and divining arrows are but defilement from the work of Satan, so avoid it that you may be successful' (al-Ma'idah:90). And the believer is the one who succeeds. And He said: 'Prohibited to you are dead animals, blood, and the flesh of swine' (al-Ma'idah:3). End. (al-Qamar) 'And on the beliefs etc.' is conjuncted to 'on the Shari'ah etc.' (al-Qamar) 'Between Jabr and Qadr': The Jabrites said that the servant is inanimate, having no power at all, neither creative nor acquisitive; they are refuted by the nullification of reward and punishment. The Qadarites said that the servant has creative power; they are refuted by His saying 'And Allah created you and what you do' (al-Saffat:96). And the Prophet said: 'The Qadarites are the Magians of this ummah.' Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said that the servant has acquisitive power, not creative. The proofs of the sects are in the detailed works. (al-Qamar) 'And between Rafd etc.': The Rafidites rejected most of the Companions, denied the caliphate of the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar) and wiping over the socks, and insulted Mu'awiyah and his party; they exaggerated in love of Ali. The Kharijites fell short in love of him until they left the upright way and fought against Ali and insulted his in-laws. Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah restrained their tongues and were certain that all the Companions are the just and best of the ummah. The proofs are in the science of kalam. (al-Qamar) 'Tashbih and Ta'til': The anthropomorphists likened Allah to creation and affirmed corporeality for Him; their extremists insisted on pure incarnation, and the moderate among them said He is a body unlike bodies, of blood and flesh unlike flesh. The negators said that He is negated, as the philosophers said that from Him emanated the First Intellect, then from it a second Intellect, then in order until the tenth Intellect, which is the Active Intellect, and upon it depends the system of the world. Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said that He is transcendent above direction and corporeality, and the forelocks of creatures are in His hand; He does what He wills and judges what He desires. (al-Qamar) 'Which etc.' is an adjective for each of Jabr and Qadr up to Ta'til. (al-Qamar) 'In other than them' i.e., in other than the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'الصراط المستقيم' (the straight path) as the middle way between extremes, both in practice (Shari'ah) and belief (aqidah). It explains that the Shari'ah of Muhammad is moderate between the severity of Judaism (e.g., cutting off impurity, strict penalties) and the laxity of Christianity (e.g., permissibility of wine). The marginal note clarifies that wine and pork were initially lawful even for Muslims, then prohibited specifically for them, remaining lawful for non-Muslims. The definition extends to creed: Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah are moderate between fatalism (Jabriyya) and free will (Qadariyya), between extremism in love of Ali (Rafidah) and extremism against him (Khawarij), and between anthropomorphism (Mushabbiha) and negation (Mu'attila). The commentary provides examples from the Quran and hadith to refute each deviation. This passage is typical of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, which grounds legal and theological definitions in the concept of the balanced middle path.

Key Terms
الصراط المستقيم (al-ṣirāṭ al-mustaqīm): The straight path; defined as the moderate, balanced way in both practice (Shari'ah) and belief (aqidah), avoiding extremes of excess and negligence.
الإفراط (al-ifrāṭ): Excess; going beyond the proper limit. In this passage, it is associated with the severity in the religion of Moses (e.g., strict penalties).
التفريط (al-tafrīṭ): Negligence; falling short of the proper limit. Here associated with the laxity in the religion of Jesus (e.g., permissibility of wine).
الجبر والقدر (al-jabr wa al-qadr): Compulsion and free will; two extreme theological positions regarding human action. Ahl al-Sunnah adopts the middle position of acquisition (kasb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what example is given of the 'excess' (ifrat) in the religion of Moses?
A) Permitting wine
B) Moderate treatment of sinners
C) Cutting off the place of impurity
D) Denying free will

Key Takeaway
The straight path is defined as the moderate path between extremes in both Shari'ah and aqidah, and this definition underlies many Hanafi positions.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of al-Din and Its Refinement
Defines and refines the term 'din' with a critical analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of din, identify its four components (divine institution, rational beings, choice, good in itself), and explain the critique and correction regarding the fitr charity for an infant.

Core Idea
The definition of din must account for cases where choice is absent, such as the fitr charity for an infant.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, defining 'din' precisely is crucial because it sets the scope of religious obligation. The author presents a refined definition that addresses a key flaw: a one-day-old infant cannot exercise choice, yet the fitr charity is incumbent on its guardian. This lesson dissects the definition, its critique, and the corrected formulation.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the base definition of din
Locate the phrase 'al-din: huwa wad' ilahi sa'iq li-dhawi al-'uqul bi-ikhtiyarihim al-mahmud ila al-khayr bi-dhatihi'. List its four components: divine institution, rational beings, praiseworthy choice, good in itself.
The definition appears after the blessings on the family.
2
2. Understand the critique
Find the sentence: 'hadha al-tafsir li al-din makhdush, fa-innahu yakhruju 'anhu sadaqat al-fitr 'an ibn yawm'. Explain why the original definition excludes the fitr charity for a one-day-old child.
The child cannot exercise choice, so the definition would not cover this act, yet it is a religious obligation.
3
3. Analyze the corrected definition
The commentary offers: 'wad' ilahi sa'iq li-man tahqaqa fihi ila al-khayr bi-dhatihi'. Note the replacement of 'li-dhawi al-'uqul...' with 'li-man tahqaqa fihi'. Explain what 'man tahqaqa fihi' means and how it fixes the flaw.
'Man tahqaqa fihi' means 'one who is realized in it' i.e., the person is within the scope of the din even if choice is not exercised directly.
4
4. Distinguish din from madhab
The commentary states: 'bi-dhatihi ihtirazan 'an al-madhab; fa-innahu wad' ilahi sa'iq ... ila al-khayr lakin bi-wasita'. Compare din and madhab: both are divine institutions, but madhab leads to good through a mediator (e.g., the religion of a previous prophet).
This is a subtle usul point: din is directly from Allah to the people, while madhab is a path that depends on a previous revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى آله الذين قاموا بنصرة الدين القويم عطف على قوله على من 1 : والآل أهل بيته أو عترته، أو كل مؤمن تقي وهو الأنسب ههنا؛ لأن المصنف له لم يتعرض لذكر أي أولاده الأصحاب في الصلاة، فكان الأولى هو التعميم. والدين: هو وضع إلهي سائق لذوي العقول باختيارهم المحمود إلى الخير بالذات، وهو يشمل العقائد والأعمال، ويطلق على كل دين والإسلام هو الدين المخصوص لمحمد ولعل في وصفه بالقويم إشارة إليه؛ لأن دين الإسلام هو الموصوف بالاستقامة. أهل بيته أي نساء النبي كذا في "الجلالين" . (القمر) وهو أي المعنى الأخير الأنسب ههنا إلخ، وهذا يؤمي إلى أن المعنى الأول والثاني أيضاً مما يستقيم، وما قال أعظم العلماء من أن المراد بالآل أتباعه لا أهل البيت فقط بقرينة اتصافهم بصفة تعم أهل البيت والصحابة رضوان الله عليهم انتهى فما لا أفهم فإن هذه القرينة كيف تنفي إرادة أهل البيت فقط. (القمر) وضع إلهي أي أمر موضوع من الإله. (القمر) إلى الخير بالذات والمراد بالخير بالذات رضوان الله تعالى أو رؤيته تعالى فإنه خير بالذات أي بلا واسطة، وقال ابن الملك: إن قوله بالذات متعلق بسائق يعني وضع إلهي سائق بذاته؛ لأنه ما وضع إلا لذلك، ثم اعلم أن هذا التفسير للدين مخدوش، فإنه يخرج عنه صدقة الفطر عن ابن يوم؛ إذ لا تتأدى باختياره، فالأصوب أن يفسر الدين بوضع إلهي سائق لمن تحقق فيه إلى الخير بالذات.(القمر) بالذات واحترز به عن المذهب؛ لأنه وضع إلهي سائق لذوي العقول باختيارهم المحمود إلى الخير لكن بواسطة الدين] علية ودين عيسى علة . (القمر) إشارة إليه : فإن القويم هو المستقيم من قومت على کل دین کدین موسی الشيء فهو قويم أي مستقيم كذا في "مشكاة الأنوار في أصول المنار " . (القمر)
And upon his family who supported the upright religion – it is conjuncted to his saying 'upon whom'. And 'al' (family) means his household or his descendants, or every pious believer – and the last is most appropriate here because the author did not mention any of his children or companions in the prayer, so generalization is preferable. And 'al-din' (religion) is a divine institution that drives rational beings by their praiseworthy choice towards good in itself. It includes beliefs and actions. It is applied to every religion, and Islam is the specific religion of Muhammad. Perhaps the description 'upright' (al-qawim) alludes to this, because the religion of Islam is described as upright. 'Ahl baytihi' means the Prophet's wives – as in al-Jalalayn. (al-Qamar) The last meaning (every pious believer) is most appropriate here etc., and this indicates that the first and second meanings are also plausible. What the greatest scholars said – that the intended meaning of 'al' is his followers, not only the household, because they are described with a quality that includes the household and the companions – is hard for me to understand, for how does this evidence negate the intention of only the household? (al-Qamar) 'Divine institution' means a matter put by the Divine. (al-Qamar) 'Towards good in itself' – what is meant by good in itself is the pleasure of Allah or His vision, for it is good in itself, i.e., without intermediary. Ibn al-Malik said: the phrase 'in itself' (bi-dhatihi) is related to 'driver' (sa'iq), meaning a divine institution that drives by itself, because it was only instituted for that. Then know that this interpretation of 'din' is flawed because it excludes the charity of fitr from a one-day-old child, since it is not carried out by his choice. So the more correct interpretation is that 'din' is a divine institution that drives one who is realized in it towards good in itself. (al-Qamar) 'Bi-dhatihi' – it differentiates it from the school (madhab), because it is a divine institution that drives rational beings by their praiseworthy choice towards good, but through a mediator. (al-Qamar) 'Upright' (al-qawim) is the straight – from 'qawwama' something, so it is upright, i.e., straight – as in Mishkat al-Anwar fi Usul al-Manar. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage continues the introduction by defining the term 'din' (religion) and explaining its meaning. The author first sends blessings on the Prophet's family ('al') who supported the upright religion, and discusses the possible meanings of 'al': household (ahl al-bayt), descendants, or every pious believer. The last is deemed most appropriate here because the author did not specify children or companions in the prayer. The central definition: 'Din is a divine institution (wad' ilahi) that drives rational beings (dhawu al-'uqul) by their praiseworthy choice (ikhtiyarihim al-mahmud) towards good in itself (al-khayr bi-dhatihi).' This includes both beliefs (aqa'id) and actions (a'mal). It applies to all religions, but Islam is the specific religion of Muhammad. The description 'qawim' (upright) alludes to Islam's straightness. The commentary (from al-Qamar) then critiques and refines the definition: 'good in itself' is explained as the pleasure of Allah or His vision (ru'ya). Ibn al-Malik's interpretation ties 'bi-dhatihi' to 'driver', meaning the institution drives by its own nature. However, this definition is considered flawed because it excludes the fitr charity on behalf of a one-day-old infant, who cannot exercise choice. Therefore, the more correct definition is: 'a divine institution that drives one who is realized in him (man tahqaqa fihi) towards good in itself' – meaning the person must be capable of being driven. The commentary also clarifies that 'bi-dhatihi' differentiates religion from a madhab (school of thought), which drives towards good but through a mediator (i.e., the religion of a previous prophet mediates for a later one). Finally, 'qawim' means 'straight,' as in the Arabic verb 'qawwama'.

Key Terms
الدين (al-din): A divine institution that drives rational beings by choice towards ultimate good.
وَضْع إلهي (wad' ilahi): A matter placed by Allah; a divine establishment or ordinance.
الخير بالذات (al-khayr bi-dhatihi): Good in itself, i.e., intrinsically valuable, such as divine pleasure or vision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the initial definition of 'din' considered flawed?
A) It does not include beliefs.
B) It excludes obligatory charity for a one-day-old child.
C) It is not based on revelation.
D) It includes too many religions.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of din underwent refinement to ensure it encompasses all obligations, even those where personal choice is absent, as seen in the fitr charity for an infant.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of the Qur'an: Tawatur, Shubha, and the Basmalah
Defining the Qur'an and excluding the basmalah via shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the Qur'an and explain why the basmalah is included but with shubha, affecting its legal consequences.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is defined by tawatur without shubha; the basmalah qualifies but shubha prevents takfir of its denier.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar defines the Qur'an (Kitab Allah) by setting conditions: it must be transmitted via tawatur, be free from shubha (doubt), and be recorded in the mushafs. The most nuanced part is the exclusion of the basmalah from this definition due to shubha, despite the preferred view that it is part of the Qur'an. Understanding this definition helps you grasp why certain transmissions (mashhur, ahad) are not considered Qur'an and why the basmalah has special rulings.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition's components
Identify the three conditions implied in the definition: tawatur, absence of shubha, and inclusion in the mushafs. Note that these are not explicit in a single sentence but emerge from the discussion.
The phrase 'bila shubha' is key.
2
Distinguish between tawatur, mashhur, and ahad
Understand that tawatur yields certainty; mashhur (according to al-Khassaf) is a type of mutawatir with shubha because its origin is ahad; ahad does not meet tawatur conditions.
Mashhur can be used for additions to the Qur'an, but not as Qur'an itself.
3
Analyze the function of 'bila shubha'
The phrase 'without doubt' removes from the definition anything that is not certain. The majority say it's an emphasis, but al-Khassaf says it excludes mashhur. Another view says it excludes the basmalah because it has shubha.
This shows a Hanafi usul principle: certainty prevents shubha.
4
Apply the definition to the basmalah
The basmalah is transmitted via tawatur in the sense that it is in the mushafs, but there is a disagreement about its status as a complete verse, creating shubha. Therefore, according to the explicit wording of the definition, the basmalah is not included as a certain part of the Qur'an, but the correct position (al-asahh) is that it is from the Qur'an.
This shows how a condition (absence of shubha) can exclude something even if it is mostly there.
5
Derive the legal consequences
Because of shubha, a denier of the basmalah as Qur'an is not a kafir; it is not sufficient for obligatory recitation in prayer; a junub may recite it for blessing, not as tilawah.
These are practical applications of the usul definition.

Source Text

فعدةٌ من أيام أخر متتابعات، وعما نُقِلَ بطريق الشهرة كقراءة ابن مسعود في حدّ السرقة فاقطعوا أيمانهما، وفي كفارة اليمين فصيام ثلاثة أيام متتابعات. وقوله: بلا شبهة تأكيد على مذهب الجمهور؛ لأن كل ما يكون متواتراً يكون بلا شبهة،
وعند الخصاف هو احتراز عن المشهور؛ لأنّ المشهور عنده قسم من المتواتر، لكن مع شبهة،

(السنبلي) فتخرج إلخ لأن القراءة الغير المتواترة، سواء نقلت بطريق الآحاد أو بطريق الشهرة، ليست بمكتوبة في مصاحف القراء السبعة (القمر) وقيل قوله بلا شبهة هذا جواب اعتراض أيضًا تقريره أن تعريف الكتاب غير مانع عن دخول الغير؛ لأن التسمية سوى التي في سورة النمل دخلت في الحد، مع أنها ليست بقرآن؛ لأنه لم يتعلق بها جواز الصلاة، ولا حرمة القراءة على الجنب والحائض، فأجاب بما حاصله أن قوله بلا شبهة حصل الاحتراز عن التسمية أي لم يصدق تعريف الكتاب عليها ليلزم كون التعريف غير مانع عن دخول الغير. أي الحائض والنفساء
Chapter on the Book. Definition of the Book of Allah: '...several other days in succession,' and what is transmitted via mashhur like Ibn Mas'ud's reading in the hadd of theft 'so cut off their hands' and in the expiation of the oath 'then fasting three days in succession.' And His word: 'without doubt' is an emphasis according to the majority, because everything that is mutawatir is without doubt. According to al-Khassaf, it is a restriction against the mashhur, because mashhur in his view is a division of mutawatir but with doubt, since its origin is from ahad. All this is on the assumption that the lam in 'al-masahif' is for genus, but if it is for covenant, then all non-mutawatir readings are excluded by 'in the mushafs', and His word 'transmitted from him' etc. becomes a description of the reality. And it is said: His word 'without doubt' is a restriction against the basmalah because there is doubt in it, and therefore its denier is not declared an unbeliever, nor is it sufficient in prayer, and its recitation is not forbidden for the junub, menstruating woman, and postpartum woman. 'No restrictive condition'? The isolated [report] does not combine the conditions of tawatur as said by Ibn Hajar, and among its divisions is a division specifically called mashhur, which acquires the quality of tawatur after the first century, and addition to the Book is permissible by mashhur report, not by ahad report. (al-Qamar) 'so cut off their hands' instead of 'so cut off their hands'. (al-Qamar) 'emphasis etc.' said the greatest scholar, our master Abd al-Salam al-Azami: The text of the Qur'an is transmitted via tawatur, and whoever thinks that the text of the Qur'an may be transmitted via ahad and then established as Qur'an by consensus, making the ahad like mutawatir in certainty, like Shaykh Ilah Dad al-Bukhari in his commentary on al-Bazdawi, has broken the egg of Islam. (al-Qamar) 'And this': i.e., excluding non-mutawatir readings by his word 'transmitted from him etc.' (al-Qamar) 'And all this on the assumption etc.' This is an answer to an implicit question: that in the author's word 'al-masahif' the lam is for covenant, and the thing covenanted is the seven mushafs, which are mutawatir, so it restricts against all besides the mutawatir, so what is the benefit of presenting this speech? He answered: This exposition is on the form of the lam being for genus, not on the assumption of its covenant status, so understand. (al-Sunbuli) 'So it excludes etc.' because the non-mutawatir readings, whether transmitted via ahad or via mashhur, are not written in the mushafs of the seven reciters. (al-Qamar) 'And it is said: without doubt' this is also an answer to an objection: that the definition of the Book is not preventive against the entry of other; because the basmalah other than that in Surah al-Naml enters the definition, while it is not Qur'an, because permissibility of prayer and prohibition of recitation for the junub and menstruating woman are not attached to it. So he answered in summary that his word 'without doubt' achieves the restriction against the basmalah, i.e., the definition of the Book does not apply to it, so that the definition is not non-preventive. (al-Sunbuli) 'Its denier' i.e., denier of the basmalah that it is from the Qur'an. (al-Qamar) Chapter on the Book. Division of the aspects of the structure. And the correct view is that it (the basmalah) is from the Qur'an, but its denier is not declared an unbeliever due to the existence of doubt, and it is not sufficient in prayer because it is not a complete verse according to some, and it is permissible for the junub and his two sisters (menstruating and postpartum woman) to recite it with the intention of blessing, not with the intention of recitation. i.e., the menstruating and postpartum woman.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage defines the Qur'an (Kitab Allah) and explains its conditions. The definition includes that it is transmitted by tawatur, without shubha (doubt), and found in the mushafs. The discussion revolves around the phrase 'bila shubha' which excludes the basmalah because it has some doubt (since it is not mutawatir but mashhur or ahad). The author explains that the basmalah is not considered part of the Qur'an in the sense of being required for prayer or making its recitation forbidden for a junub. However, the correct position (al-asahh) is that it is from the Qur'an, but due to the difference of opinion (shubha), a denier is not declared a kafir, and it is not accepted as sufficient for the obligatory recitation in prayer. The passage also touches on the types of transmission: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad, and the ruling on adding to the Qur'an based on mashhur reports.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawātir): Transmission by such a large number that it is impossible for them to have conspired on a lie; yields certain knowledge.
مشهور (mashhūr): A hadith that becomes widely known after the first century, attaining tawatur after that; it is used for additions to the Qur'an.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt due to conflicting evidence; prevents takfir and other strict rulings.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The basmalah (bismillah al-rahman al-rahim).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, why is a person who denies that the basmalah is from the Qur'an not declared an unbeliever (kafir)?
A) Because the basmalah is not in the Qur'an at all.
B) Because there is shubha (doubt) due to disagreement among scholars.
C) Because the basmalah is only in Surah al-Naml.
D) Because denial of any part of the Qur'an is not disbelief.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is defined by tawatur without shubha; the basmalah is part of it but carries shubha, affecting legal consequences like takfir and sufficiency in prayer.

The Hanafi Definition of the Qur'an: Nazm and Ma'na
Defining the Qur'an as wording that conveys meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of the Qur'an as the nazm (wording) that indicates the ma'na (meaning) and justify why it is not the mere composite of the two.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is the divinely revealed wording conveying meaning; the definition focuses on the nazm.

In this passage, al-Quduri clarifies the precise technical meaning of 'Qur'an'. It is not simply the words and meaning together, but the specific wording that conveys the meaning. This definition serves as a prelude to dividing the Qur'an into its components and is foundational for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components
Recognize that the Qur'an comprises both nazm (wording) and ma'na (meaning), but the correct definition focuses on the wording.
The initial statement 'It is a name for the nazm and ma'na together' requires clarification.
2
Understand the author's clarification
The commentators explain that the intended meaning is that the Qur'an is the nazm that indicates the ma'na, not the composite itself. This is supported by the consensus that the Imam (Abu Hanifa) returned to the Sahibayn's view.
3
Note the tamhid purpose
This definition is presented as a tamhid (prelude) to the subsequent division of the Qur'an into different parts, such as suras and verses.
4
Apply to usul
Understanding that the Qur'an is the nazm affects how we derive rulings: the specific wording is the locus of legal commands, and the meaning is understood from it.

Source Text

وهو اسم للنظم والمعنى جميعًا، تمهيد لتقسيمه بعد بيان تعريفه،
البسملة
الفاتحة، ولا من
والأصح إلخ اعلم أن التسمية آية من القرآن كله أنزلت للفصل بين السور، وليست جزء من كل سورة كما نقل عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان لا يعرف ختم سورة، ولا ابتداء أخرى حتى نزل عليه جبرائيل عليه بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم في أوّل كل سورة رواه أبو داود والحاكم، كذا قال العلي القاري، فالقرآن عبارة عن مائة وأربعة عشر سورة وآية. وهي التسمية، فلابد في ختم القرآن من قراءة التسمية مرة، على صدر أية سورة كانت وهذا كله عندنا على المختار وعند الإمام الشافعي هي جزء من كل سورة سوى سورة البراءة، فهي مائة وثلاثة عشر آية فلو تركت في صدر سورة ما ما حصل الختم، ثم هذا الاختلاف في غير التي في سورة النمل، وأما ما في النمل فهو بعض آية اتفاقا. (القمر) وإنما لم يكفر إلخ هذا أيضًا جواب سؤال تقرير السؤال: أنه لما ثبت كون التسمية على الأصح من القرآن فلم لم يكفر من يجحد كونها منه؟ والحال أن جاحد آية من آيات القرآن وجب تكفيره، فأجاب بما تقريره: ظاهر. (السنبلي) لوجود الشبهة لاختلاف مالك حيث قال بعدم قرآنية البسملة كذا قال الطحطاوي.(القمر) وإنما لم يجز الاكتفاء إلى هذا أيضًا جواب دخل مقدر تقريره أنه لما ثبت كون التسمية من القرآن على الأصح فلم لم يجز الاكتفاء بها في الصلاة؟ فأجاب بما تقريره: ظاهر. (السنبلي) عند البعض على ما قالت أم سلمة : قرأ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الفاتحة، وعد بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله رب العالمين آية، وعند البعض: هي آية تامة على ما روى أبو هريرة أنه عليه قال: "فاتحة الكتاب آيات، أولهن بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم ، كذا قال البيضاوي في تفسيره وقال المصنف له في شرحه وإنما لم يتأد فرض القراءة بها عند أبي حنيفة لله لاختلاف العلماء في كونها آيةً تامةً من القرآن وأدنى درجات الاختلاف المعتبر إيراث الشبهة، وما كان فرضاً لا يتأدى بما فيه شبهة انتهى (القمر) للنظم والمعنى إلخ إجماعًا؛ لما أن الأصح أن الإمام رجع إلى قولهما، والظاهر أن المراد بالنظم الدال على المعنى كما في التوضيح: أي لا مجموع اللفظ والمعنى. (إفاضة الأنوار (۱۲) جميعًا أراد به أنه اسم للنظم الدال على المعنى كما هو مشروح في التلويح، لا أنه اسم للمجموع المركب من النظم والمعنى، فإنه لم ينقل عن معتد به ثم اعلم أن النظم عبارة ههنا عن الألفاظ المخصوصة المرتبة بالترتيب المخصوص (القمر) تمهيد إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن تعريف الكتاب قد مرّ سابقا، وبه وضح حقيقته، فما فائدة هذه العبارة؟ فأجاب بما حاصله أن هذه العبارة لم يأت بها المصنف لتوضيح الكتاب أو القرآن بل تمهيد لتقسيمه. (السنبلي)
It is a name for the wording and meaning together, a prelude to dividing it after clarifying its definition. The basmalah, the Fatiha, and not from... And the correct view etc. Know that the basmalah is a verse from the entire Qur'an revealed for separation between surahs, and it is not part of every surah, as narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (saw) did not know the end of a surah nor the beginning of another until Jibril (as) came down with 'bismillah al-rahman al-rahim' at the beginning of every surah, reported by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim, as said by al-Qari. Thus the Qur'an consists of one hundred and fourteen surahs and one verse, which is the basmalah. So it is necessary in completing the Qur'an to recite the basmalah once at the beginning of any surah it may be. All this according to our school on the chosen view. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is part of every surah except Surah al-Bara'ah, so it is one hundred and thirteen verses; if it is omitted at the beginning of any surah, the completion is not achieved. Then this difference is for other than that in Surah al-Naml; as for what is in al-Naml, it is part of a verse by agreement. (al-Qamar) 'And it is not declared an unbeliever etc.' This is also an answer to a question; the formulation of the question: Since it is established on the correct view that the basmalah is from the Qur'an, why is the one who denies it not declared an unbeliever, given that the denier of any verse of the Qur'an is required to be declared an unbeliever? He answered with what is apparent. (al-Sunbuli) 'Due to the existence of doubt' because of the disagreement of Malik, who said that the basmalah is not part of the Qur'an, as al-Tahawi said. (al-Qamar) 'And it is not sufficient' This is also an answer to an implied difficulty; its formulation: Since it is established on the correct view that the basmalah is from the Qur'an, why is it not sufficient in prayer? He answered with what is apparent. (al-Sunbuli) 'According to some' as Umm Salamah said: The Messenger of Allah (saw) recited the Fatiha and counted 'bismillah al-rahman al-rahim' as 'al-hamdu lillahi rabbi al-alamin' as a verse. And according to some, it is a complete verse as reported by Abu Hurairah that he (saw) said: 'The opening of the Book is seven verses; the first of them is bismillah al-rahman al-rahim', as said by al-Baydawi in his tafsir. And the author (al-Quduri) said in his commentary: It is not that the obligatory recitation is achieved by it according to Abu Hanifah because of the disagreement of the scholars on whether it is a complete verse of the Qur'an, and the lowest degree of considered disagreement causes shubha, and what is obligatory is not achieved by what contains shubha. End. (al-Qamar) 'For the wording and meaning etc.' by consensus; because the correct view is that the Imam (Abu Hanifah) returned to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view, and the apparent meaning is that intended by 'al-nazm' is that which indicates the meaning, as in al-Tawdih: i.e., not the combination of the wording and meaning. (Ifadat al-Anwar (12)) 'Together' he intended by it that it is a name for the wording that indicates the meaning, as elaborated in al-Talwih, not that it is a name for the composite of wording and meaning, for it has not been transmitted from anyone reliable. Then know that 'al-nazm' here refers to the specific words arranged in a specific order. (al-Qamar) 'Prelude etc.': Repelling an implied difficulty; its formulation: The definition of the Book has already passed, and thereby its reality is clarified, so what is the benefit of this statement? He answered in summary that the author did not bring this statement to clarify the Book or the Qur'an, but as a prelude to its division. (al-Sunbili)
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion about the nature of the Qur'an. It states that the Qur'an is both the nazm (wording) and the ma'na (meaning), but the correct understanding is that it is the nazm that indicates the ma'na, not the mere combination. This serves as a prelude (tamhid) for dividing the Qur'an into different aspects. The commentary also revisits the basmalah issue, explaining that it is a verse from the Qur'an but not counted as a separate verse in every surah according to the Hanafis, unlike the Shafi'is who consider it a verse of each surah except al-Bara'ah. The reason why its denier is not a kafir is the shubha caused by the disagreement of scholars like Imam Malik. Likewise, it is not sufficient for the obligatory recitation in prayer because of this shubha. The passage ends with a note that the definition of 'kitab' was already given, and this new definition is only to introduce the division.

Key Terms
النظم (al-naẓm): The specific words arranged in a particular order.
المعنى (al-ma‘nā): The meaning indicated by the wording.
تمهيد (tamhīd): A prelude or introduction to a subsequent division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi definition, what does the term 'Qur'an' refer to?
A) The meaning alone
B) The wording and meaning together as a composite
C) The wording that indicates the meaning
D) The divine attribute of speech

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is defined as the specific revealed wording that conveys the meaning; this precise definition underpins Hanafi usul.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Basmalah: Rulings and Scholarly Disagreement
Continuing basmalah discussion with fiqh implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the basmalah and explain why the denier is not considered a kafir and why the basmalah is not sufficient for the obligatory recitation in prayer.

Core Idea
The basmalah is a verse of the Qur'an for separation, but scholarly disagreement (ikhtilaf) creates shubha, preventing takfir and making it insufficient for prayer.

This passage continues with the basmalah, a topic of ikhtilaf between the Hanafis and Shafi'is. The Hanafis hold that the basmalah is a verse of the Qur'an but not part of each surah. The difference of opinion with Imam Malik and others creates shubha, which has practical consequences: a denier is not declared a disbeliever, and the basmalah cannot fulfill the obligation of recitation in prayer. This case illustrates how ikhtilaf affects fiqh rulings through the principle of shubha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The basmalah is a verse from the entire Qur'an, revealed for separation between surahs, not part of each surah. The Qur'an consists of 114 surahs and one verse (the basmalah).
2
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the basmalah a verse of every surah except al-Bara'ah, making it 113 basmalah verses.
3
Understand the takfir response
Despite the basmalah being part of the Qur'an on the preferred view, a denier is not declared a disbeliever because of the shubha arising from Imam Malik's position that it is not Qur'an at all.
The lowest degree of difference creates shubha.
4
Understand the prayer response
The basmalah is not sufficient for the obligatory recitation (fard) in prayer because of the same shubha; obligatory acts require certainty.
The hadiths about the Prophet counting it as a verse create further shubha but do not resolve it.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو اسم للنظم والمعنى جميعًا، تمهيد لتقسيمه بعد بيان تعريفه،
البسملة
الفاتحة، ولا من
والأصح إلخ اعلم أن التسمية آية من القرآن كله أنزلت للفصل بين السور، وليست جزء من كل سورة كما نقل عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان لا يعرف ختم سورة، ولا ابتداء أخرى حتى نزل عليه جبرائيل عليه بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم في أوّل كل سورة رواه أبو داود والحاكم، كذا قال العلي القاري، فالقرآن عبارة عن مائة وأربعة عشر سورة وآية. وهي التسمية، فلابد في ختم القرآن من قراءة التسمية مرة، على صدر أية سورة كانت وهذا كله عندنا على المختار وعند الإمام الشافعي هي جزء من كل سورة سوى سورة البراءة، فهي مائة وثلاثة عشر آية فلو تركت في صدر سورة ما ما حصل الختم، ثم هذا الاختلاف في غير التي في سورة النمل، وأما ما في النمل فهو بعض آية اتفاقا. Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Hanafi Definition of Al-Amr (Command)
Defines amr and defends against objections from Talwih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of al-amr, identify its conditions (isti'la', intent of wujub), and defend it against the key objections regarding inclusion of iltimas, du'a, and tahdid.

Core Idea
Al-amr is a speaker's utterance to another with assumed superiority, intending obligation, and is exclusive to wujub.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar defines al-amr (command) in the Hanafi usul tradition, defending the definition against objections from al-Talwih. The definition is crucial because it determines the legal force of imperative forms in the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding the precise conditions – especially isti'la' (assuming superiority) and the intent of obligation – is essential for correctly deriving rulings from commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's components
The definition is: 'the utterance of one person to another on a level of superiority to do an action.' Break it down: qawl (utterance), isti'la' (superiority), bi-fi'l (to do). Note that 'qawl' here means the thing said (maqul), not the act of speaking.
This is the classical definition accepted by the majority.
2
Understand the condition of isti'la'
Isti'la' means the speaker considers themselves superior, whether actually superior or not. This excludes iltimas (equal level) and du'a (submission). The Hanafi view is that actual 'uluww is not required, unlike the Mu'tazila.
If a lower person commands a higher, it is considered bad manners but still a command linguistically.
3
See how the definition excludes nahy (prohibition)
Nahy has the same structure (utterance on isti'la') but is removed by including 'if'al' (do). The imperative form 'if'al' is a necessary condition.
The word 'if'al' represents all derived imperative forms.
4
Address the objection about tahdid and ta'jiz
Tahdid (threat) and ta'jiz (incapacitation) are on isti'la' but lack the intent of imposing obligation (ilzam al-fi'l). The usul definition requires that the speaker intends to oblige the action, which only applies to wujub.
Examples: 'Do whatever you wish' (tahdid) is not a real command despite the form.
5
Understand the exclusivity of amr for wujub
The Hanafi position is that al-amr in usul is exclusively for obligation (wujub), not for recommendation (nadb) or permission (ibaha). This is expressed by 'bighiyatin lazimatin' (a necessary form) – the imperative form is inseparable from the meaning of obligation.
This refutes both ishtirak (commonality with nadb/ibaha) and taraduf (synonymy with action).

Source Text

تعريف الأمر

والقول مصدر يراد به المقول؛ لأن الأمر من أقسام الألفاظ، وهو جنس يشمل كل
لفظ، وقوله : على سبيل الاستعلاء يخرج به الالتماس والدعاء، وبقي فيه النهي داخلاً، فخرج بقوله: افعل والمراد بقوله: افعل كل ما كان مشتقا من المضارع على هذه
الطريقة، سواء كان حاضرًا أو غائبا أو متكلما معروفًا أو مجهولاً، ولكن بشرط أن يكون المقصود منه إيجاب الفعل، ويعد القائل نفسه عاليًا سواء كان عاليًا في الواقع أو لا؛ ولهذا نُسب إلى سوء الأدب إن لم يكن عاليًا.
وبما ذكرنا اندفع ما قيل: إن أريد به اصطلاح العربية، فلا حاجة إلى قوله: من الاشتراط
به مسماه
و مسمى
والقول إلخ: دفع دخل تقريره: أن مسمى الأمر لفظ فكيف يحمل عليه القول.(القمر) والقول إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقرير الدخل: أن القول خبر للضمير الغائب أي هو وهو راجع إلى الأمر والمراد الأمر ذات ،محضة فيلزم حمل الوصف المحض على الذات وهو غير جائز، فأجاب بأن القول وإن كان مصدرًا لكنه بمعنى المقول، فيلزم حمل الذات مع الوصف على الذات وهو جائز، أو تقرير الدخل بأن يقال: الأمر من أقسام اللفظ فهو لفظ، وحمل القول على اللفظ غير صحيح؛ لأن اللفظ يكون مقولاً لا قولاً، فأجاب بما ترى، وقوله : وهو جنس يشمل كل لفظ يفيد أن الفعل والإشارة خارجان عن الأمر. (السنبلي)
يخرج به إلخ فإن طلب الفعل مع التساوي التماس، ومع الخضوع دعاء، ومع الاستعلاء أمر. (القمر) : وبقي إلخ فإن النهي أيضًا قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء. (القمر) والمراد إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن التعريف غير جامع؛ لعدم شموله الأمر الغائب والمتكلم معروفًا كان أو مجهولاً؛ اذ ليس فيها افعل.(القمر) من المضارع إلخ احتراز به عن نحو نزال بمعنى انزل، وعن كل فعل لا يكون مشتقا من المضارع بهذه الطريقة وإن كان مستعملاً في الطلب نحو أو جبت عليك إن تفعل كذا، أو يجب عليك إن تفعل كذا، والعجب من البعض له أنه قال :أولاً: إن في هذين القولين طلبًا ثم قال: إن في الأول إخبارًا عن الإيجاب، وفي الثاني إخبارًا عن الوجوب تدبر . (القمر) على هذه الطريقة أي على الطريقة المعروفة لاتخاذ الأمر. (القمر) المقصود منه أي مقصود القائل من الأمر. (القمر) ويعد إلخ هذا على رأي الجمهور، فإنه لو قال الأدنى للأعلى: افعل يذم؛ لسوء الأدب، فلو كان المعتبر هو العلو في نفس الأمر لم يكن هذا أمر إلا أنه يذم، ولو لم يكن الاستعلاء معتبرًا لا يذم فعلم أن الاستعلاء شرط، وعند بعض المعتزلة : يشترط العلو في الأمر، وقيل: لا يشترط العلو ولا الاستعلاء، والتفصيل في المطولات. (القمر) ما قيل: القائل صاحب "التلويح". (القمر)

مبحث الخاص
٦٨
تعريف الأمر

على سبيل الاستعلاء؛ لأن الالتماس والدعاء أيضًا أمر عندهم، وإن أريد به اصطلاح الأصول، فيصدق على ما أريد به التهديد والتعجيز؛ لأنه أيضًا على سبيل الاستعلاء؛ وذلك لأنا نتكلم على اصطلاح الأصول وليس المقصود مجرد الاستعلاء،
أي الاندفاع
بل إلزام الفعل وذا لا يصدق إلا على الوجوب، بخلاف التهديد والتعجيز ونحوهما. ويختص مراده بصيغة لازمة بيان لكون الأمر خاصا يعني يختص مراد الأمر وهو الوجوب بصيغة لازمة للمراد، والغرض منه بيان الاختصاص من الجانبين أي لا يكون الأمر إلا للوجوب، ولا يثبت الوجوب إلا من الأمر دون الفعل، فيكون نفيا للاشتراك
قول المصنف
والترادف جميعًا، وذلك بأن يقال : دخول الباء ههنا على المختص على طريقة قولهم:
ما
لأن الالتماس: وهو قول لفظ الأمر مع التساوي والدعاء، وهو قول صيغة الأمر مع الخضوع أيضا أمر عندهم أي عند أهل العربية، فلا يكون التعريف جامعا حينئذ. (القمر) فيصدق إلخ مع أن ما أريد به التهديد نحو: اعملوا شئتم، والتعجيز نحو: فَأْتُوا بِسُورَةٍ مِّنْ مِثْلِهِ ﴾ (البقرة:۲۳) ليسا من الأمر حقيقة، فلا يكون التعريف مانعا. (القمر) وذا أي الإلزام لا يصدق إلا على الوجوب، فصار التعريف مانعا . (القمر) ونحوهما كالإباحة نحو: وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَاصْطَادُوا (المائدة: ۲) (القمر) بصيغة لازمة إلخ أي صيغة لازمة لذلك المراد، ولولا تلك الصيغة لما عرف المراد، والمراد باللازم اللازم الخاص ؛ لأن اللازم قد يكون خاصا، وقد يكون عامًا لكن المراد ههنا هو الخاص. (السنبلي)
به
من الجانبين: قال شارح مختصر" الحسامي واعلم أن اللفظ قد يكون مختصا بالمعنى، ولا يكون المعنى مختصاً كالألفاظ المترادفة مثل: ليث وأسد، وقد يكون العكس كالأعلام المنقولة، وبعض الألفاظ المشتركة، وقد يكون الاختصاص من الجانبين كالألفاظ المتباينة. (القمر) إلا للوجوب: أي لا للندب ولا للإباحة، فليس الأمر مشتر
بين الوجوب والندب والإباحة. (القمر) دون الفعل أي فعل النبي عليه فليس الأمر والفعل مترادفين.(القمر) وذلك: أي كون قول المصنف نفيًا للاشتراك بين الوجوب والندب والإباحة والترادف أي بين الأمر والفعل جميعًا. (القمر) وذلك بأن يقال إلخ هذا دفع دخل مقدره تقريره أن مدخول الباء في قول الماتن بصيغة لا يخلو إما أن يكون مختصاً أو مختصا به الأول خلاف الأصل، وعلى الثاني لا يحصل مقصوده وهو الاختصاص من الجانبين؛ لأن الظاهر أن المراد باللازم لازم أعم وهو ما يوجد بدون الملزوم، فعلى هذا يلزم وجود الصيغة بدون الوجوب، فيثبت الاشتراك والمصنف بصدد نفيه ولو سلم أن المراد باللازم اللازم المساوي، فيحصل الاختصاص من الجانبين بقوله : صيغة لازمة فيلغو قوله ويختص فأجاب بما حاصله ظاهر بالتأمل القليل. (السنبلي)
Section on the Specific (al-Khass). 67. Definition of al-Amr (Command). And 'al-qawl' (utterance) is a verbal noun intended to mean the thing said (al-maqul) because al-amr is a category of words (alfaz). It is a genus that encompasses every word. And his statement: 'on the level of superiority (isti'la')' excludes iltimas (request) and du'a (supplication), and prohibition (nahy) remains included within it. Then by his statement: 'do (if'al)' it is removed. And by his statement 'if'al' is intended every word derived from the mudari' (imperfect) in this manner, whether it is addressed to a present person, absent person, or one speaking, known or unknown, but with the condition that the intent from it is the obligation (wujub) of the action, and the speaker considers himself superior (aaliyan) whether he is actually superior in reality or not; for this reason, it is attributed as bad manners if he is not superior. And by what we have mentioned, it is refuted what was said: If the term is intended by the Arabic terminology, then there is no need for his statement 'from the condition'. And so forth. (al-Qamr) And there is a repulsion of an implicit objection the summary of which: that the meaning of al-amr is a word (lafz), so how can 'al-qawl' be predicated on it? (al-Qamr) And so on. (al-Sunbuli) And the objection about inclusiveness and exclusiveness are addressed. (al-Qamr) And it is clarified that iltimas and du'a are also called 'amr' by the Arabic scholars, so the definition would not be comprehensive if interpreted according to Arabic terminology. (al-Qamr) Therefore, if interpreted according to usul terminology, it would apply to what is intended by threat (tahdid) and incapacitation (ta'jiz) because they are also on the level of superiority. But we are speaking according to usul terminology, and the purpose is not mere superiority, but the imposition of the action, and that only applies to obligation (wujub), unlike threat and incapacitation and the like. And his (the author's) intent is specified by a necessary (lazima) form, showing that al-amr is specific. That is, the intended meaning of al-amr (obligation) is specified by a form that is necessary for that meaning, and the purpose of that is to show specification from both sides: that al-amr is only for obligation, and obligation is only proven by al-amr, not by action (fi'l). So it negates both commonality (ishtirak) and synonymy (taraduf). (al-Qamr) And he (the commentator) explains the objection and resolution. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition of the term 'amr' (command), expanding upon the classical definition and defending it against various objections. The author begins by stating that 'amr' is a category of speech (qawl), meaning the thing said, not the act of speaking. It is a genus that includes every word. The definition: 'the utterance of one person to another on a level of superiority (isti'la') to do an action (bi-fi'l)'. The condition of isti'la' excludes iltimas (request made on equal footing) and du'a (supplication made with humility). Nahy (prohibition) is initially included because it also has the form of command not to do; then it is excluded by specifying 'if'al' (do). The word 'if'al' includes all derived forms from the imperfect, whether addressing present, absent, or oneself, known or unknown, but the key condition is that the speaker intends the action to be obligatory (wajib) and considers himself superior (even if not in reality). This last point distinguishes the Hanafi view from the Mu'tazila, who require actual superiority. The passage then addresses objections raised by the author of Al-Talwih (Taftazani). One objection is that if we take the Arabic linguistic definition, the condition of isti'la' is unnecessary because Arabic includes iltimas and du'a as types of 'amr'. The response is that we are speaking according to usul terminology, not Arabic. Another objection is that the definition would include threat (tahdid) and incapacitation (ta'jiz) because they are also on a level of superiority. The response is that the usul definition requires the intent to impose the action (ilzam al-fi'l), which only applies to obligation, not threat. Further, the passage specifies that the form is 'lazima' (necessary) for the meaning of obligation, meaning that the imperative form is exclusively used for obligation, not for recommendation (nadb) or permission (ibaha). This also rejects synonymy between 'amr' and 'fi'l' (the Prophet's action), because obligation is only established by command, not by action. The final part resolves a potential objection regarding the parsing of 'bighiyatin lazimatin' to ensure the specification is mutual. The Hanafi position is that 'amr' is for wujub only (not nadb or ibaha), and this is the relied-upon view. The reference to Mu'tazila shows an ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi view (following the majority) is that isti'la' (pretension to superiority) is sufficient, not actual superiority.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء بفعل (the speaker's utterance to another on a level of superiority to do an action) with the intent of obligation.
الاستعلاء (al-isti'la'): The speaker's assumption of superiority over the addressee, whether real or pretended.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation (fard) that is demanded by the command; the ruling indicated by amr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of al-amr (command), what is the key condition in the speaker's attitude towards the addressee?
A) The speaker must be actually superior to the addressee.
B) The speaker must consider themselves superior, whether actual or not.
C) The addressee must consent to the command.
D) The command must be expressed in the imperative form only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, al-amr is defined by the conditions of assumed superiority, intent of obligation, and the imperative form, making it exclusive to wujub.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Command Implies Obligation
Expands and defends the principle that command implies obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that command (amr) implies obligation (wujub) and identify the opposing views, applying the principle to a sample Quranic command.

Core Idea
Command in its real sense obligates; any other meaning requires a contextual indicator.

This passage clarifies a foundational usul principle: when the Quran or Sunnah uses a command, does it automatically create an obligation? The Hanafi school holds yes — the default is wujub. Other schools disagree. We'll explore the dispute and the Hanafi proof, and see how this principle affects fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle under discussion
The passage addresses the implication (mujib) of the command (amr). Is it obligation (wujub), recommendation (nadb), permission (ibaha), or something else?
This is a core usul question that affects all subsequent fiqh rulings.
2
State the Hanafi position and its key proof
The Hanafi position: amr implies wujub in its real sense (haqiqa). The proof: the command is a request for action; its absolute form directs to the complete request, which is obligation. Also, the default in language is haqiqa, and the haqiqa of command is obligation.
The proof is linguistic and rational, not necessarily from a single text.
3
Summarize the opposing views and their evidence
Some say it implies nadb (citing Quran 24:33 about kitaba); some say ibaha; some say tawaqquf (suspension); some say ishtirak (homonymy). The text mentions these briefly.
Be careful: the verse 24:33 is not an absolute command but qualified by context (if you know good).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opponents
The Hanafi response: the verse about kitaba is not a pure command; it has a contextual indicator (qarina) that shifts it from obligation to recommendation. The command in its absolute form remains for wujub.
This shows that the Hanafi view accepts exceptions when there is a proven qarina.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
When a command appears in the Quran or Sunnah without any qarina, the Hanafi school treats it as obligatory, while other schools may treat it as recommended or suspend judgment. This affects the classification of many acts.
For example, the command to pray (aqimu al-salah) is seen as obligatory by Hanafis; commands with qarina, like kitaba, are seen as recommended.

بيان موجب الأمر
إن الفعل قسم من الأمر؛ لأن الأمر نوعان: قول وفعل؛ لأنه أطلق الله تعالى لفظ الأمر على الفعل في قوله: ﴿وَمَا أَمْرُ فِرْعَوْنَ بِرَشِيدٍ ﴾ أي فعله؛ لأن القول لا يوصف بالرشيد، وإنما يوصف بالسديد، فأجاب المصنف عنه بقوله : وسمي الفعل به؛ لأنه سببه أي سمي الفعل بلفظ الأمر؛ لأن الأمر سبب للفعل، فيكون من باب المجاز، وإنما الكلام في الحقيقة.
ولما فرغ عن نفي الترادف قصداً شرع في نفي الاشتراك قصدًا، فقال: وموجبه الوجوب لا الندب والإباحةُ والتوقفُ يعني أن موجب الأمر الوجوب فقط عند العامة لا الندب كما ذهب إليه بعض ولا الإباحةُ كما ذهب إليه بعض، ولا التوقفُ كما ذهب إليه بعض، ولا الاشتراك لفظًا أو معنى بين الثلاثة أو الاثنين كما ذهب إليه آخرون، و لم يذكره المصنف؛ لأنه يفهم مما ذكره التزاما، فأهل الندب يقولون : الأمر للطلب فلابد أن يكون جانب الفعل فيه راجحًا حتى يطلب، وأدناه الندب، وهذا كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَكَاتِبُوهُمْ إِنْ عَلِمْتُمْ فِيهِمْ خَيْراً﴾ (النور: ۳۳) وأهل الإباحة يقولون: إن معنى الطلب أن يكون مأذونا فيه، ولا يكون حراما، وأدناه هو الإباحة، كما ذهب إليه بعض هو أبو هاشم، وأكثر المعتزلة، ويروى عن الشافعي في قول. ولا الإباحة كما نقل عن بعض أصحاب مالك. ذهب إليه بعض هو أبو العباس أحمد بن شريح من أصحاب الشافعي، ثم اعلم أن التوقف عنده في تعين المراد عند الاستعمال كما يشعر عليه قول الشارح فيما سيأتي، فيجب التوقف لا في تعيين الموضوع له، فإن الأمر عنده موضوع بالاشتراك اللفظي للوجوب والندب والإباحة والتهديد. ولا الاشتراك لفظا إلخ اعلم :أولاً: أن الاشتراك اللفظي عبارة عن كون اللفظ موضوعا لكل واحد من المعاني ابتداء، والاشتراك المعنوي عبارة عن كون اللفظ موضوعًا لمعنى واحد كلي له أفراد وثانيا: أنه روي عن الشافعي أنه مشترك لفظًا بين الوجوب والندب، ونقل عن الشيخ أبي منصور الماتريدي أنه موضوع للاقتضاء حتمًا كان أو ندبًا، فصار مشتركًا معنويًا بينهما، وقيل: هو مشترك لفظًا بين الوجوب والندب والإباحة، وقيل: مشترك معنى بين هذه الثلاثة بأن يكون موضوعًا للإذن الشامل لهذه الثلاثة وهو مذهب المرتضى من الشيعة لأنه يفهم إلخ فإنه لما نفى كون الندب والإباحة موجب الأمر فهم أنه ليس مشتركا بين الاثنين أو الثلاثة، ولما قال: إن موجب الأمر الوحوب، فهم أنه ليس مشتركًا معنًا بين الثلاثة أو الاثنين، فإنه على الأول موجبه الإذن، وعلى الثاني موجبه الاقتضاء على ما مرّ آنفا تدبر وأدناه الندب فإن في الإباحة الطرفان متساويان، وأما المنع عن الترك كما هو في الوجوب فأمر زائد على الرجحان. وأدناه الندب إلخ قلنا الأمر طلب، فمطلقه ينصرف إلى الكامل و ذا بالوجوب. فكاتبوهم إلخ : قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَبْتَغُونَ الْكِتَابَ مِمَّا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ فَكَاتِبُوهُمْ إِنْ عَلِمْتُمْ فِيهِمْ خَيْرا﴾ (النور: ٣٣) أي إصلاحًا واستطاعة لأداء مال، المكاتبة وهي أن يقول السيد لعبده كاتبتك على كذا من المال، فإن وإن بقي عليه شيء فهو عبد، له فأمر الكتابة ههنا للندب.
Topic of the Specific. Clarification of the Implication of Command. Indeed, the action is a part of command; because command is of two types: speech and action; because Allah Almighty applied the word 'command' to action in His saying: 'And the command of Pharaoh was not right' i.e., his action; because speech is not described as 'right' but is described as 'correct'. So the author answered about it by saying: 'And the action is called by it because it is its cause', i.e., the action is called by the word 'command' because command is a cause for action, so it is from the category of metaphor, but the discussion is about the real meaning. And when he finished from negating synonymy intentionally, he started negating homonymy intentionally, and said: 'And its implication is obligation, not recommendation, permission, or suspension', meaning that the implication of command is only obligation according to the common people, not recommendation as some held, nor permission as some held, nor suspension as some held, nor homonymy in wording or meaning between the three or the two as others held. And the author did not mention it because it is understood from what he mentioned implicitly. The proponents of recommendation say: command is for request, so the side of action must be preponderant so that it is requested, and its minimum is recommendation. This is like His saying: 'So contract with them if you know in them good'. And the proponents of permission say: the meaning of request is that it is permitted, not forbidden, and its minimum is permission, as some held, namely Abu Hashim and most Mu'tazila, and it is narrated from al-Shafi'i in one opinion. And permission as narrated from some of Malik's companions. Some held it, namely Abu al-Abbas Ahmad ibn Shuraih from al-Shafi'i's companions. Then know that suspension according to him is regarding determining the intended meaning at the time of usage, as the commentator's statement later indicates, so suspension is necessary, not regarding determining the posited meaning, for the command according to him is posited by verbal homonymy for obligation, recommendation, permission, and threat. And as for verbal homonymy etc. Know: first, that verbal homonymy is that the word is posited for each of the meanings initially, and conceptual homonymy is that the word is posited for a single universal meaning having individuals. Second, it is narrated from al-Shafi'i that it is homonymous verbally between obligation and recommendation, and transmitted from Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi that it is posited for exigency, whether definite or recommendatory, so it becomes homonymous conceptually between them. And it is said: it is homonymous verbally between obligation, recommendation, and permission. And it is said: homonymous conceptually between these three by being posited for permission encompassing these three, which is the doctrine of al-Murtada from the Shi'a. Because it is understood etc., for when he negated recommendation and permission as implications of command, it is understood that it is not homonymous between two or three. And when he said that the implication of command is obligation, it is understood that it is not conceptually homonymous between three or two, for in the first case its implication is permission, and in the second its implication is exigency as has just passed. Consider. And its minimum is recommendation, for in permission the two sides are equal. As for prohibition from abandoning as in obligation, it is something additional to preponderance. And its minimum is recommendation etc. We say: command is request, so its absolute form is directed to the perfect (obligation). 'So contract with them' etc.: Allah Almighty said: 'And those who seek a contract from among those whom your right hands possess, then contract with them if you know in them good' (24:33), i.e., reform and ability to pay wealth. The kitaba is that the master says to his slave: I contract with you for such and such wealth, for if he remains owing something, he is a slave. So the command of kitaba here is for recommendation.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Noor ul-Anwar, explaining the implication of the legal command (amr). The author first establishes that action can be called 'amr' metaphorically, but the real discussion concerns the actual command in speech. The main point is that the command (in its real sense) obligates action; it does not merely recommend, permit, or leave suspended. The Hanafi position is that when Allah or the Prophet issues a command, the default implication is obligation (wujub). The text rejects views that command implies only recommendation (nadb) or permission (ibaha), citing those who argue from the verse about kitaba (24:33) that the command to contract with slaves is recommended, not obligatory. The Hanafi response is that command is a request, and its absolute form points to the complete request, which is obligation. The text also refutes the idea of suspension (tawaqquf) or homonymy (ishtirak), whether verbal or conceptual. The author clarifies that the command is not a homonym for multiple meanings; it is univocally for obligation in its real usage. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul: the command is for obligation unless there is a clear indicator (qarina) to the contrary.

Key Terms
أمر (amr): The legal command; a request for action from a superior to an inferior. In its real sense (haqiqa), it implies obligation.
موجب (mujib): The legal effect or implication of a word; here, the obligatory status that results from a command.
اشتراك لفظي (ishtirak lafzi): Verbal homonymy: a single word has multiple distinct meanings assigned to it from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the default implication of a command (amr) in its real sense?
A) It implies recommendation (nadb).
B) It implies permission (ibaha).
C) It implies obligation (wujub).
D) It is homonymous between obligation and recommendation.

Key Takeaway
The command in its real sense imposes obligation unless a clear contextual indicator shifts it to another meaning.

The Imperative Form Indicates Obligation: Hanafi Usul Evidence
Exposition that the imperative indicates obligation with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) as default, and identify the contextual indicators (qara'in) that divert it to other meanings.

Core Idea
The default meaning of the imperative is obligation; only clear contextual indicators shift it to permission or recommendation.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational principle of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the imperative verb form (amr) primarily signifies obligation (wujub). We will see how the commentator defends this view against opponents who cite the verse about hunting after ihram (5:2), and explore the two Quranic proofs from surah al-Ahzab and al-Nur. By the end, you will understand the rationale behind the Hanafi default and how to handle apparent counterexamples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul rule at stake
The text addresses the indication (dalalah) of the imperative form. The Hanafi rule is: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the imperative indicates obligation).
This is a default rule; it can be overridden by qarina.
2
Examine the counterexample raised by opponents
Opponents cite Quran 5:2: 'When you are free from ihram, hunt.' They argue the imperative here indicates permission, not obligation.
This is a key test for the Hanafi position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator shows that permissibility comes from other indicators: the explicit statement 'Lawful to you are good things' (5:5) and the context of benefit, not from the imperative itself.
The imperative alone does not carry permissibility; the qarina does.
4
Study the Quranic proofs for obligation
Two proofs: (1) Quran 33:36 negates choice for believers after Allah and His Messenger decree, implying obligation. (2) Quran 24:63 threatens punishment for opposing the command, which only applies to wajib.
These establish that the default is obligation, not permission.
5
Evaluate the objection and its response
The objection claims second proof is circular: it assumes the command indicates obligation. The text implicitly relies on the principle that punishment only applies to wajib, which is independently established.
This objection is acknowledged but the Hanafi response stands.
