بيان أنواع الحسن
بل لا بد أن يوجد المأمور به بفعل آخر فهو كامل في كونه حسنًا للغير، أو يتأدى بنفس فعل المأمور به لا يحتاج إلى فعل آخر، فهو قريب من الحسن لعينه أو يكون ذلك المأمور به شرط المأمور به من المأمور حسنًا لحسن في شرطه، وهو القدرة يعني لا يكلف الله تعالى لأحد بأمر إلا بحسب طاقته وقدرته، فهذا أيضًا حسن، وهذا القسم ليس بقسم في الواقع، ولكنه شرط للأقسام الخمسة المقدمة لعينه ولغيره، ولهذا لم يذكره الجمهور بعنوان التقسيم، وإنما ذكره فخر الإسلام ،مسامحة، وسماه ضربًا سادسًا جامعًا لكل من الخمسة المتقدمة، فإذا كان فهي : أي حسن المأمور به الحسن للغير بأن يكون الغير لا يتأدى بفعل المأمور به. (القمر) أو يتأدى إلخ : معطوف على قوله : إما أن لا يتأدى (القمر) فهو إلخ : أي حسن المأمور به الحسن للغير بأن يكون الغير يتأدى بفعل المأمور به قريب من الحسن لعينه؛ لعدم الانفصال بين المأمور به، وذلك الغير. (القمر) فهذا أيضًا حسن لا يخفى عليك أن الحسن بالمعنى الذي مر لا يتحقق في الشرط الذي هو القدرة، فالمراد بالحسن كونه صفة كمال، والقدرة كذلك كذا في الصبح الصادق فتأمل. (القمر) شرط إلخ فما لم يوجد القدرة لم يوجد مأمور. (القمر) الخمسة: الأول: ما لا يكون شبيها بالحسن لمعنى في غيره ولا يقبل السقوط كالتصديق، والثاني: ما لا يكون شبيهًا بالحسن لمعنى في غيره ويقبل السقوط كالصلاة، والثالث : ما يكون مشابها لما حسن لمعنى في غيره، ويكون ملحقا بالحسن لعينه كالزكاة والصوم والحج، وهذه أقسام للحسن لعينه والرابع: الحسن لغيره ولا يتأدى الغير بنفس المأمور به كالوضوء، والخامس: الحسن لغيره ويتأدى الغير بنفس المأمور به كالجهاد وهذان قسمان للحسن لغيره. (القمر) هي ولهذا أي لكونه ليس بقسم في الواقع. (القمر) مسامحة: هذه هي المسامحة الثانية كذا رأيت بخط الشارح. (القمر) فإذا كان إلخ تقريره أنه إذا كان الحسن لحسن الشرط جامعا للأقسام الخمسة فينبغي أن يقول المصنف: بعد ما كان إلخ، ولم يخصص الحسن لمعنى في نفسه، والملحق به بالذكر هذه المسامحة الثالثة كذا رأيت بخط الشارح، وقد أجيب عنه بوجوه: الأول: أنه اختصار منهم في العبارة؛ لأن حسن الحسن لغيره تابع لحسن الغير الذي هو حسن ،لعينه، فلما توقف تحقق حسن الحسن لعينه على الشرط الذي هو القدرة يعلم بالمقايسة توقف حسن الحسن لغيره أيضًا على القدرة للعلم بقبح تكليف العاجز في الحسن لعينه والحسن لغيره والثاني: أن المقصود بيان الحسن يكون بحسن الشرط، فيتوهم منه أنه ينافي القسم الأول فأقحم بعد ما كان حسنًا لمعنى في نفسه، أو ملحقا به لدفع هذا التوهم، ولم يقصد أنه منحصر فيه فذكره وفاقي؛ لأجل هذه الفائدة كذا في الصبح الصادق والثالث ما ذكره الشارح بقوله : ولكن الحسن إلخ. (القمر) جامعًا فينبغي أن يقول: بعد ما كان حسنًا لمعنى في نفسه، أو ملحقا به، أو لغيره حتى يكون المعنى أن المأمور به بعد ما كان حسنًا لمعنى في نفسه كالتصديق والصلاة أو ملحقا به كالزكاة والصوم والحج أو لغيره كالوضوء والجهاد صار حسنًا لمعنى آخر، وهو كونه مشروطا بالقدرة، فلهذا القدرة صارت أوامر الشرع كلها حسنًا للغير، ولكن الحسن لمعنى في نفسه، والملحق به صار جامعًا؛ لكونه لعينه ولغيره، ولهذا قيده بهما، بخلاف ما كان لغيره، فإنه اجتمع فيه الحسن لغيره من جهتين لأجل الغير المعين، ولأجل القدرة فلا يخرج عن كونه لغيره، ولعله لهذا لم يقيده به. ثم بعد هذه المسامحات الثلاثة قد تسامح في أمثلته حيث قال: كالوضوء، والجهاد، والقدرة التي يتمكن بها العبد من أداء ما لزمه، فالوضوء مثال للمأمور به الذي لا يتأدى الغير بأدائه، أي الواسطة فإنه في نفسه تبريد وتنظيف للأعضاء، وإضاعة للماء، وإنما حسن لأجل أداء الصلاة كسائر التبريدات قيده بهما أي قيد المصنف قوله أو يكون حسنًا لحسن في شرطه بالحسن لمعنى في نفسه، والملحق به. (القمر) الغير المعين: أي الغير المخصوص بالمأمور به كالصلاة للوضوء، وإعلاء كلمة الله للجهاد، وقس على هذا. (القمر) ولأجل القدرة: وهو غير مشترك بين الأقسام الخمسة. (القمر) لم يقيده به أي لم يقيد المصنف قوله أو يكون حسنًا لحسن في شرطه بالحسن لغيره. (القمر) هذه المسامحات إلخ الأولى مسامحة الانتشار، والثانية: مسامحة جعله قسما، والثالثة مسامحة ترك قيد لغيره. (القمر) قد تسامح في أمثلته فإن الوضوء والجهاد مثالان للمأمور به الذي صار حسنًا بحسن الغير، والقدرة مثال للغير الذي صار المأمور به حسنًا ،بحسنه، وليس مثالاً للمأمور به والقول بأن المضاف محذوف والمعنى ومشروط القدرة إلخ لا يخلو عن تكلف. (القمر) لأجل أداء الصلاة إلخ وليس الوضوء قربة مقصودة حيث يسقط بسقوطها، فلا يحتاج في كونه وسيلة للصلاة إلى النية؛ لأن الصلاة إنما تفتقر إلى الوضوء باعتبار كونه طهارة لا باعتبار وصف كونه عبادة، والمفتقر إلى النية هو هذا الوصف أي كونه عبادة وكذا السعي مأمورًا به؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسَعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ (الجمعة: 9) إلخ عبارة عن المشي ونقل الأقدام وليس في ذاته ،حسن، وإنما حسن لإقامة الجمعة المؤدية بفعل آخر بعده. (السنبلي)
Topic: The Specific. Statement of the types of goodness (hasan). Rather, it is necessary that the commanded act exist with another act, so it is complete in being good due to another, or the other is achieved by the very act of the commanded act without needing another act, so it is close to goodness in itself, or that commanded act is a condition of the commanded act from the commander, good due to goodness in its condition, which is capability (qudra), meaning Allah Most High does not charge anyone with a command except according to his capacity and ability. So this too is good. And this division is not actually a division, but it is a condition for the five preceding divisions for [goodness] in itself and for another. Therefore, the majority (jumhur) did not mention it under the heading of division. Rather, Fakhr al-Islam mentioned it by leniency (musamaha) and called it a sixth type encompassing all of the preceding five. So if it is... That is: the goodness of the commanded act that is good due to another is that the other is not achieved by the act of the commanded act. (al-Qamar) Or it is achieved etc.: conjunction to his saying: either it is not achieved (al-Qamar). So it is etc.: i.e., the goodness of the commanded act that is good due to another is that the other is achieved by the act of the commanded act, close to goodness in itself, because there is no separation between the commanded act and that other. (al-Qamar) So this too is good. It should not be hidden from you that goodness in the sense that passed is not realized in the condition which is capability, so what is meant by goodness is that it is an attribute of perfection, and capability is likewise. Thus in al-Subh al-Sadiq, so reflect. (al-Qamar) Condition etc.: so as long as capability is not present, there is no commanded [act]. (al-Qamar) The five: First: what is not similar to goodness due to a meaning in other than itself and does not admit of dropping, like affirmation (tasdiq). Second: what is not similar to goodness due to a meaning in other than itself and admits of dropping, like prayer. Third: what is similar to what is good due to a meaning in other than itself and is annexed to goodness in itself, like zakah, fasting, and hajj. These are divisions of goodness in itself. Fourth: goodness due to another and the other is not achieved by the very act of the commanded act, like wudu. Fifth: goodness due to another and the other is achieved by the very act of the commanded act, like jihad. These two are divisions of goodness due to another. (al-Qamar) It is. Therefore: i.e., because it is not actually a division. (al-Qamar) Musamaha: This is the second lenience, as I saw in the handwriting of the commentator. (al-Qamar) So if it is etc.: Its exposition is that if goodness due to goodness of condition encompasses the five divisions, then the author should say: 'after it was' etc., and he did not specify goodness due to a meaning in itself and what is annexed to it by mention; this is the third lenience, as I saw in the handwriting of the commentator. And it has been answered with several aspects: First: it is conciseness in expression on their part, because the goodness of what is good due to another is dependent on the goodness of the other which is good in itself. So when the realization of goodness in itself depends on the condition which is capability, it is known by analogy that the realization of goodness due to another also depends on capability, due to the knowledge of the ugliness of obligating the incapable in goodness in itself and goodness due to another. Second: the intended [point] is to state that goodness occurs through goodness of condition, and it might be imagined from this that it contradicts the first division, so he inserted it after 'it was good due to a meaning in itself or annexed to it' to repel this misconception, and he did not intend that it is confined to it; so he mentioned it for the sake of this benefit. Thus in al-Subh al-Sadiq. Third: what the commentator mentioned with his statement: 'but goodness' etc. (al-Qamar) Encompassing, so he should say: 'after it was good due to a meaning in itself, or annexed to it, or due to another' so that the meaning is that the commanded act, after it was good due to a meaning in itself like tasdiq and prayer, or annexed to it like zakah, fasting, and hajj, or due to another like wudu and jihad, became good due to another meaning, which is its being conditioned by capability. So because of this, all the commands of the Sharia become good due to another. But goodness due to a meaning in itself and what is annexed to it became encompassing because it is for itself and for another; therefore he restricted it to these two, unlike what is due to another, for in it goodness due to another is combined from two aspects: because of the specific other, and because of capability, so it does not exit from being due to another, and perhaps for this he did not restrict it with it. Then after these three leniencies, he was lenient in his examples where he said: like wudu, jihad, and the capability by which the servant is able to perform what is incumbent upon him. So wudu is an example of the commanded act by the performance of which the other is not achieved, i.e., the intermediary; for in itself it is cooling and cleaning of the limbs and wasting of water, and it is only good for the sake of performing prayer, like other cooling actions. He restricted it to these two, i.e., the author restricted his statement 'or it is good due to goodness in its condition' to goodness due to a meaning in itself and what is annexed to it. (al-Qamar) The specific other: i.e., the specific other particular to the commanded act, like prayer for wudu, and raising the word of Allah for jihad, and analogize to this. (al-Qamar) And because of capability: and it is not shared among the five divisions. (al-Qamar) He did not restrict it with it: i.e., the author did not restrict his statement 'or it is good due to goodness in its condition' with goodness due to another. (al-Qamar) These leniencies etc.: the first is lenience of extension, the second is lenience of making it a division, the third is lenience of omitting the restriction with 'due to another'. (al-Qamar) He was lenient in his examples: for wudu and jihad are examples of the commanded act that became good due to goodness of the other, and capability is an example of the other by whose goodness the commanded act became good, and it is not an example of the commanded act. And the statement that the added [noun] is omitted and the meaning is 'and conditioned by capability' etc. is not free from affectation. (al-Qamar) For the sake of performing prayer etc.: and wudu is not an intended act of worship in itself, since it drops with the dropping of prayer, so it does not require intention for its being a means to prayer; because prayer only needs wudu by virtue of it being purification, not by virtue of its being an act of worship; and what needs intention is this attribute, i.e., its being an act of worship. Similarly, sa'y (striving to the prayer) is commanded by His statement: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (al-Jumu'a 9) etc., which is an expression of walking and moving feet, and in itself it is not good; it is only good for establishing the Friday prayer, which is fulfilled by another act after it. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from Noor al-Anwar is an advanced discussion on the classification of goodness (husn) in commanded acts (al-mamur bih). The text first establishes that commanded acts are good either inherently (hasan li-aynihi) or due to another act (hasan li-ghayrihi). Within goodness due to another, it further subdivides based on whether the other act is achieved by the very performance of the commanded act or not. The author then introduces a third category: goodness due to the goodness of a condition (hasan bi-husn al-shart), namely capability (al-qudra). Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi calls this a sixth division, but the majority (jumhur) do not treat it as a separate division because it is a prerequisite for all commands. The commentary (marked with al-Qamar) clarifies that the intended meaning of 'hasan' here is not the technical legal goodness (which entails reward) but rather being an attribute of perfection; capability is also such an attribute. The text then enumerates the five actual divisions: three for 'hasan li-aynihi' (acts that do not resemble goodness due to another: those that cannot be dropped like belief, those that can be dropped like prayer, and those that are annexed to the former like zakah) and two for 'hasan li-ghayrihi' (acts where the other is not achieved by the act itself like wudu, and acts where the other is achieved like jihad). The discussion on leniencies (musamahat) shows how the author's presentation is concise yet complete, ensuring no misunderstanding arises.

Key Terms
حسن لعينه (hasan li-aynihi): Goodness inherent in the act itself, not due to any external factor.
حسن لغيره (hasan li-ghayrihi): Goodness acquired from another act, either by enabling it (like wudu for prayer) or by achieving it (like jihad for raising Allah's word).
حسن بحسن الشرط (hasan bi-husn al-shart): Goodness derived from the condition of capability (al-qudra) making the command possible and thus good.
القدرة (al-qudra): Capability or ability of the servant to perform the commanded act, without which the command would be burdensome and hence not good.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification presented, which of the following is an example of 'hasan li-ghayrihi' where the other act is achieved by the very performance of the commanded act?
A) Wudu (ablution)
B) Jihad (struggle)
C) Prayer (salat)
D) Belief (tasdiq)

Key Takeaway
Goodness in commanded acts is classified as inherent or derived; capability is a universal condition, not a separate division, ensuring that only feasible commands are good.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Classifying Commanded Acts: Intrinsic vs. Instrumental Beauty
Analyzing commanded acts and their external ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ḥasan li-ʿaynihi and ḥasan li-ghayrihi, correctly classify commanded acts from the Hanafi examples, and apply the framework to similar acts.

Core Idea
An act may be legally good not for itself but for an external benefit it serves.

This passage explores a fundamental classification in Hanafi uṣūl: the beauty (ḥusn) of commanded acts. Some acts are intrinsically good (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi), like faith; others, like wuḍūʾ, become good only because they serve a higher purpose, such as enabling prayer. The author walks through vivid examples—jihād, ḥudūd, ṣalāt al-janāzah—to clarify how the external meaning (maʿnan) determines the ruling. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to analyze why the Sharīʿa commands specific actions and how intention and reward are assigned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of beauty
Locate the author's explicit distinction: ḥasan li-ʿaynihi (intrinsically good) and ḥasan li-ghayrihi (good due to an external goal). Note that the latter's goodness depends on a separate meaning (maʿnan).
The text begins by mentioning 'بيان أنواع الحسن' – exposition of the types of beauty.
2
Analyze the main examples
The author gives four examples: wuḍūʾ (for prayer), jihād (for elevating Allah's word), ḥudūd (for deterrence), and ṣalāt al-janāzah (for fulfilling the Muslim's right). For each, identify the external meaning that justifies the act.
Marginal notes (e.g., from al-Qamar) clarify nuances: jihād and funeral prayer became good due to kufr al-kāfir and islām al-mayyit.
3
Understand the role of choice in intermediaries
Contrast the above with zakāh, ṣawm, and ḥajj: their intermediaries (poverty of the poor, hostility of the soul, honor of the place) are purely created by Allah, not generated by the servant's choice. Hence they are 'annexed' to the intrinsically good.
This distinction determines whether the act is classified as ḥasan li-ʿaynihi or li-ghayrihi.
4
Examine the discussion on 'ability' (qudra)
The text reviews whether qudra is an example of a condition (sharṭ) for which an act is good, not the act itself. Follow the different interpretations to see how pronoun references affect the analysis.
The commentator resolves apparent contradictions by allowing interpretations: qudra as condition or as conditioned.

مبحث الخاص

بيان أنواع الحسن والصلاة مما لا يتأدى بنفس فعل الوضوء، بل لا بد لها من فعل آخر قصدًا توجد به الصلاة، وإذا نوى في هذا الوضوء كان منويًا، وقربة مقصودة يثاب عليها.
والجهاد مثال للمأمور به الذي يتأدى الغير بأدائه، فإنه في نفسه تعذيب عباد الله، وتخريب بلاد الله، وإنما حسن لأجل إعلاء كلمة الله يحصل بمجرد فعل الجهاد لا بفعل آخر بعده. وكذلك إقامة الحدود في نفسها تعذيب، وإنما حسن لزجر الناس من المعاصي، والزجر يحصل بمجرد إقامة الحدود لا بفعل آخر بعده. وكذلك صلاة الجنازة في نفسها بدعة مشابهة لعبادة الأصنام، وإنما حسنت لأجل قضاء حق المسلم، وهو يحصل بمجرد صلاة الجنازة لا بفعل بعدها، فهذه الوسائط قضاء حق المسلم نعم التعذيب فعل آخر أي الركوع والقيام والسجود وغيرها. (المحشي) كان منويًا إلخ إلا أن الصلاة تستغني عن النية في الوضوء حتى يصح الوضوء بغير نية في حق جواز الصلاة فمن هذه الحيثية ليس الوضوء قربة مقصودة، وحسنة لغيره وهو الصلاة أفاد بحر العلوم (أي) مولانا عبد العلي ليه أن في التمثيل بالوضوء شائبة من الخفاء، فإن الوضوء بما هو طهارة حسن وإن كان له حسن آخر من جهة مشروطه أي الصلاة كيف والدوام على الوضوء مندوب شرعًا، وليس لإقامة الصلاة فإن أوقات مندوبية الطهارة وقت الخطبة وسائر الأوقات المكروهة، والأصلح في التمثيل السعي إلى الجمعة، فإنه إنما حسن لأجل صلاة الجمعة فتدبر. (القمر) تعذيب عباد الله إلخ : هذا مسلم لكن لا نسلم قبح هذا التعذيب لم لا يجوز أن يكون حسنًا لذاته الذي هو غير الجهاد لا حسن فيه فتدبر. (القمر) لأجل إعلاء كلمة الله إلخ أي الجهاد ليس حسنًا بنفسه، قال عليه "الآدمي بنيان الرب ملعون من هدم بنيانه، وإنما حسن لأجل إعلاء كلمة الله قال في "التلويح": قال فخر الإسلام إنهما أي الجهاد وصلاة الجنازة إنما صارا حسنين لمعنى كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت، وذلك معنى منفصل عن الجهاد والصلاة. (السنبلي) مشابهة إلخ لحضور الميت الذي هو كالحجر بين يدي المصلين.(القمر) لأجل قضاء حق المسلم إلخ : اعلم أولاً أن صلاة الجنازة تشتمل على أمرين: ثناء الله تعالى وهو حسن لعينه، ودعاء الميت وهو حسن لواسطة قضاء حق المسلم، فتسميته صلاة الجنازة حسنة لغيرها بالنظر إلى جزء معناها كذا قال أعظم العلماء (أي مولانا عبد السلام ، وثانيا : أنه إنما قيد بالإسلام؛ لأن الميت لو لم يكن مسلما كانت الصلاة عليه قبيحة منهية عنها؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تُصَلِّ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ مَاتَ أَبَدا (التوبة: ٨٤) (القمر)

وهي كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت، وهتك حرمة المناهي كلها بفعل العباد واختيارهم، أي قضاء حقه أي الزجر عنه فلهذا اعتبرت الوسائط ههنا وجعلت داخلة في الحسن لغيره، بخلاف وسائط الزكاة والصوم والحج أعني فقر الفقير، وعداوة النفس، وشرف المكان، فإنها بمحض خلق الله تعالى، ولا اختيار فيها للعبد أصلا، ولهذا جعلت من الملحق بالحسن لعينه، فتأمل. والقدرة مثال للشرط الذي حسن المأمور به لأجله لا للمأمور به، وإن قدرت المضاف وقلت ومشروط القدرة كان مثالاً للمأمور به المشروط بها، وإن جعلت ضمير أو يكون حسنًا راجعا إلى الغير كما كان ضمير لا يتأدى أو يتأدى راجعا إليه كما قيل لم ينتشر الكلام وتكون القدرة مثالاً للغير بلا تكلف لكن يكون الشرط حينئذ بمعنى المشروط،القدرة
ويكون المعنى أو يكون الغير كالقدرة حسنة لحسن في مشروطها،
وهي كفر الكافر إلخ فيه بحث، فإن كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت وهتك حرمة المناهي ليست مما يتأدى بنفس المأمور به أعني الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة وإقامة الحدود والجواب: أن المراد بحذف المضاف أي إعدام كفر الكافر، وقضاء حق إسلام الميت والزجر عن هتك حرمة المناهي. (القمر) وجعلت أي الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة، وإقامة الحدود.(القمر) أعني فقر الفقير إلخ: هذا إقرار بالحق، ومخالف لظاهر ما سبق من الشارح من أن الواسطة في الزكاة دفع حاجة الفقير، وفي الصوم قهر النفس. (القمر) جعلت أي الزكاة والصوم والحج. (القمر)
ولهذا جعلت إلخ لعل هذا إيفاء لما وعد الشارح قبل الورقة بقوله: كما ستقف عليه فيما بعد. (السنبلي) فتأمل لعله إيماء إلى المباحث التي بيناها (القمر) والقدرة إلخ : دفع دخل تقريره أن هذا المثال ليس بمطابق للمثل له؛ فإنه كان المأمور به الذي حسن الحسن في شرطه إلخ، والقدرة ليس مأمور به بل هو شرطه، ولو جعل الممثل له الغير الذي حسن بواسطته المأمور به لا يكون عبارته السابقة مستقيمة؛ لأن المعنى حينئذ أو يكون الغير حسنًا لحسن في الغير، فإن الشرط هو الغير وهو ليس بصحيح، فأجاب بأن كلاً من ذلك بالتأويل صحيح.(السنبلي) لا للمأمور به: أي ليس مثالاً للمأمور به (القمر) مثالاً للغير إلخ وحينئذ وإن كان المثال مطابقا للممثل له لكن يلزم خلاف المقصود، فإن المقصود تمثيل المأمور به الحسن لغيره كالوضوء، والجهاد، والقدرة ليست مأمورًا بها، ولا تصغ إلى قول من قال (أي) المولوي أبو الفضل جونفوري : إنه يلزم على تقدير إرجاع ضمير أو يكون إلى الغير عدم مطابقة المثال للممثل له فتدبر . (القمر)
لكن يكون إلخ ويكون ضمير "كان" في قوله: بعد ما كان إلخ راجعا إلى الشرط بمعنى المشروط.(القمر)
Section on the Specific. 132. Exposition of the types of beauty and prayer from what is not accomplished by the act of ablution itself, rather it necessarily requires another act intentionally by which prayer is achieved, and if one intends in this ablution, it becomes intended and a sought-after act of worship for which one is rewarded. Jihad is an example of a commanded act by which the other is achieved through its performance, for it is in itself torture of Allah's servants and destruction of Allah's lands, and it is only beautiful for the sake of elevating Allah's word, which is achieved by the mere act of jihad and not by another act after it. Similarly, establishing the prescribed punishments is in itself torture, and it is only beautiful for deterring people from sins, and deterrence is achieved by the mere establishing of the prescribed punishments and not by another act after it. Likewise, the funeral prayer is in itself an innovation resembling idol worship, and it is only beautiful for the sake of fulfilling the right of the Muslim, which is achieved by the mere funeral prayer and not by an act after it. So these intermediaries are: fulfilling the right of the Muslim, yes, torture, another act meaning bowing, standing, prostration, etc. (al-Muhashi) 'it becomes intended' etc. except that prayer dispenses with intention in ablution such that ablution is valid without intention regarding the permissibility of prayer, so from this perspective ablution is not an intended act of worship and is beautiful for another, namely prayer. Bahr al-Ulum (i.e. Mawlana Abd al-Ali) stated that there is an element of obscurity in the example of ablution, for ablution as purification is beautiful even if it has another beauty from the aspect of its conditioned thing, i.e. prayer, especially since continuous ablution is recommended by the Law, and not for performing prayer, for the times of recommended purification are the time of the sermon and other disliked times. The better example is going to Friday prayer, for it is only beautiful for the sake of Friday prayer, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'torture of Allah's servants' etc.: This is conceded but we do not concede the ugliness of this torture; why is it not permissible that it be beautiful in itself? That which is other than jihad has no beauty in it, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'for the sake of elevating Allah's word' etc.: i.e. jihad is not beautiful in itself; he said 'the human is the building of the Lord, cursed is he who demolishes his building', and it is only beautiful for the sake of elevating Allah's word. He said in al-Talwih: Fakhr al-Islam said that both, i.e. jihad and funeral prayer, became beautiful for the meaning of the disbelief of the disbeliever and the Islam of the deceased, and that meaning is separate from jihad and prayer. (al-Sanbali) 'resembling' etc. due to the presence of the deceased who is like a stone before the worshippers. (al-Qamar) 'for the sake of fulfilling the right of the Muslim' etc.: Know first that the funeral prayer includes two matters: praise of Allah, which is beautiful in itself, and supplication for the deceased, which is beautiful for the sake of fulfilling the right of the Muslim; so calling the funeral prayer beautiful for another is with consideration of part of its meaning. Thus said the greatest scholars (i.e. Mawlana Abd al-Salam). Secondly, it is restricted to Islam because if the deceased was not a Muslim, praying over him would be ugly and prohibited; due to His saying: 'And never pray over any one of them who has died' (9:84). (al-Qamar) And they are: the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the deceased, and the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions all by the act and choice of servants, i.e. fulfilling his right, i.e. deterrence from it. Therefore the intermediaries were considered here and made included in the beautiful for another, contrary to the intermediaries of zakah, fasting, and Hajj, i.e. the poverty of the poor, the hostility of the soul, and the honor of the place, for they are purely by the creation of Allah and the servant has no choice in them at all; therefore they are made annexed to the beautiful in itself, so reflect. And ability (qudra) is an example of the condition for which the commanded act is beautiful, not of the commanded act. If you consider the genitive construction and say 'the conditioned by ability' it becomes an example of the commanded act conditioned by it. And if you make the pronoun of 'or it is beautiful' refer to the other, just as the pronoun of 'is not accomplished' or 'is accomplished' refers to it, as was said, the speech is not incoherent, and ability becomes an example of the other without effort. But then the condition would be in the sense of the conditioned, and the meaning would be: or the other, like ability, is beautiful due to beauty in its conditioned thing. 'They are the disbelief of the disbeliever' etc.: There is a discussion, for the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the deceased, and the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions are not things that are achieved by the commanded act itself, i.e. jihad, funeral prayer, and establishing the prescribed punishments. The answer: The intended meaning, by deleting the genitive, is the removal of the disbelief of the disbeliever, the fulfilling of the right of the Muslim deceased, and the deterrence from violating the sanctity of prohibitions. (al-Qamar) 'And they were made' i.e. jihad, funeral prayer, and establishing the prescribed punishments. (al-Qamar) 'i.e. the poverty of the poor' etc.: This is an acknowledgment of the truth, and contrary to what appears previously from the commentator that the intermediary in zakah is relieving the need of the poor, and in fasting is subduing the soul. (al-Qamar) 'were made' i.e. zakah, fasting, and Hajj. (al-Qamar) 'Therefore they were made' etc.: Perhaps this fulfills what the commentator promised before the folio by his saying: 'as you will see later.' (al-Sanbali) 'So reflect' perhaps hinting at the investigations we have presented. (al-Qamar) 'And ability' etc.: A rebuttal of an objection that this example does not correspond to the exemplified; for the commanded act that has beauty in its condition was the exemplified, and ability is not a commanded act but its condition. If the exemplified were made the other through which the commanded act is beautiful, his previous expression would not be straight; because the meaning then would be: or the other is beautiful due to beauty in the other, for the condition is the other, and that is not correct. So he answered that both of these are correct through interpretation. (al-Sanbali) 'not of the commanded act': i.e. not an example of the commanded act. (al-Qamar) 'an example of the other' etc. Then although the example corresponds to the exemplified, yet it contradicts the intended purpose, for the intended purpose is to give an example of the commanded act that is beautiful for another, like ablution and jihad, and ability is not a commanded act. And do not listen to the saying of whoever said (i.e. Mawlana Abu al-Fadl Junpuri): 'It implies, on the assumption of referring the pronoun of 'or it is beautiful' to the other, a lack of correspondence of the example to the exemplified,' so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'but it is' etc. and the pronoun of 'was' in his saying 'after what was' etc. refers to the condition in the sense of the conditioned. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This is a detailed textual analysis from a Hanafi usul work, discussing the classification of commanded acts (al-mā'mūr bih) into those that are beautiful in themselves (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi) and those that are beautiful for the sake of something else (ḥasan li-ghayrihi). The author provides examples: ablution (wuḍūʾ) is good because it enables prayer, not for itself; jihad is good for elevating Allah's word; prescribed punishments (ḥudūd) for deterrence; and funeral prayer for fulfilling the right of the Muslim. A key distinction is that the beauty of these acts depends on an external meaning (maʿnan) that is separate from the act itself. For instance, jihad and funeral prayer become good due to the disbelief of the disbeliever and the Islam of the deceased—meanings not inherent in the acts. The commentator (al-Qamar) clarifies that funeral prayer has two aspects: praise of Allah (intrinsically good) and supplication for the deceased (good for another). The text then contrasts these with acts like zakah, fasting, and Hajj, where the intermediaries (poverty, soul's hostility, place's honor) are purely created by Allah and thus these acts are annexed to the intrinsically good. Finally, the text examines the example of ability (qudra) as a condition for which an act is good, not the act itself. There is a refined discussion on whether ability is a condition or the conditioned, and how to understand the pronoun reference to maintain coherence.

Key Terms
الحسن (al-ḥasan): The quality of being good or praiseworthy in the sight of the Law.
الحسن لعينه (al-ḥasan li-ʿaynihi): An act that is good and praiseworthy in itself, regardless of external purpose.
الحسن لغيره (al-ḥasan li-ghayrihi): An act that is not intrinsically good but becomes good due to an external end or benefit.
الوسائط (al-wasāʾiṭ): The intermediaries (external meanings) that make an act ḥasan li-ghayrihi, such as enabling prayer, elevating Allah's word, deterrence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, which of the following is an example of an act that is 'annexed to the intrinsically good' (mulḥaq bi al-ḥasan li-ʿaynihi)?
A) Jihad
B) Wudu
C) Hajj
D) Funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
An act can be legally beautiful not for itself but for an external purpose; discerning this depends on whether the intermediary involves human choice or is purely divine creation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
10 min
Types of Ḥasan: Intrinsic vs. Extrinsic Goodness
Defining two types of ḥasan with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an action as ḥasan li-ʿaynihi or ḥasan li-ghayrihi according to the Hanafi criterion of human choice in the beneficial outcome.

Core Idea
An action is good in itself if its benefit is purely from Allah; good for a result if that result is within human choice.

In Hanafi legal theory, not all good actions are good in the same way. Some are intrinsically praiseworthy, while others derive their moral value from the external outcomes they bring about. This lesson unpacks that distinction using concrete examples from ibādāt and muʿāmalāt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Locate where the text defines al-ḥasan li-ʿaynihi and al-ḥasan li-ghayrihi. Understand that the distinction hinges on whether the beneficial result (the 'mediator') is within the servant's choice or solely Allah's creation.
The passage mentions that for jihad, funeral prayer, and hadd, the mediators (removing kufr, etc.) are by human choice, making the acts ḥasan li-ghayrihi.
2
Examine the contrasting examples
Look at how the text contrasts jihad with zakat, fasting, and hajj. For the latter, the mediators (poverty of the poor, subduing the self, honor of the place) are purely Allah's creation, so these acts are annexed to ḥasan li-ʿaynihi.
The phrase 'فتأمل' (so reflect) indicates a key point: the classification depends on the nature of the mediator.
3
Apply the criterion
Generalize the rule: if the beneficial outcome is achievable through human agency and choice, the act is ḥasan li-ghayrihi; if the outcome is a direct creation of Allah without human intermediary, the act is ḥasan li-ʿaynihi.
This criterion is used when evaluating new actions by analogy.
4
Test with a new action
Consider an act like teaching the Qur'an: its beneficial outcome (guidance) involves human choice, so it would be ḥasan li-ghayrihi. Contrast with a natural disaster causing reflection – that outcome is from Allah, so the reflection is ḥasan li-ʿaynihi.
This shows the practical utility of the classification for deriving rulings.

بيان أنواع الحسن
وهي كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت، وهتك حرمة المناهي كلها بفعل العباد واختيارهم، أي قضاء حقه أي الزجر عنه
فلهذا اعتبرت الوسائط ههنا وجعلت داخلة في الحسن لغيره، بخلاف وسائط الزكاة والصوم والحج أعني فقر الفقير، وعداوة النفس، وشرف المكان، فإنها بمحض خلق الله تعالى، ولا اختيار فيها للعبد أصلا، ولهذا جعلت من الملحق بالحسن لعينه، فتأمل. والقدرة مثال للشرط الذي حسن المأمور به لأجله لا للمأمور به، وإن قدرت المضاف وقلت ومشروط القدرة كان مثالاً للمأمور به المشروط بها، وإن جعلت ضمير أو يكون حسنًا راجعا إلى الغير كما كان ضمير لا يتأدى أو يتأدى راجعا إليه كما قيل لم ينتشر الكلام وتكون القدرة مثالاً للغير بلا تكلف لكن يكون الشرط حينئذ بمعنى المشروط،

ويكون المعنى أو يكون الغير كالقدرة حسنة لحسن في مشروطها،
وهي كفر الكافر إلخ فيه بحث، فإن كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت وهتك حرمة المناهي ليست مما يتأدى بنفس المأمور به أعني الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة وإقامة الحدود والجواب: أن المراد بحذف المضاف أي إعدام كفر الكافر، وقضاء حق إسلام الميت والزجر عن هتك حرمة المناهي. (القمر) وجعلت أي الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة، وإقامة الحدود.(القمر) أعني فقر الفقير إلخ: هذا إقرار بالحق، ومخالف لظاهر ما سبق من الشارح من أن الواسطة في الزكاة دفع حاجة الفقير، وفي الصوم قهر النفس. (القمر) جعلت أي الزكاة والصوم والحج. (القمر)
ولهذا جعلت إلخ لعل هذا إيفاء لما وعد الشارح قبل الورقة بقوله: كما ستقف عليه فيما بعد. (السنبلي) فتأمل لعله إيماء إلى المباحث التي بيناها (القمر) والقدرة إلخ : دفع دخل تقريره أن هذا المثال ليس بمطابق للمثل له؛ فإنه كان المأمور به الذي حسن الحسن في شرطه إلخ، والقدرة ليس مأمور به بل هو شرطه، ولو جعل الممثل له الغير الذي حسن بواسطته المأمور به لا يكون عبارته السابقة مستقيمة؛ لأن المعنى حينئذ أو يكون الغير حسنًا لحسن في الغير، فإن الشرط هو الغير وهو ليس بصحيح، فأجاب بأن كلاً من ذلك بالتأويل صحيح.(السنبلي) لا للمأمور به: أي ليس مثالاً للمأمور به (القمر) مثالاً للغير إلخ وحينئذ وإن كان المثال مطابقا للممثل له لكن يلزم خلاف المقصود، فإن المقصود تمثيل المأمور به الحسن لغيره كالوضوء، والجهاد، والقدرة ليست مأمورًا بها، ولا تصغ إلى قول من قال أي) المولوي أبو الفضل جونفوري : إنه يلزم على تقدير إرجاع ضمير أو يكون إلى الغير عدم مطابقة المثال للممثل له فتدبر . (القمر)
لكن يكون إلخ ويكون ضمير "كان" في قوله: بعد ما كان إلخ راجعا إلى الشرط بمعنى المشروط.(القمر)
فانقلب المقصود وانعكس المدعى، وبالجملة لا يخلو هذا المقام عن تمحل. ثم وصف القدرة بقوله : يتمكن بها العبد من أداء ما لزمه للإيماء إلى أن هذه القدرة ليست قدرة حقيقية يكون معها الفعل، وتكون علة له بلا تخلف فإن ذلك ليس مدار التكليف؛ لأنه لا يكون سابقا على الفعل حتى يكلف بسببه الفاعل، بل المراد بها ههنا هي القدرة التي بمعنى سلامة الأسباب والآلات وصحة الجوارح، فإنها تتقدم على الفعل، وصحة التكليف إنما يعتمد على هذه الاستطاعة، فقدرة التوضيء حين وجدان الماء، وإلا فالتيمم وقدرة توجه القبلة حين عدم الخوف ووجود العلم، وإلا فجهة القدرة أو التحري، وقدرة القيام حين الصحة، وإلا فالقعود أو الإيماء، وقدرة الزكاة حين ملك النصاب، وإلا فهو معفو، وقدرة الصوم حين الصحة والإقامة وإلا فالقضاء، وقدرة الحج حين وجدان الزاد والراحلة وصحة الأعضاء، وأمن الطريق، وإلا فهو تطوع، وعلى هذا القياس.
وانعكس المدعى: فإنه يلزم حينئذٍ أن الشرط حسن لحسن في مشروطه والمدعى أن المشروط حسن الحسن في شرطه. (القمر) عن تمحل: إما كون القدرة مثالاً للغير لا للمأمور به ، وإما تقدير المضاف (القمر) وصف القدرة دفع دخل وهو: أن المثال لا يكون لتوضيح الممثل له وهو حاصل بقوله: والقدرة فقط، فوصفها بقوله: يتمكن إلخ لغو المحشي) يكون معها الفعل أي معية زمانية وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن العلة التامة، وتتقدم على الفعل بالذات؛ لكونها محتاجة إليها وهي القوة (أي القوة الحقيقية المستجمعة لجميع الشرائط. (القمر) فإن ذلك: أي القدرة الحقيقية ليس مدار التكليف وإلا لما كان الكافر الذي مات على الكفر مكلفا بالإيمان؛ لعدم القدرة الحقيقية؛ لأنها مع الفعل ولم يوجد فلم توجد القدرة (القمر)
فإنها أي القدرة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب إلخ. (القمر) فإنها تتقدم على الفعل إلخ فلو لم يقيد القدرة بقوله: التي يتمكن إلخ لم تحصل هذه الفائدة، ولذهب بعض الأوهام إلى كونها قدرة حقيقية ووقع بذلك في ورطة الظلمة (السنبلي) وصحة التكليف إلخ أي كون العبد مكلفا إنما مداره على هذه الاستطاعة، وإلا لزم تكليف ما لا يطاق، وهو غير جائز عندنا. (السنبلي حين وجدان الماء: أي مع عدم المانع من المرض وغيره. (القمر) فجهة القدرة إلخ: أي عند وجود الخوف القبلة جهة القدرة وعند عدم العلم القبلة جهة التحري ففي الكلام لف نشر مرتب. (القمر)
Discussion of al-Khass: Explanation of the types of al-Hasan: They are: the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the dead, and the violation of the sanctity of all prohibitions by the actions of servants and their choice, i.e., fulfilling its due, i.e., deterring from it. For this reason, the mediators are considered here and made included in al-hasan li-ghayrihi, unlike the mediators of zakat, fasting, and hajj, meaning the poverty of the poor, the enmity of the self, and the honor of the place, for they are purely by the creation of Allah Almighty, and the servant has no choice in them at all, and for this reason they are made among those annexed to al-hasan li-'aynihi. So reflect. And ability (al-qudra) is an example of the condition for which the commanded act is good, not for the commanded act itself. And if you estimate the genitive construction and say 'and the conditional of ability' it would be an example of the commanded act conditioned by it. And if you make the pronoun of 'or be good' referring to the other (al-ghayr) just as the pronoun of 'is not performed' or 'is performed' refers to it, as was said, the speech would not be coherent, and ability would be an example of the other without effort, but then the condition would be in the sense of the conditioned. And ability would be the meaning: or the other like ability is good due to goodness in its conditioned. And 'they are the disbelief of the disbeliever, etc.' contains discussion, for the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the dead, and the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions are not among the things that are performed by the commanded act itself, namely jihad, funeral prayer, and execution of hadd punishments. And the answer: that what is meant is the deletion of the genitive, i.e., the removal of the disbelief of the disbeliever, the fulfillment of the right of the Islam of the dead, and the deterrence from the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions. (al-Qamar) 'And they are made' i.e., jihad, funeral prayer, and execution of hadd. (al-Qamar) 'I mean the poverty of the poor, etc.': this is an acknowledgment of the truth, and contradicts the apparent meaning of what the commentator previously stated that the mediator in zakat is the removal of the poor's need, and in fasting is conquering the self. (al-Qamar) 'Made' i.e., zakat, fasting, and hajj. (al-Qamar) 'And for this reason they are made, etc.' Perhaps this is a fulfillment of what the commentator promised before the folio by his statement: 'as you will come across it later.' (al-Sunbuli) 'So reflect' perhaps alludes to the discussions we have explained. (al-Qamar) 'And ability, etc.' is a rebuttal of an objection. Its explanation: that this example does not correspond to the thing exemplified; for the commanded act was such that goodness is due to its condition, etc., and ability is not a commanded act but rather its condition. And if the thing exemplified is made the other (al-ghayr) through which the commanded act becomes good, his previous expression would not be straightforward, because the meaning then would be: or the other is good due to goodness in the other, for the condition is the other, and that is not correct. So he answered that each of these is correct by interpretation. (al-Sunbuli) 'Not for the commanded act' i.e., it is not an example for the commanded act. (al-Qamar) 'An example for the other, etc.' And then, even if the example corresponds to the thing exemplified, it contradicts the intent, for the intent is to exemplify the commanded act that is hasan li-ghayrihi like wudu and jihad, and ability is not commanded. And do not listen to the word of him who said (i.e., Mawlawi Abu al-Fadl Junfuri): that on the assumption of referring the pronoun of 'or be' to the other, there would be a lack of correspondence between the example and the thing exemplified, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'But it would be, etc.' And the pronoun of 'was' in his statement: 'after it was, etc.' refers to the condition in the sense of the conditioned. (al-Qamar) So the intended meaning turned around and the claim reversed. In short, this station is not free from artificiality. Then he described ability by his statement: 'by which the servant is able to perform what is incumbent upon him' to indicate that this ability is not the real ability with which the act occurs and which is a cause of it without fail, for that is not the basis of obligation; because it does not precede the act so that the doer is obligated on account of it. Rather, what is meant here is the ability in the sense of soundness of causes and instruments and soundness of limbs, for they precede the act, and the soundness of obligation is based on this capacity. So the ability for wudu at the time of finding water, otherwise tayammum; the ability to face the qibla at the time of absence of fear and presence of knowledge, otherwise the direction of ability or ijtihad; the ability to stand at the time of health, otherwise sitting or gestures; the ability for zakat at the time of possessing the nisab, otherwise it is forgiven; the ability for fasting at the time of health and residence, otherwise the make-up; the ability for hajj at the time of finding provision and mount, soundness of limbs, and safety of road, otherwise it is voluntary. And so on analogically. And the claim reversed: for then it would require that the condition is good due to goodness in its conditioned, while the claim is that the conditioned is good due to goodness in its condition. (al-Qamar) 'From artificiality' either because ability is an example for the other not for the commanded act, or because of the estimation of the genitive. (al-Qamar) 'Described ability' rebuts an objection which is: that the example does not clarify the thing exemplified, and it is obtained by his statement: 'and ability' only, so describing it by his statement: 'by which he is able, etc.' is redundant. (al-Muhashi) 'The act occurs with it' i.e., temporal concomitance, otherwise it would require the effect to be delayed from the complete cause, and it precedes the act in essence because it is needed for it, and it is the power (i.e., the real power that includes all conditions). (al-Qamar) 'For that' i.e., real ability is not the basis of obligation, otherwise the disbeliever who died in disbelief would not be obligated to believe, due to the absence of real ability; because it is with the act, and since the act did not occur, ability did not exist. (al-Qamar) 'For it' i.e., ability in the sense of soundness of causes, etc. (al-Qamar) 'For it precedes the act, etc.' So if ability had not been restricted by his statement: 'by which he is able, etc.' this benefit would not be obtained, and some misconceptions would lead to it being real ability and thus falling into the trap of darkness. (al-Sunbuli) 'And the soundness of obligation, etc.' i.e., the soundness of the servant being obligated is based on this capacity, otherwise it would require the imposition of what is unbearable, which is not permissible according to us. (al-Sunbuli) 'At the time of finding water' i.e., with the absence of impediment like illness, etc. (al-Qamar) 'So the direction of ability, etc.' i.e., when there is fear, the direction of the qibla is the direction of ability, and when there is no knowledge of the qibla, the direction is ijtihad. So in the speech there is a disarranged and arranged form. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the matn explains the types of al-Hasan (goodness/beauty) as applied to actions in Hanafi usul. The author distinguishes between actions that are good in themselves (al-hasan li-'aynihi) and those that are good due to something else (al-hasan li-ghayrihi). The examples given show that jihad, funeral prayer, and hadd punishments are good due to their results (removing disbelief, causing Islam of the dead, deterring violations), and these results are within human choice, hence the means are considered hasan li-ghayrihi. In contrast, for zakat, fasting, and hajj, the beneficial outcomes (poverty of the poor, conquering the self, honor of the place) are purely from Allah's creation, not from human choice, so these acts are annexed to hasan li-'aynihi. The passage then delves into a debate about the example of ability (qudra). Some scholars argued that ability is not a commanded act but a condition, so it cannot be an example for the commanded act that is hasan li-ghayrihi. The commentator reconciles by interpreting ability either as a condition or as the conditioned act itself depending on the pronoun reference. Finally, the passage clarifies that the ability relevant to taklif is not the real ability that coincides with the act (as that would make impossible obligations), but rather the ability in the sense of sound health, available means, and absence of impediments. This is the capacity that precedes the act and forms the basis of obligation. Examples are given for various acts of worship, showing the different requirements and alternatives (tayammum, sitting, etc.) when the condition is missing. The overall lesson is a nuanced discussion of how goodness is attributed to actions and the role of conditions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
الحسن لعينه (al-ḥasan li-ʿaynihi): An action that is good in itself, not dependent on external beneficial results.
الحسن لغيره (al-ḥasan li-ghayrihi): An action that is good due to some external beneficial outcome that it achieves.
الوسائط (al-wasā'iṭ): The mediators or intermediate beneficial outcomes through which an action becomes good.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the act of jihad considered ḥasan li-ghayrihi while the act of zakat is annexed to ḥasan li-ʿaynihi?
A) Because jihad is a fard while zakat is a sunnah.
B) Because the beneficial outcome of jihad (removing disbelief) is within human choice, while that of zakat (poverty relief) is purely from Allah.
C) Because jihad involves killing which is essentially bad, while zakat is essentially good.
D) Because jihad is a physical act while zakat is a financial act.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the goodness of an action is either intrinsic (if its beneficial outcome is solely from Allah) or extrinsic (if the outcome is within human choice), and this classification affects how the act is analogized.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Concept of Ability (Qudra) in Legal Obligation
Clarifying the nature of ability (qudra) as a condition for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between real ability (coincident with the act) and capacity (prior soundness of means) and apply it to determine the basis of obligation.

Core Idea
Ability for obligation is the prior capacity of sound means and limbs, not the real power simultaneous with the act.

One of the most subtle points in Hanafi usul is the concept of ability (qudra) relevant to taklif. The passage clarifies that the ability that makes an act wajib is not the power to perform the act at the moment of doing it, but rather the pre-existing soundness of causes, instruments, and limbs. Without this distinction, we would fall into impossible obligations or exemptions that contradict revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem with ability as an example
The passage starts by raising an objection: if ability (qudra) is used as an example for the 'other' (al-ghayr) that makes an act good, it does not fit because ability is a condition, not a commanded act. Understand why this creates a mismatch.
The author notes that if we interpret the pronouns differently, ability can be an example for the conditioned act, but then the meaning becomes strained.
2
Understand the final resolution
The commentator resolves by saying that regardless of the grammatical issue, the intended meaning is that this ability is not real power but prior capacity. Locate the key sentence: 'the ability in the sense of soundness of causes and instruments and soundness of limbs.'
This is the core definition: al-qudra = salāmat al-asbāb wa al-ālāt wa ṣiḥḥat al-jawāriḥ.
3
Apply the definition to different acts of worship
The passage lists examples: wudu (ability = finding water), qibla (absence of fear and knowledge), standing (health), zakat (nisab), fasting (health and residence), hajj (provision, mount, etc.). For each, if the condition is missing, a substitute (tayammum, sitting, qada, etc.) applies.
Note that these conditions are all prior: one must have water before wudu, health before standing, etc.
4
Contrast with real ability and avoid misconception
The passage warns against thinking that ability means real power that arises simultaneously with the act. That would make obligation impossible for those who never perform the act (e.g., a disbeliever who dies in disbelief could not be obligated to believe).
Therefore, the capacity that precedes the act is the basis of taklif, preventing the impossible burden.

مبحث الخاص
بيان أنواع الحسن
وهي كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت، وهتك حرمة المناهي كلها بفعل العباد واختيارهم، أي قضاء حقه أي الزجر عنه
فلهذا اعتبرت الوسائط ههنا وجعلت داخلة في الحسن لغيره، بخلاف وسائط الزكاة والصوم والحج أعني فقر الفقير، وعداوة النفس، وشرف المكان، فإنها بمحض خلق الله تعالى، ولا اختيار فيها للعبد أصلا، ولهذا جعلت من الملحق بالحسن لعينه، فتأمل. والقدرة مثال للشرط الذي حسن المأمور به لأجله لا للمأمور به، وإن قدرت المضاف وقلت ومشروط القدرة كان مثالاً للمأمور به المشروط بها، وإن جعلت ضمير أو يكون حسنًا راجعا إلى الغير كما كان ضمير لا يتأدى أو يتأدى راجعا إليه كما قيل لم ينتشر الكلام وتكون القدرة مثالاً للغير بلا تكلف لكن يكون الشرط حينئذ بمعنى المشروط،
القدرة
ويكون المعنى أو يكون الغير كالقدرة حسنة لحسن في مشروطها،
وهي كفر الكافر إلخ فيه بحث، فإن كفر الكافر، وإسلام الميت وهتك حرمة المناهي ليست مما يتأدى بنفس المأمور به أعني الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة وإقامة الحدود والجواب: أن المراد بحذف المضاف أي إعدام كفر الكافر، وقضاء حق إسلام الميت والزجر عن هتك حرمة المناهي. (القمر) وجعلت أي الجهاد، وصلاة الجنازة، وإقامة الحدود.(القمر) أعني فقر الفقير إلخ: هذا إقرار بالحق، ومخالف لظاهر ما سبق من الشارح من أن الواسطة في الزكاة دفع حاجة الفقير، وفي الصوم قهر النفس. (القمر) جعلت أي الزكاة والصوم والحج. (القمر)
ولهذا جعلت إلخ لعل هذا إيفاء لما وعد الشارح قبل الورقة بقوله: كما ستقف عليه فيما بعد. (السنبلي) فتأمل لعله إيماء إلى المباحث التي بيناها (القمر) والقدرة إلخ : دفع دخل تقريره أن هذا المثال ليس بمطابق للمثل له؛ فإنه كان المأمور به الذي حسن الحسن في شرطه إلخ، والقدرة ليس مأمور به بل هو شرطه، ولو جعل الممثل له الغير الذي حسن بواسطته المأمور به لا يكون عبارته السابقة مستقيمة؛ لأن المعنى حينئذ أو يكون الغير حسنًا لحسن في الغير، فإن الشرط هو الغير وهو ليس بصحيح، فأجاب بأن كلاً من ذلك بالتأويل صحيح.(السنبلي) لا للمأمور به: أي ليس مثالاً للمأمور به (القمر) مثالاً للغير إلخ وحينئذ وإن كان المثال مطابقا للممثل له لكن يلزم خلاف المقصود، فإن المقصود تمثيل المأمور به الحسن لغيره كالوضوء، والجهاد، والقدرة ليست مأمورًا بها، ولا تصغ إلى قول من قال أي) المولوي أبو الفضل جونفوري : إنه يلزم على تقدير إرجاع ضمير أو يكون إلى الغير عدم مطابقة المثال للممثل له فتدبر . (القمر)
لكن يكون إلخ ويكون ضمير "كان" في قوله: بعد ما كان إلخ راجعا إلى الشرط بمعنى المشروط.(القمر)
فانقلب المقصود وانعكس المدعى، وبالجملة لا يخلو هذا المقام عن تمحل. ثم وصف القدرة بقوله : يتمكن بها العبد من أداء ما لزمه للإيماء إلى أن هذه القدرة ليست قدرة حقيقية يكون معها الفعل، وتكون علة له بلا تخلف فإن ذلك ليس مدار التكليف؛ لأنه لا يكون سابقا على الفعل حتى يكلف بسببه الفاعل، بل المراد بها ههنا هي القدرة التي بمعنى سلامة الأسباب والآلات وصحة الجوارح، فإنها تتقدم على الفعل، وصحة التكليف إنما يعتمد على هذه الاستطاعة، فقدرة التوضيء حين وجدان الماء، وإلا فالتيمم وقدرة توجه القبلة حين عدم الخوف ووجود العلم، وإلا فجهة القدرة أو التحري، وقدرة القيام حين الصحة، وإلا فالقعود أو الإيماء، وقدرة الزكاة حين ملك النصاب، وإلا فهو معفو، وقدرة الصوم حين الصحة والإقامة وإلا فالقضاء، وقدرة الحج حين وجدان الزاد والراحلة وصحة الأعضاء، وأمن الطريق، وإلا فهو تطوع، وعلى هذا القياس.
وانعكس المدعى: فإنه يلزم حينئذٍ أن الشرط حسن لحسن في مشروطه والمدعى أن المشروط حسن الحسن في شرطه. (القمر) عن تمحل: إما كون القدرة مثالاً للغير لا للمأمور به ، وإما تقدير المضاف (القمر) وصف القدرة دفع دخل وهو: أن المثال لا يكون لتوضيح الممثل له وهو حاصل بقوله: والقدرة فقط، فوصفها بقوله: يتمكن إلخ لغو المحشي) يكون معها الفعل أي معية زمانية وإلا يلزم تخلف المعلول عن العلة التامة، وتتقدم على الفعل بالذات؛ لكونها محتاجة إليها وهي القوة (أي القوة الحقيقية المستجمعة لجميع الشرائط. (القمر) فإن ذلك: أي القدرة الحقيقية ليس مدار التكليف وإلا لما كان الكافر الذي مات على الكفر مكلفا بالإيمان؛ لعدم القدرة الحقيقية؛ لأنها مع الفعل ولم يوجد فلم توجد القدرة (القمر)
فإنها أي القدرة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب إلخ. (القمر) فإنها تتقدم على الفعل إلخ فلو لم يقيد القدرة بقوله: التي يتمكن إلخ لم تحصل هذه الفائدة، ولذهب بعض الأوهام إلى كونها قدرة حقيقية ووقع بذلك في ورطة الظلمة (السنبلي) وصحة التكليف إلخ أي كون العبد مكلفا إنما مداره على هذه الاستطاعة، وإلا لزم تكليف ما لا يطاق، وهو غير جائز عندنا. (السنبلي حين وجدان الماء: أي مع عدم المانع من المرض وغيره. (القمر) فجهة القدرة إلخ: أي عند وجود الخوف القبلة جهة القدرة وعند عدم العلم القبلة جهة التحري ففي الكلام لف نشر مرتب. (القمر)
Discussion of al-Khass: Explanation of the types of al-Hasan: They are: the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the dead, and the violation of the sanctity of all prohibitions by the actions of servants and their choice, i.e., fulfilling its due, i.e., deterring from it. For this reason, the mediators are considered here and made included in al-hasan li-ghayrihi, unlike the mediators of zakat, fasting, and hajj, meaning the poverty of the poor, the enmity of the self, and the honor of the place, for they are purely by the creation of Allah Almighty, and the servant has no choice in them at all, and for this reason they are made among those annexed to al-hasan li-'aynihi. So reflect. And ability (al-qudra) is an example of the condition for which the commanded act is good, not for the commanded act itself. And if you estimate the genitive construction and say 'and the conditional of ability' it would be an example of the commanded act conditioned by it. And if you make the pronoun of 'or be good' referring to the other (al-ghayr) just as the pronoun of 'is not performed' or 'is performed' refers to it, as was said, the speech would not be coherent, and ability would be an example of the other without effort, but then the condition would be in the sense of the conditioned. And ability would be the meaning: or the other like ability is good due to goodness in its conditioned. And 'they are the disbelief of the disbeliever, etc.' contains discussion, for the disbelief of the disbeliever, the Islam of the dead, and the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions are not among the things that are performed by the commanded act itself, namely jihad, funeral prayer, and execution of hadd punishments. And the answer: that what is meant is the deletion of the genitive, i.e., the removal of the disbelief of the disbeliever, the fulfillment of the right of the Islam of the dead, and the deterrence from the violation of the sanctity of prohibitions. (al-Qamar) 'And they are made' i.e., jihad, funeral prayer, and execution of hadd. (al-Qamar) 'I mean the poverty of the poor, etc.': this is an acknowledgment of the truth, and contradicts the apparent meaning of what the commentator previously stated that the mediator in zakat is the removal of the poor's need, and in fasting is conquering the self. (al-Qamar) 'Made' i.e., zakat, fasting, and hajj. (al-Qamar) 'And for this reason they are made, etc.' Perhaps this is a fulfillment of what the commentator promised before the folio by his statement: 'as you will come across it later.' (al-Sunbuli) 'So reflect' perhaps alludes to the discussions we have explained. (al-Qamar) 'And ability, etc.' is a rebuttal of an objection. Its explanation: that this example does not correspond to the thing exemplified; for the commanded act was such that goodness is due to its condition, etc., and ability is not a commanded act but rather its condition. And if the thing exemplified is made the other (al-ghayr) through which the commanded act becomes good, his previous expression would not be straightforward, because the meaning then would be: or the other is good due to goodness in the other, for the condition is the other, and that is not correct. So he answered that each of these is correct by interpretation. (al-Sunbuli) 'Not for the commanded act' i.e., it is not an example for the commanded act. (al-Qamar) 'An example for the other, etc.' And then, even if the example corresponds to the thing exemplified, it contradicts the intent, for the intent is to exemplify the commanded act that is hasan li-ghayrihi like wudu and jihad, and ability is not commanded. And do not listen to the word of him who said (i.e., Mawlawi Abu al-Fadl Junfuri): that on the assumption of referring the pronoun of 'or be' to the other, there would be a lack of correspondence between the example and the thing exemplified, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'But it would be, etc.' And the pronoun of 'was' in his statement: 'after it was, etc.' refers to the condition in the sense of the conditioned. (al-Qamar) So the intended meaning turned around and the claim reversed. In short, this station is not free from artificiality. Then he described ability by his statement: 'by which the servant is able to perform what is incumbent upon him' to indicate that this ability is not the real ability with which the act occurs and which is a cause of it without fail, for that is not the basis of obligation; because it does not precede the act so that the doer is obligated on account of it. Rather, what is meant here is the ability in the sense of soundness of causes and instruments and soundness of limbs, for they precede the act, and the soundness of obligation is based on this capacity. So the ability for wudu at the time of finding water, otherwise tayammum; the ability to face the qibla at the time of absence of fear and presence of knowledge, otherwise the direction of ability or ijtihad; the ability to stand at the time of health, otherwise sitting or gestures; the ability for zakat at the time of possessing the nisab, otherwise it is forgiven; the ability for fasting at the time of health and residence, otherwise the make-up; the ability for hajj at the time of finding provision and mount, soundness of limbs, and safety of road, otherwise it is voluntary. And so on analogically. And the claim reversed: for then it would require that the condition is good due to goodness in its conditioned, while the claim is that the conditioned is good due to goodness in its condition. (al-Qamar) 'From artificiality' either because ability is an example for the other not for the commanded act, or because of the estimation of the genitive. (al-Qamar) 'Described ability' rebuts an objection which is: that the example does not clarify the thing exemplified, and it is obtained by his statement: 'and ability' only, so describing it by his statement: 'by which he is able, etc.' is redundant. (al-Muhashi) 'The act occurs with it' i.e., temporal concomitance, otherwise it would require the effect to be delayed from the complete cause, and it precedes the act in essence because it is needed for it, and it is the power (i.e., the real power that includes all conditions). (al-Qamar) 'For that' i.e., real ability is not the basis of obligation, otherwise the disbeliever who died in disbelief would not be obligated to believe, due to the absence of real ability; because it is with the act, and since the act did not occur, ability did not exist. (al-Qamar) 'For it' i.e., ability in the sense of soundness of causes, etc. (al-Qamar) 'For it precedes the act, etc.' So if ability had not been restricted by his statement: 'by which he is able, etc.' this benefit would not be obtained, and some misconceptions would lead to it being real ability and thus falling into the trap of darkness. (al-Sunbuli) 'And the soundness of obligation, etc.' i.e., the soundness of the servant being obligated is based on this capacity, otherwise it would require the imposition of what is unbearable, which is not permissible according to us. (al-Sunbuli) 'At the time of finding water' i.e., with the absence of impediment like illness, etc. (al-Qamar) 'So the direction of ability, etc.' i.e., when there is fear, the direction of the qibla is the direction of ability, and when there is no knowledge of the qibla, the direction is ijtihad. So in the speech there is a disarranged and arranged form. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the matn explains the types of al-Hasan (goodness/beauty) as applied to actions in Hanafi usul. The author distinguishes between actions that are good in themselves (al-hasan li-'aynihi) and those that are good due to something else (al-hasan li-ghayrihi). The examples given show that jihad, funeral prayer, and hadd punishments are good due to their results (removing disbelief, causing Islam of the dead, deterring violations), and these results are within human choice, hence the means are considered hasan li-ghayrihi. In contrast, for zakat, fasting, and hajj, the beneficial outcomes (poverty of the poor, conquering the self, honor of the place) are purely from Allah's creation, not from human choice, so these acts are annexed to hasan li-'aynihi. The passage then delves into a debate about the example of ability (qudra). Some scholars argued that ability is not a commanded act but a condition, so it cannot be an example for the commanded act that is hasan li-ghayrihi. The commentator reconciles by interpreting ability either as a condition or as the conditioned act itself depending on the pronoun reference. Finally, the passage clarifies that the ability relevant to taklif is not the real ability that coincides with the act (as that would make impossible obligations), but rather the ability in the sense of sound health, available means, and absence of impediments. This is the capacity that precedes the act and forms the basis of obligation. Examples are given for various acts of worship, showing the different requirements and alternatives (tayammum, sitting, etc.) when the condition is missing. The overall lesson is a nuanced discussion of how goodness is attributed to actions and the role of conditions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Not real ability (coincident with act) but capacity in the sense of soundness of causes, instruments, and limbs, which precedes the act and is the basis of obligation.
القدرة الحقيقية (al-qudra al-ḥaqīqiyya): Real power that is simultaneous with the act and is a cause of it without fail. This is not the basis of taklif.
سلامة الأسباب والآلات (salāmat al-asbāb wa al-ālāt): Soundness of causes and instruments – a component of the ability that precedes the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ability (qudra) that forms the basis of obligation (taklif)?
A) Real power that occurs simultaneously with the act.
B) Soundness of causes, instruments, and limbs that precede the act.
C) The absence of any external impediments.
D) The certainty that the act will be performed perfectly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of ability for obligation is the prior capacity of sound means and limbs, not the real power to perform the act at the very moment.

The Nature of Capability in Taklif: Real vs. Soundness of Means
Defining capability and distinguishing real capability from soundness of means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real capability and capability as soundness of means, and explain why the latter is the basis of obligation in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Taklif depends on capability as soundness of means, not real capability that accompanies the act.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational concept in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the type of capability that makes religious obligations valid. The text clarifies that the capability required for obligation is not the real capability that coincides with the act, but rather the capacity that precedes it—soundness of means and health of limbs. This distinction is crucial for understanding when an obligation becomes binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two concepts of capability
In the text, the author distinguishes between 'real capability' (القدرة الحقيقية) and 'capability in the sense of soundness of means' (القدرة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب). Locate these terms in the Arabic passage.
The passage uses the phrase 'ليس مدار التكليف' to deny real capability as the basis.
2
Understand the timing of each capability
Real capability occurs with the act (مع الفعل) and is a cause without delay. Capability as soundness of means precedes the act (تتقدم على الفعل). Explain why only the latter can be a condition for obligation.
The author gives the example: if real capability were required, a disbeliever who dies on disbelief would not have been obligated to believe.
3
Apply the distinction to examples
The text lists several obligations: wudu, qibla direction, standing, zakat, fasting, hajj. For each, identify the required capability as soundness of means.
Example: capability of wudu is finding water (with absence of illness).
4
Cite the Quranic proof
The passage references Quran 2:286: 'Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity.' Explain how this verse supports the Hanafi position that obligation is based on pre-existing capacity, not simultaneous real capability.
The dalil_block in the source provides the wajh al-dalalah.

Statement of the types of good. Then the intended meaning is inverted and the claim is reversed; in short, this situation is not free from contrivance. Then he described capability by his saying: 'the servant can perform what is obligatory upon him' to indicate that this capability is not real capability by which the act occurs, being a cause without delay, for that is not the basis of obligation; because it does not precede the act so that the agent is obligated due to it. Rather, what is meant here is the capability that is in the sense of soundness of means and organs and health of limbs, for it precedes the act. The validity of obligation depends on this capacity. So the capability of performing ablution is at the time of finding water; otherwise, tayammum. The capability of facing the qibla is at the time of absence of fear and presence of knowledge; otherwise, the direction of capability or ijtihad. The capability of standing is at the time of health; otherwise, sitting or gestures. The capability of zakat is at the time of owning the nisab; otherwise, it is forgiven. The capability of fasting is at the time of health and residence; otherwise, making up. The capability of Hajj is at the time of finding provision and mount, health of limbs, and safety of the road; otherwise, it is supererogatory. And on this analogy.
And the claim is reversed: for then it would follow that the condition is good for good in its conditional, while the claim is that the conditional is good for good in its condition. (al-Qamar) Regarding contrivance: either the capability is an example for something else not for the commanded act, or estimation of the genitive. (al-Qamar) Describing capability refutes an objection, which is: the example would not clarify the thing exemplified, which is obtained by his saying 'capability' alone, so describing it by his saying 'can perform' etc. is redundant (al-Muhashi). The act occurs with it, i.e., temporal concomitance; otherwise, the effect would be delayed from the complete cause. And it precedes the act by essence because it needs it, and it is the strength (i.e., real strength combining all conditions). (al-Qamar) For that: i.e., real capability is not the basis of obligation; otherwise, the disbeliever who died on disbelief would not have been obligated with faith due to lack of real capability; because it is with the act, and since the act did not occur, capability did not exist. (al-Qamar)
For it: i.e., capability in the sense of soundness of means etc. (al-Qamar) For it precedes the act etc. If he had not restricted capability by his saying 'by which [the servant] can [perform]' etc., this benefit would not be obtained, and some minds would think it is real capability and fall into the blunder of injustice (al-Sanbali). And the validity of obligation etc., i.e., the servant being obligated depends on this capacity; otherwise, obligation of what is beyond capacity would follow, which is not permissible according to us. (al-Sanbali) At the time of finding water: i.e., with absence of preventer like illness etc. (al-Qamar) So the direction of capability etc.: i.e., at the time of fear of the qibla, the direction of capability; at the time of ignorance of the qibla, the direction of ijtihad; so in the speech there is ordered disjunction. (al-Qamar)

Statement of the division of capability
Then he divided this capability into absolute and complete, saying: It is two types: absolute, i.e., the capability by which the servant can [perform], and it is in the sense of soundness of means and organs, two types: one of them is absolute, i.e., not restricted by the quality of ease and facility as in the following division, and it is the minimum by which the commanded person can perform what is obligatory upon him, and it is a condition for the performance of every command. i.e., the absolute is the minimum by which the servant can [perform], and this amount of capability is a condition for the performance of every command, and the rest is additional. It is the amount that accommodates four rak'ats of Zuhr. If he is satisfied with this, it is called possible capability, which the author called absolute. He should have said: absolute and restricted for proper opposition, or complete and deficient. By adding the word 'minimum', the divisor and the division are distinguished; because the divisor is that by which the servant can [perform], and the division is the minimum by which the servant can [perform]. So the objection that a thing is divided into itself and another is not raised. He restricted it to the performance of every command because for making up, this capability is not required absolutely.
The author: This capability: i.e., the capability by which the servant can perform what is obligatory upon him. (al-Qamar) 'By which' etc.: the word 'by which' refers to capability. (al-Qamar) In the performance etc.: the genitive is omitted, i.e., in the obligation of performance of every command, i.e., every commanded act whether religious like prayer or financial like zakat. We estimated the genitive because the apparent wording of the author is not sound; for this capability is a condition for the obligation of performance, not for the performance itself; for the condition of performance is real capability, not this capability. (al-Qamar) The minimum by which the servant can [perform]: because it would be objected that they said that provision and mount in Hajj are from possible capability, although Hajj is performed without the mount as well, so provision and mount are not the minimum by which the servant can [perform]; some added another restriction, which is a way free from hardship, and Hajj without mount occurs but is not free from hardship, so reflect. (al-Qamar) Condition: and obligation of what is beyond capacity is negated by the Almighty's saying: "Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity" (Quran 2:286). (al-Qamar) And it: i.e., this amount, i.e., the minimum. (al-Qamar) And by adding the word 'minimum' etc.: refutes an estimated objection, the import of which is: that here the divisor unites with the division because the divisor was the capability by which the servant can [perform] and the division is the same; he answered that it is not so, but rather there is a difference between them by adding the word 'minimum' in the division and its absence in the divisor. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a definition and division of capability (قدرة) in the context of taklif. The author begins by clarifying that the capability required for obligation is not real capability (القدرة الحقيقية) which coexists with the act, but rather capability in the sense of soundness of means (سلامة الأسباب) and health of limbs, which precedes the act. This is the basis of valid obligation. Examples include: ablution when water is available, tayammum when not; facing qibla when fear is absent and knowledge present, otherwise direction of capability or ijtihad. The passage then divides this capability into two types: absolute (مطلق) and complete (كامل). Absolute capability is the minimum required for performance of any commanded act, e.g., enough time for four rak'ats of Zuhr. It is a condition for the obligation of performance. Complete capability includes ease and facility. The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sanbali clarifies that absolute capability is a condition for the obligation of performance (وجوب الأداء), not for the performance itself, which requires real capability. The Quranic verse (2:286) is invoked to negate burdening beyond capacity.

Key Terms
القدرة الحقيقية (al-qudra al-haqīqiyya): القدرة التي تكون مع الفعل وتكون علة له بلا تخلف
القدرة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب والآلات (al-qudra bi-ma‘nā salāmat al-asbāb wa’l-ālāt): الاستطاعة التي تتقدم على الفعل وتكون شرطاً لوجوب الأداء
القدرة المطلقة (al-qudra al-muṭlaqa): أدنى ما يتمكن به العبد من أداء المأمور به، وهي غير مقيدة باليسر والسهولة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the condition for the obligation of performance (وجوب الأداء)?
A) Real capability
B) Capability as soundness of means
C) Complete capability
D) Both absolute and complete capability

Key Takeaway
The capability that makes an obligation valid is soundness of means, not real capability that coincides with the act.

The Division of Capability: Absolute and Complete
Dividing capability into absolute and complete.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define absolute and complete capability, and explain their roles in the obligation and performance of acts.

Core Idea
Absolute capability is the minimum condition for obligation; complete capability adds ease but is not required.

Having established that capability is soundness of means, the author now divides that capability into absolute and complete. Absolute capability is the bare minimum needed to perform an act, such as the time for four rak'ats. It is a condition for the obligation of performance. Complete capability includes additional ease. This division clarifies the boundary of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of capability
The text states: 'It is two types: absolute and complete.' Locate the definitions: absolute is not restricted by ease and is the minimum to perform; complete includes ease.
The author notes that absolute capability is the minimum by which the servant can perform what is obligatory.
2
Understand the function of absolute capability
Absolute capability is a condition for the obligation of performance (شرط في وجوب الأداء). The commentary clarifies that it is not a condition for performance itself, which requires real capability.
The text gives the example: the amount that accommodates four rak'ats of Zuhr.
3
Distinguish absolute from real capability
Absolute capability (soundness of means) is different from real capability. Real capability is needed for the actual performance, but absolute capability is needed only for the obligation.
The commentary says: 'For the condition of performance is real capability, not this capability.'
4
Apply the division to examples
Consider different acts: prayer, zakat, hajj. What is the absolute capability for each? The text implies that absolute capability varies by act, e.g., for Hajj it includes provision and mount, but others argue that the minimum might be less.
The passage mentions a debate: provision and mount in Hajj are considered possible capability, but Hajj can be performed without a mount, so they are not the minimum.
