Statement of the types of good. Then the intended meaning is inverted and the claim is reversed; in short, this situation is not free from contrivance. Then he described capability by his saying: 'the servant can perform what is obligatory upon him' to indicate that this capability is not real capability by which the act occurs, being a cause without delay, for that is not the basis of obligation; because it does not precede the act so that the agent is obligated due to it. Rather, what is meant here is the capability that is in the sense of soundness of means and organs and health of limbs, for it precedes the act. The validity of obligation depends on this capacity. So the capability of performing ablution is at the time of finding water; otherwise, tayammum. The capability of facing the qibla is at the time of absence of fear and presence of knowledge; otherwise, the direction of capability or ijtihad. The capability of standing is at the time of health; otherwise, sitting or gestures. The capability of zakat is at the time of owning the nisab; otherwise, it is forgiven. The capability of fasting is at the time of health and residence; otherwise, making up. The capability of Hajj is at the time of finding provision and mount, health of limbs, and safety of the road; otherwise, it is supererogatory. And on this analogy.
And the claim is reversed: for then it would follow that the condition is good for good in its conditional, while the claim is that the conditional is good for good in its condition. (al-Qamar) Regarding contrivance: either the capability is an example for something else not for the commanded act, or estimation of the genitive. (al-Qamar) Describing capability refutes an objection, which is: the example would not clarify the thing exemplified, which is obtained by his saying 'capability' alone, so describing it by his saying 'can perform' etc. is redundant (al-Muhashi). The act occurs with it, i.e., temporal concomitance; otherwise, the effect would be delayed from the complete cause. And it precedes the act by essence because it needs it, and it is the strength (i.e., real strength combining all conditions). (al-Qamar) For that: i.e., real capability is not the basis of obligation; otherwise, the disbeliever who died on disbelief would not have been obligated with faith due to lack of real capability; because it is with the act, and since the act did not occur, capability did not exist. (al-Qamar)
For it: i.e., capability in the sense of soundness of means etc. (al-Qamar) For it precedes the act etc. If he had not restricted capability by his saying 'by which [the servant] can [perform]' etc., this benefit would not be obtained, and some minds would think it is real capability and fall into the blunder of injustice (al-Sanbali). And the validity of obligation etc., i.e., the servant being obligated depends on this capacity; otherwise, obligation of what is beyond capacity would follow, which is not permissible according to us. (al-Sanbali) At the time of finding water: i.e., with absence of preventer like illness etc. (al-Qamar) So the direction of capability etc.: i.e., at the time of fear of the qibla, the direction of capability; at the time of ignorance of the qibla, the direction of ijtihad; so in the speech there is ordered disjunction. (al-Qamar)

Section on the Specific
135
Statement of the division of capability
Then he divided this capability into absolute and complete, saying: It is two types: absolute, i.e., the capability by which the servant can [perform], and it is in the sense of soundness of means and organs, two types: one of them is absolute, i.e., not restricted by the quality of ease and facility as in the following division, and it is the minimum by which the commanded person can perform what is obligatory upon him, and it is a condition for the performance of every command. i.e., the absolute is the minimum by which the servant can [perform], and this amount of capability is a condition for the performance of every command, and the rest is additional. It is the amount that accommodates four rak'ats of Zuhr. If he is satisfied with this, it is called possible capability, which the author called absolute. He should have said: absolute and restricted for proper opposition, or complete and deficient. By adding the word 'minimum', the divisor and the division are distinguished; because the divisor is that by which the servant can [perform], and the division is the minimum by which the servant can [perform]. So the objection that a thing is divided into itself and another is not raised. He restricted it to the performance of every command because for making up, this capability is not required absolutely.
The author: This capability: i.e., the capability by which the servant can perform what is obligatory upon him. (al-Qamar) 'By which' etc.: the word 'by which' refers to capability. (al-Qamar) In the performance etc.: the genitive is omitted, i.e., in the obligation of performance of every command, i.e., every commanded act whether religious like prayer or financial like zakat. We estimated the genitive because the apparent wording of the author is not sound; for this capability is a condition for the obligation of performance, not for the performance itself; for the condition of performance is real capability, not this capability. (al-Qamar) The minimum by which the servant can [perform]: because it would be objected that they said that provision and mount in Hajj are from possible capability, although Hajj is performed without the mount as well, so provision and mount are not the minimum by which the servant can [perform]; some added another restriction, which is a way free from hardship, and Hajj without mount occurs but is not free from hardship, so reflect. (al-Qamar) Condition: and obligation of what is beyond capacity is negated by the Almighty's saying: "Allah does not burden a soul except its capacity" (Quran 2:286). (al-Qamar) And it: i.e., this amount, i.e., the minimum. (al-Qamar) And by adding the word 'minimum' etc.: refutes an estimated objection, the import of which is: that here the divisor unites with the division because the divisor was the capability by which the servant can [perform] and the division is the same; he answered that it is not so, but rather there is a difference between them by adding the word 'minimum' in the division and its absence in the divisor. (al-Sanbali)
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a definition and division of capability (قدرة) in the context of taklif. The author begins by clarifying that the capability required for obligation is not real capability (القدرة الحقيقية) which coexists with the act, but rather capability in the sense of soundness of means (سلامة الأسباب) and health of limbs, which precedes the act. This is the basis of valid obligation. Examples include: ablution when water is available, tayammum when not; facing qibla when fear is absent and knowledge present, otherwise direction of capability or ijtihad. The passage then divides this capability into two types: absolute (مطلق) and complete (كامل). Absolute capability is the minimum required for performance of any commanded act, e.g., enough time for four rak'ats of Zuhr. It is a condition for the obligation of performance. Complete capability includes ease and facility. The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sanbali clarifies that absolute capability is a condition for the obligation of performance (وجوب الأداء), not for the performance itself, which requires real capability. The Quranic verse (2:286) is invoked to negate burdening beyond capacity.

Key Terms
القدرة الحقيقية (al-qudra al-haqīqiyya): القدرة التي تكون مع الفعل وتكون علة له بلا تخلف
القدرة بمعنى سلامة الأسباب والآلات (al-qudra bi-ma‘nā salāmat al-asbāb wa’l-ālāt): الاستطاعة التي تتقدم على الفعل وتكون شرطاً لوجوب الأداء
القدرة المطلقة (al-qudra al-muṭlaqa): أدنى ما يتمكن به العبد من أداء المأمور به، وهي غير مقيدة باليسر والسهولة
القدرة الكاملة (al-qudra al-kāmila): القدرة التي تتضمن اليسر والسهولة، زائدة على المطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Absolute capability is the minimum threshold for obligation; complete capability is additional and not required.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Condition of Capacity and Presumption of Time Extension
Expanding the rule of capacity with istihsan dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul concept of presumed capacity (توهم الوجود) as a condition for obligation, distinguish between capacity for action and capacity for consequence, and apply the istihsan-based principle to cases where one becomes mukallaf at the end of prayer time.

Core Idea
Presumed capacity, not actual, suffices for obligation – time may extend by miracle, making prayer wajib.

This passage from the usul text delves into a critical Hanafi principle: capacity (qudra) is a condition for demanding an action, but that capacity need not be actual; presumption of possibility suffices. The author uses the example of a person who becomes mukallaf at the very end of prayer time, and the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Zufar over whether prayer is obligatory. By understanding this, you will see how Hanafi usul employs istihsan and miraculous evidence to ground obligation where strict qiyas would not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of required (matlub)
The passage distinguishes between matlub al-fi'l (action demanded) and matlub al-wasiyya wal-ithm (bequeathing fidya and sin). Capacity is a condition only for the former.
This distinction is key: one can be obligated to arrange for fidya even without capacity to perform the prayer itself.
2
Recognize the condition of presumed existence
The condition for performance is not actual capacity (hagīqī) but presumed capacity (mutawahham al-wujūd). The author argues it suffices that the time could plausibly be extended.
The basis is that real capacity accompanies the action, not precedes it.
3
Examine the specific case
Consider a child who reaches puberty, a disbeliever who accepts Islam, or a menstruating woman who becomes pure at the very end of prayer time – when only enough time for takbīr remains. According to Abu Hanifa, prayer becomes obligatory due to the presumption of time extension (istihsan).
Zufar opposed this by qiyas, arguing actual capacity is lacking and the possibility is too remote.
4
Analyze the evidence from miracles
The passage cites the miracles of Prophet Sulayman (the sun returned so he could pray Asr) and Prophet Yusha (the sun held back for battle) to prove that time extension is possible. This supports the presumption.
These miracles are considered established (qat'ī?) and thus grounds for istihsan.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If time actually extends, the prayer is performed as ada; otherwise, it must be made up (qada). The sin attaches to abandoning qada, not the original performance. Also, later scholars disagreed about the menstruating woman's obligation.
The ruling differs between Abu Hanifa and Zufar: one makes prayer wajib, the other not.

حتى إذا بلغ الصبي، أو أسلم الكافر، أو طهرت الحائض في آخر الوقت لزمته الصلاة لتوهم الامتداد في آخر الوقت بوقف الشمس،

(السنبلي) والشرط: أي شرط وجوب الأداء.(القمر) بل يكفي وهمه إلخ لأن القدرة التي يبني عليها التكليف حقيقة أي متحققة لا تسبق الفعل لما عرف في مسألة من أن حقيقتها تكون مع الفعل لا قبله فتدبر (السنبلي) لزمته الصلاة وهذا عند الإمام الأعظم ه استحسانًا، وخالف فيه زفر وهو القياس يقول: إن القدرة على الأداء منعدمة حقيقة، ولا وجه لاعتبار احتمال حدوث القدرة بامتداد الوقت؛ لأن هذا الاحتمال بعيد لا يصلح أن يكون مدادًا للتكليف وسبب وجوب الصلاة الوقت الذي الصلاة لا أيّ وقت كان ولو كان قليلا فحينئذٍ لا يجب الأداء، فلا يجب القضاء؛ لأنه خلف عنه. (القمر) لتوهم الامتداد أي على وجه الكرامة، وثبوت الكرامة للبشر قطعي كذا قيل. (القمر)

بيان تقسيم القدرة والمراد بآخر الوقت الذي لا يسع فيه إلا مقدار التحريمة، فإذا حدثت هذه الموجبات في هذا الوقت لزمته الصلاة لاحتمال امتداده بوقف الشمس، فإن امتد في الواقع يؤديه فيه، وإلا يقضيها، وهذا الوقف أمر ممكن خارق للعادة كما كان لسليمان عليها حيث عرضت عليه بالعشي الصافنات الجياد، فكادت الشمس تغرب فضرب سوقها وأعناقها، فرد الله الشمس

(القمر) حيث عرضت عليه إلخ قال مقاتل ورث سليمان من أبيه داود ألف فرس فصلى سليمان عليه صلاة الظهر وقعد على كرسيه والأفراس تعرض عليه فعرضت عليه تسع مائة، فتنبه لصلاة العصر وكادت الشمس تغرب، وتوارى أكثرها كذا قيل وفاتته الصلاة فاغتم لذلك ، وقال: ردّوا الأفراس عليّ فردّوها عليه، فضرب أي قطع سوق الأفراس وأعناقها بالسيف طلبًا لمرضاة الله وتقرّبا إليه تعالى وقهراً للنفس عن حظوظها، فلما عقر الخيل سخر له الريح مكان الخيل تجري بأمره كيف يشاء. والعشي آخر النهار كذا في "القاموس"، والصافنات: هي الخيل القائمة على ثلاث قوائم وأقامت واحدة على طرف الحافر من يد أو رجل، والجياد المختار السراع كذا قال البغوي في "المعالم"، والسوق بالضم جمع الساق والأعناق جمع العنق. (القمر) وقد كان ليوشع إلخ قاتل يوشع بن نون يوم الجمعة الجبارين، وكادت الشمس تغرب، فقال للشمس: إنك مأمورة بالغروب وأنا مأمور بالقتال قبل الغروب، فإن القتال في يوم السبت وليله كان محرما فدعا، فقال: اللهم احبس الشمس علينا، فحبست حتى فتح عليه كذا روى البخاري عن أبي هريرة . (القمر)
أن رد الشمس غير وقفها، والكلام
Section on the Specific. Explanation of the division of capacity. But if the required is the action, and if the required is compensation and sin, then that condition is not required. For one who owes a thousand prayers, it is said to him in the last breath: This prayer is obligatory upon you, and its effect appears in the obligation of bequeathing fidya and sin. And the condition is its presumption, not its reality – meaning the condition among this minimal possible capacity is that it is presumed to exist, not that it actually exists. That is, it is not necessary that the time which accommodates four rak'ats actually exists at the moment; rather its presumption suffices. If this presumed thing is realized externally, for instance by the time extending from Allah's side, he performs it in it; otherwise its effect appears in making up (qada). So if a boy reaches puberty, or a disbeliever accepts Islam, or a menstruating woman becomes pure at the end of the time, prayer becomes obligatory upon him/her due to the presumption of extension at the end of time by the stopping of the sun. (Commentary: The clarification is that possible capacity is a condition for qada if the action is required, i.e., performing the missed prayer, because demanding an action without capacity is not permissible. But if the required is bequeathing fidya for the heir to ransom after his death, and sin if he abandons the bequest of fidya, then that possible capacity is not required. For one who owes a thousand prayers, it is said to him in the last breath: This prayer is obligatory upon you even though he is not able to perform at this time, so the effect of this obligation is not performance, rather bequeathing fidya and sin for not bequeathing. (Bahr al-Ulum) (Qamar) 'the required action' etc. Now, demanding action without capacity is not permissible. For example, if prayer becomes obligatory in health while standing, he makes it up in illness while sitting; if it becomes obligatory in illness while lying down, he makes it up in health while standing, not lying down. Thus it is known that capacity is required at the time when action is demanded; otherwise the ruling would be opposite. (Sunbuliy) And the condition: i.e., condition of obligation of performance. (Qamar) 'Rather its presumption suffices' etc., because the capacity upon which taklif is built is real, i.e., actual, it does not precede the action, as known in the issue that its reality is with the action, not before it, so reflect. (Sunbuliy) prayer becomes obligatory upon him, and this according to Imam al-A'zam Abu Hanifa – may Allah have mercy on him – as istihsan, and Zufar opposed him, and it is qiyas: he says that capacity for performance is actually nonexistent, and there is no basis for considering the possibility of capacity arising by extension of time, because this possibility is remote and does not qualify as a basis for taklif. And the cause of prayer's obligation is time, not any time, even if little; then performance is not obligatory, so qada is not obligatory because it is its substitute. (Qamar) 'due to presumption of extension' i.e., in the manner of a miracle, and the proof of miracles for humans is certain – thus it is said. (Qamar) Capacity. Accommodates. And the intended meaning by the end of time is that which does not accommodate except the amount of takbir tahrima. When these causes occur in this time, prayer becomes obligatory upon him due to the possibility of its extension by the stopping of the sun. If it actually extends, he performs it in it; otherwise he makes it up. And this stopping is a possible event that breaks the norm, as was for Sulayman – peace be upon him – when the swift, refined horses were presented to him in the afternoon, and the sun was about to set, so he struck their legs and necks, and Allah returned the sun until he prayed Asr, and subjected the wind for him in place of horses, and this is by the text of the Quran. And it was for Yusha – peace be upon him – (Surah Sad). And the intended meaning by 'the end of time which does not accommodate except the amount of takbir' is not that, because the possibility of extension does not require stipulating from time that which accommodates takbir. Rather the intended meaning by the end of time is the indivisible part of time such that it cannot accommodate even a letter. And one could say that the commentator's intended meaning is that which does not accommodate except the amount of takbir, even by possibility of extension, so reflect. (Qamar) 'these causes' i.e., reaching puberty of boy, Islam of disbeliever, purity of menstruating woman. Then know that the author of al-Kashf stated that if a menstruating woman becomes pure at a time that does not accommodate takbir, prayer is obligatory upon her, but it was commented upon in Mishkat al-Anwar where he said: The truth is its invalidity as in al-Khulasa and Fath al-Qadir from the book of menstruation, and they agreed that if she becomes pure and there remains what does not accommodate takbir, qada is not required. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The ruling of a junub disbeliever if he accepts Islam in the time is like the menstruating woman, and it is considered in both that they catch the takbir. (Qamar) 'otherwise he makes it up' etc., if he catches the time of qada and does not make it up, he sins the sin of abandoning qada, not the sin of abandoning performance. (Qamar) 'when [the horses] were presented to him' etc. Muqatil said: Sulayman inherited from his father Dawud a thousand horses, so Sulayman – peace be upon him – prayed Zuhr and sat on his throne, and the horses were presented to him, and nine hundred were presented to him. Then he became alert for Asr prayer, and the sun was about to set and most of it had disappeared – thus it is said – and he missed the prayer and was distressed. So he said: Bring back the horses to me, and they returned them to him. He struck – i.e., cut – the legs and necks of the horses with the sword, seeking Allah's pleasure and drawing near to Him and subduing the soul from its desires. When he disabled the horses, Allah subjected the wind to him in place of the horses, running by his command wherever he wished. And 'al-'ashi' is the end of the day, as in al-Qamus. 'al-safinat' are horses standing on three legs and the fourth raised on the tip of the hoof from hand or foot. 'al-jiyad' are chosen swift ones – al-Baghawi said in al-Ma'alim. 'al-suq' (pl. of saq) and 'al-a'naq' (pl. of 'unuq). (Qamar) 'Allah returned' etc., i.e., due to his supplication – thus narrated from Ali. And here there is discussion: it is about stopping the sun, not returning it, so the mention of the story of Sulayman here is not appropriate – reflect. (Qamar) 'And it was for Yusha' etc. Yusha ibn Nun fought the giants on a Friday, and the sun was about to set, so he said to the sun: You are commanded to set, and I am commanded to fight before sunset, because fighting on Saturday and its night was prohibited. He made supplication, saying: O Allah, hold back the sun for us, so it was held back until conquest was granted – thus reported by Bukhari from Abu Hurayra. (Qamar) That returning the sun is not its stopping, and the discussion.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an advanced Hanafi usul discussion on the concept of capacity (qudra) as a condition for obligation (taklif). The author distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) when the action itself is demanded (e.g., performing a missed prayer), where capacity is a necessary condition; and (2) when only the consequence (like bequeathing fidya or incurring sin) is at stake, where capacity is not required. A key point is that the capacity required is not actualized capacity at the moment of obligation, but merely a presumed capacity (توهم الوجود). For example, if a child reaches puberty at the very end of prayer time (when only the takbir can be said), prayer becomes obligatory due to the possibility that the time might miraculously extend. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa (istihsan). His disciple Zufar opposed using qiyas, arguing that actual capacity is lacking and the possibility is too remote. The author supports Abu Hanifa by citing miracles: Prophet Sulayman's horses distracted him until the sun was about to set, so Allah stopped the sun until he prayed Asr; similarly, Prophet Yusha asked Allah to stop the sun on a Friday to complete battle. These prove that time extension is possible, thus the presumption suffices for obligation. The ruling applies to the one who becomes mukallaf (through puberty, Islam, or menses ending) when only the tahrima is possible. A later discussion notes that some scholars, like the author of al-Kashf, held that a menstruating woman must pray if she becomes pure at such a time, but others (e.g., in al-Khulasa and Fath al-Qadir) disagree, stating that if less than a takbir remains, no prayer is obligatory—nor qada. The passage emphasizes that the obligation here is for performance (ada) if extension actually occurs; otherwise, qada becomes obligatory, and sin attaches to abandoning qada, not original performance.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): Capacity or ability to perform an action; a condition for taklif when action is required, but can be presumed (موهومة) rather than actual.
توهم الامتداد (tawahhum al-imtidad): The presumption that the prayer time might extend miraculously, making it possible to perform the prayer even if initially insufficient time remains.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas for a stronger reason, here considering the possibility of miraculous time extension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a disbeliever accepts Islam at the very end of Asr time, when only enough time for takbir remains, what is the ruling?
A) Prayer is not obligatory because actual capacity is lacking.
B) Prayer is obligatory due to the presumption of time extension (istihsan).
C) Prayer is obligatory only if he actually catches the full prayer.
D) He must make up the prayer later (qada) but no sin for delay.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, presumed capacity (tawahhum al-imtidad) suffices as a condition for obligation when action is required, based on the possibility of miraculous time extension, as established by istihsan over strict qiyas.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Obligation at the Last Moment of Prayer Time with Possible Extension
Establishes obligation if takbirat al-ihram possible, using divine time extension proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the minimum capacity for obligation is the takbirat al-ihram and evaluate the role of miraculous time extension in establishing obligation.

Core Idea
If only the opening takbir fits, prayer is obligatory due to possible extension; but if even that doesn't fit, no obligation.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar examines the boundary of prayer obligation when someone becomes responsible at the very end of the prayer time. It uses miraculous stories to argue that time can be extended, but ultimately the Hanafi position limits obligation to the capacity for at least the opening takbir. Understanding this usul derivation helps distinguish between hypothetical possibility and legal obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the condition for prayer obligation when one becomes mukallaf at the end of time? The passage defines 'akhir al-waqt' as the moment that can only accommodate the opening takbir (tahrimah).
Tahrimah is the minimum act to 'catch' the time.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author uses stories of Solomon (Quran) and Joshua (hadith) to show that time can be extended by divine miracle. This establishes the possibility of extension.
These are dalil naqli for the possibility, not for the obligation itself.
3
Analyse the proof's legal force
How does a miraculous possibility establish obligation? The author argues that if the takbir fits, the possibility of extension makes the prayer obligatory now; if time actually extends, it is performed; otherwise it is made up.
But note: the possibility alone is not enough to impose obligation when capacity is absent.
4
Identify the furu' dispute
The passage discusses an intra-Hanafi difference: author of al-Kashf held that a menstruating woman who becomes pure at a time not even accommodating takbir must pray due to possible extension; later scholars rejected this.
The text sides with later consensus: no obligation or qada'.
5
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that obligation requires actual capacity to perform the opening takbir. If that capacity is absent, no prayer is required, even if a miracle could extend time.
This shows the limit of relying on khawariq al-'adat in legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان تقسيم القدرة والمراد بآخر الوقت الذي لا يسع فيه إلا مقدار التحريمة، فإذا حدثت هذه الموجبات في هذا الوقت لزمته الصلاة لاحتمال امتداده بوقف الشمس، فإن امتد في الواقع يؤديه فيه، وإلا يقضيها، وهذا الوقف أمر ممكن خارق للعادة كما كان لسليمان عليه حيث عرضت عليه بالعشي الصافنات الجياد، فكادت الشمس تغرب فضرب سوقها وأعناقها، فرد الله الشمس حتى صلى العصر، وسخر له الريح مكان الخيل، وهذا بنص القرآن، وقد كان ليوشع عليه قاتل يوشع بن نون يوم الجمعة الجبارين، وكادت الشمس تغرب، فقال للشمس: إنك مأمورة بالغروب وأنا مأمور بالقتال قبل الغروب، فإن القتال في يوم السبت وليله كان محرما فدعا، فقال: اللهم احبس الشمس علينا، فحبست حتى فتح عليه كذا روى البخاري عن أبي هريرة. واعلم أنه صرح صاحب 'الكشف' بأن الحائض إذا طهرت في وقت لا يسع التحريمة وجبت عليها الصلاة، وتعقبه في 'مشكاة الأنوار' حيث قال: والحق بطلانه كما في 'الخلاصة' و'فتح القدير' من كتاب الحيض، وأجمعوا على أنها لو طهرت وقد بقي ما لا يسع التحريمة لا يلزمها القضاء وفي 'السراج الوهاج': وحكم الكافر الجنب إذا أسلم في الوقت كالحائض ويعتبر فيهما أن يدركا التحريمة.
Explanation of the division of capacity and the meaning of the end of time which cannot accommodate except the measure of the opening takbir. When these obligating causes occur in this time, prayer becomes obligatory upon him due to the possibility of its extension by stopping the sun. If it actually extends, he performs it in it; otherwise he makes it up. And this stopping is a possible thing contrary to habit, as was for Solomon (peace be upon him) when the swift horses were presented to him in the evening, and the sun was about to set, so he struck their legs and necks, and God returned the sun until he prayed Asr, and subjected the wind for him instead of the horses. This is by the text of the Quran. And for Joshua (peace be upon him), he fought the giants on Friday, and the sun was about to set, so he said to the sun: You are commanded to set and I am commanded to fight before sunset, because fighting on Saturday and its night was prohibited, so he supplicated: O God, withhold the sun from us, so it was withheld until he conquered. Thus narrated Bukhari from Abu Huraira. And know that the author of 'al-Kashf' stated that if a menstruating woman becomes pure at a time that cannot accommodate the opening takbir, prayer is obligatory upon her. He was criticized in 'Mishkat al-Anwar' saying: The truth is its invalidity as in 'al-Khulasa' and 'Fath al-Qadir' from the book of menstruation. And they agreed that if she becomes pure and there remains what cannot accommodate the opening takbir, she is not obliged to make it up. And in 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj': The ruling of the disbeliever in janaba, if he accepts Islam in the time, is like the menstruating woman, and in both cases it is considered that they should catch the opening takbir.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling concerning the obligation of prayer for those who become legally responsible (mukallaf) at the very end of the prayer time. The author clarifies that the 'end of time' means the final moment that can only accommodate the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). If a person reaches puberty, a disbeliever accepts Islam, or a menstruating woman becomes pure exactly at that moment, the prayer becomes obligatory because of the possibility that the time may extend through a divine miracle like the sun being stopped. The author then proves the possibility of time extension through two prophetic stories: Solomon (peace be upon him) who was so engrossed in reviewing horses that the Asr time was about to end; when the sun was setting, he struck the horses to express regret, and God returned the sun so he could pray Asr. The second story is of Joshua (son of Nun) who was fighting on Friday; when the sun was about to set and fighting was prohibited on Saturday, he asked God to hold the sun, and it was held until he conquered. Both miracles are established by Quran and hadith. The passage then addresses a furu' ruling: If a menstruating woman becomes pure at a time that cannot accommodate even the takbir, the stronger Hanafi view (as in al-Khulasa and Fath al-Qadir) is that she is not obligated to pray that prayer or make it up. The same applies to a disbeliever in janabah who accepts Islam at such a moment. This shows that the condition for obligation is the capacity to perform at least the opening part of the prayer, and divine extension is only a hypothetical basis for obligation, not an actual cause for making up.

Key Terms
آخر الوقت (akhir al-waqt): The final part of the prayer time that can only accommodate the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram).
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer (Allahu Akbar) which begins the prayer; here, the minimum act that makes one a performer of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, if a menstruating woman becomes pure (tahir) at the very end of Asr time such that only the opening takbir can be performed, what is the ruling on that Asr prayer?
A) She must pray Asr immediately and if time runs out she makes it up.
B) She is not obligated to pray Asr nor make it up.
C) She must pray Asr but there is no qada' if missed.
D) She must make up Asr later but not pray it now.

Key Takeaway
The condition for prayer obligation at the end of time is the capacity to perform the opening takbir; miraculous time extension does not create obligation where capacity is absent.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Facilitated Capacity (al-Qudra al-Muyassara) in Hanafi Usul
Analyzing the types of capacity for worship obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between facilitated capacity and possible capacity, and explain why presumption (tawahhum) is considered for prayer but not for Hajj.

Core Idea
Facilitated capacity means the obligation was set with ease, not that it became easy later.

This passage from Noor al-Anwaar examines a key distinction in Hanafi usul: the type of capacity required for obligations. The authors discuss an objection regarding Hajj—why is presumption of ability considered for prayer but not for Hajj? The answer reveals the concept of facilitated capacity. Understanding this is crucial for determining when obligations become binding and when they fall away.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of capacity
Distinguish between 'facilitated capacity' (muyassara) and 'possible capacity' (mumkina). Note their definitions.
Facilitated capacity makes performance easy; possible capacity is merely possible.
2
Analyze the objection regarding Hajj
Understand why presumption (tawahhum) of provisions is considered for prayer but not for Hajj. The text rejects the qiyas.
Prayer has a substitute (qada); Hajj does not, and considering presumption would cause hardship.
3
Examine the concept of 'tawahhum' (presumption)
Learn when presumption is valid (when there is a fruit like qada) vs when it causes hardship.
Hardship (haraj) removes the consideration of presumption.
4
Apply the principle to financial and bodily acts
Facilitated capacity is a condition for most financial acts (like zakat). Continuity of this capacity is required for the obligation to persist.
If capacity ends (e.g., wealth destroyed), the obligation falls.
5
Recognize the exception
Some financial acts, like sadaqat al-fitr, are based on possible capacity, not facilitated.
This shows the text's precision: 'most' not 'all'.

Source Text

۱۳۸
بيان تقسيم القدرة حتى فتح القدس قبل دخول ليلة السبت، وقد كان لنبينا عليه حين فاتت صلاة العصر من علي كما ذكر في كتاب السير، وهذا بخلاف الحج، فإنه لم يعتبر فيه توهم الزاد والراحلة مع أن أكثر الناس يحجون بلا زاد وراحلة؛ لأن في اعتبار ذلك حرجًا عظيمًا، ولو اعتبر ذلك لا تظهر ثمرته في وجوب القضاء؛ لأن الحج لا يقضى، وإنما تظهر في حق الإثم والإيصاء وذلك غير معقول.
ويسمى
أي القسم الثاني
وكامل وهو : القدرة الميسرة للأداء عطف على قوله : مطلق، وهذا هو القسم الثاني، هذا ميسرة؛ لأنه جعل الأداء يسيرًا سهلاً على المكلف لا بمعنى أنه قد كان قبل ذلك عسيراً، ثم يسره الله بعد ذلك، بل بمعنى أنه أوجب من الابتداء بطريق اليسر والسهولة كما يقال: "ضيق فم الركية" أي اجعله ضيقًا من الابتداء لا أنه كان واسعا، ثم يضيقه،
أن
أهلاً
وهذا بخلاف إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أن الزاد والراحلة قدرة ممكنة للحج والشرط في القدرة الممكنة توهمه، فينبغي يعتبر توهم الزاد والراحلة في وجوب الحج كما اعتبر توهم القدرة في وجوب الصلاة في حق من صار في آخر الوقت مع أن الحج بدون الزاد والراحلة كثير، وأداء الصلاة في آخر جزء من أجزاء الوقت بامتداد الوقت نادر جدا، وحاصل الدفع أن هذا أي اعتبار التوهم بخلاف الحج فإن في اعتبار ذلك أي توهم الزاد والراحلة في وجوب الحج حرجًا عظيمًا، واعتبار التوهم في وجوب الصلاة لأجل الخلف وهو القضاء، ولو اعتبر ذلك أي التوهم في وجوب الحج لا تظهر ثمرة الوجوب؛ لأن الحج لا يقضى، وإنما تظهر في حق وجوب الإيصاء عند الموت والإثم عند عدم الإيصاء، وهذا غير معقول تدبر . (القمر) عسيراً : أي واجبًا بصفة العسرة بالقدرة الممكنة. (القمر) أوجب إلخ ولو كان واجبًا بالقدرة الممكنة لكان عسيرا، فلما توقف الوجوب على القدرة الميسرة دون الممكنة صار كأن الواجب تغير من العسر إلى اليسر بواسطة هذه القدرة الميسرة فصارت مغيرة. (القمر)
أخرجه الهيثمي في مجمع الزوائد عن أسماء بنت عميس قالت: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا نزل عليه الوحي يكاد يغشى عليه ، فأنزل عليه يوما وهو في حجر علي، فقال له رسول الله صليت العصر، قال: لا يا رسول الله، فدعا الله فرد عليه الشمس حتى صلى العصر ، قالت فرأيت الشمس طلعت بعد ما غابت حين ردت حتى صلى العصر، رواه الطبراني بأسانيد، ورجال أحدها رجال الصحيح عن إبراهيم بن حسن وهو ثقة، وثقه ابن حبان. ۲۹۷/۸، باب حبس الشمس له رسول الله .

مبحث الخاص
۱۳۹
بيان تقسيم القدرة
وهذه القدرة شرط في أكثر العبادات المالية دون البدنية.
أي الميسرة
ودوام هذه القدرة شرط لدوام الواجب أي ما دامت هذه القدرة باقية يبقى الواجب، وإذا انتفى القدرة انتفى الواجب؛ لأن الواجب كان ثابتا باليسر، فإن بقي بدون القدرة يتبدل اليسر إلى العسر الصرف.
حتى تبطل الزكاة والعشر والخراج بهلاك المال تفريع على قوله: ودوام هذه القدرة يعني أن
أي النصاب والخارج
الزكاة كانت واجبة بالقدرة الميسرة؛ لأن التمكن فيه يثبت بملك أصل المال، فإذا اشترط
أي القدرة الممكنة
النصاب الحولي عُلم أن فيه قدرةً ميسرة فإذا هلك النصاب بعد تمام الحول سقطت الزكاة؛
من
أكثر العبادات المالية كالزكاة والعشر، فإن العبادات المالية هي التي أداؤها أشق على النفس عند العامة البدنية؛ لأن المال محبوب النفس، وإنما قال أكثر ؛ لأن بعض العبادات المالية كصدقة الفطر تثبت بالقدرة الممكنة على ما سيجيء. (القمر) يتبدل اليسر إلى العسر : ليس المراد أن نفس اليسر يصير عسرا، فإنه محال، بل المراد أن الواجب كان واجبًا بطريق اليسر والسهولة، فلو أو جبناه على تقدير عدم بقاء القدرة لوجب بطريق الغرامة والعسر، فيتبدل اليسير إلى العسير. (القمر)
أصل المال المراد منه النصاب الفارغ عن الحاجة الأصلية والدين، أو تلك النصاب الكذائي قدرة ممكنة لا ملك أي قدر كان من المال، فإن المال المشغول بالحاجة منعدم شرعًا وعرفًا، فإذا اشترط في نصاب الزكاة النماء كان هذا يسيرًا، وإليه أشار الشارح بقوله: فإذا اشترط النصاب الحولي إلخ فإنه أقيم حولان الحول مقام النماء الحقيقي، لأن الحول ممكن من الاستمناء، لاشتماله على الفصول المختلفة التي يختلف فيها الأسعار غالبًا بحسب العادة وفي اعتبار حقيقة النماء ضرب حرج، وكون الواجب مرة واحدة بعد حولان الحول يسر آخر، وكونه الكثير يسر آخر، فعلم أن المعتبر في وجوب الزكاة قدرة ميسرة. (القمر) من
شيئًا قليلا
بعد تمام الحول إنما قيد به؛ لأنه لو هلك النصاب قبل الحول فلا زكاة بالاتفاق . (القمر) سقطت الزكاة فيه أن هذا يؤدي إلى تفويت أداء الزكاة، فإن تأخير الأداء جائز إلى آخر العمر، وهلاك النصاب في هذه المدة غير نادر وبعد الهلاك سقط الوجوب ويمكن أن يقال: إنا نلتزم الفوات في صورة هلاك المال، ولا محذور في ذلك؛ لأنه ما فوت بهذا التأخير على أحد ملكًا ولا يدًا، وللمناقش أن يناقش بأنه لا يلزم من اعتبار اليسر في وجوب الزكاة بالوجوه المذكورة اعتبار يسر أخر ما نص الشارع عليه، وهو سقوط الزكاة بهلاك النصاب بعد حولان الحول فتدبر . (القمر)
Section on Specificity. * 138 Explanation of the division of capacity until the conquest of Jerusalem before the entry of Saturday night. Our Prophet (peace be upon him) had missed the afternoon prayer of Ali as mentioned in the book of Siyar. This is unlike Hajj, for presumption of provisions and mount is not considered in it, even though most people perform Hajj without provisions and mount; because considering that would cause great hardship. And if it were considered, its fruit would not appear in the obligation of make-up because Hajj is not made up; rather it appears regarding sin and bequest, and that is not reasonable. And it is called—i.e., the second type—and complete: it is the capacity facilitated for performance, an apposition to his saying: absolute. This is the second type, this is facilitated because it makes performance easy and simple for the obligated person; not in the sense that before it was difficult then God made it easy afterward, but in the sense that He obligated from the beginning in a way of ease and facility, as it is said: 'Make narrow the mouth of the well,' i.e., make it narrow from the beginning, not that it was wide and then you narrow it. That 'And this is unlike...' etc.: a rebuttal of an estimated objection. Its gist is that provisions and mount are possible capacity for Hajj, and the condition for possible capacity is its presumption, so presumption of provisions and mount should be considered in the obligation of Hajj just as presumption of capacity was considered in the obligation of prayer for one who ends up at the end of the time, even though Hajj without provisions and mount is frequent, and performing prayer in the last part of the time with the extension of time is very rare. The gist of the rebuttal is that this, i.e., considering presumption, is unlike Hajj, for considering that, i.e., presumption of provisions and mount, in the obligation of Hajj would be great hardship, and considering presumption in the obligation of prayer is for the substitute which is make-up. And if that, i.e., presumption, were considered in Hajj, no fruit of obligation would appear because Hajj is not made up; rather it appears regarding the obligation of bequest at death and sin upon non-bequest, and this is inconceivable. Ponder. (al-Qamar) 'Difficult': i.e., obligatory with the quality of difficulty by possible capacity. (al-Qamar) 'Obligated... etc.': And if it were obligatory by possible capacity, it would be difficult; so when obligation depended on facilitated capacity rather than possible, it became as if the obligatory changed from difficulty to ease through this facilitated capacity, so it became transformative. (al-Qamar) Al-Haythami narrated it in Majma' al-Zawa'id from Asma bint Umays: she said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would almost faint when revelation descended upon him. One day revelation came while he was in the lap of Ali. The Messenger said to him: 'Did you pray Asr?' He said: 'No, O Messenger of Allah.' So he supplicated Allah and the sun was returned for him until he prayed Asr.' She said: 'I saw the sun rise after it had set when it was returned until he prayed Asr.' Narrated by al-Tabarani with chains, and one of its chains are the men of Sahih from Ibrahim ibn Hasan, who is trustworthy, authenticated by Ibn Hibban. 297/8, Chapter on the detention of the sun for the Messenger of Allah. [PAGE_140] Section on Specificity. 139 Explanation of the division of capacity. And this capacity is a condition in most financial acts of worship, not bodily ones. —i.e., the facilitated one. And the continuity of this capacity is a condition for the continuity of the obligation, i.e., as long as this capacity remains, the obligation remains; and if capacity is removed, the obligation is removed, because the obligation was established by ease. If it remains without capacity, ease turns into pure difficulty. So that zakat, tithe, and land tax are nullified by the destruction of wealth, a branch on his saying: And the continuity of this capacity. Means that —i.e., nisab and output — zakat was obligatory by facilitated capacity, because ability in it is established by ownership of the original capital. So when the annual nisab was stipulated —i.e., possible capacity — it was known that there is facilitated capacity in it. So if the nisab perishes after the completion of the year, zakat falls. From 'most financial acts of worship' like zakat and tithe, for financial acts of worship are more difficult for the soul according to common people than bodily ones, because wealth is beloved to the soul. He only said 'most' because some financial acts of worship like sadaqat al-fitr are established by possible capacity, as will come. (al-Qamar) 'Ease turns into difficulty': It is not meant that ease itself becomes difficulty, for that is impossible; rather the meaning is that the obligatory was obligatory by way of ease and facility. If we were to obligate it on the assumption that capacity does not remain, it would be obligatory by way of indemnity and difficulty, so the easy would turn into the difficult. (al-Qamar) The original capital means the nisab free from basic need and debt, or that nisab is such possible capacity, not ownership of any amount of wealth. For wealth occupied by need is non-existent legally and customarily. So when growth was stipulated in the nisab of zakat, this was ease. And the commentator pointed to this by his saying: 'So when the annual nisab was stipulated, etc.', for he substituted the passing of the year for real growth, because the year is a substitute for profit, due to its inclusion of different seasons in which prices often vary according to custom. And considering real growth would involve great hardship. And the obligation being once after the passing of the year is another ease, and its being little is another ease. So it is known that what is considered in the obligation of zakat is facilitated capacity. (al-Qamar) From 'a little thing' after the completion of the year was only restricted by that, because if the nisab perishes before the year, there is no zakat by agreement. (al-Qamar) 'Zakat fell' in that this leads to missing the payment of zakat, because delaying payment is permissible until the end of life, and destruction of the nisab in this period is not rare, and after destruction the obligation falls. And it can be said: We accept the loss in the case of destruction of wealth, and there is no harm in that, because by this delay one has not lost anyone's ownership or possession. And the objector may object that it does not follow from considering ease in the obligation of zakat by the mentioned aspects to consider another ease that the Lawgiver did not specify, which is the falling of zakat by destruction of nisab after the passing of the year. So ponder. (al-Qamar).
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of 'facilitated capacity' (al-qudra al-muyassara) and contrasts it with 'possible capacity' (al-qudra al-mumkina). It begins by addressing an objection: why is presumption (tawahhum) of provisions and mount not considered for Hajj, even though it is considered for the prayer of one who delays until the end of time? The answer is that considering presumption for Hajj would cause great hardship, and its fruit (obligation of make-up) does not apply because Hajj is not made up; the only fruits would be sin and bequest, which are not reasonable. The text then defines facilitated capacity: it is not that an obligation changed from difficult to easy, but that it was originally obligated in an easy manner. A hadith about the sun being returned for Ali is cited as an example of extraordinary facilitation. The passage then states that facilitated capacity is a condition for most financial acts of worship (like zakat), but not for bodily acts. The continuity of this capacity is also a condition for the continuity of the obligation: if the wealth perishes, the obligation falls. This is illustrated with zakat: it is a financial worship that requires facilitated capacity, so if the nisab is lost after the year, zakat is no longer due. The commentator notes exceptions like sadaqat al-fitr, which is based on possible capacity. The reasoning is that financial acts are harder on the soul, so facilitated capacity is needed. The passage ensures that the obligation remains easy, not burdensome.

Key Terms
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): The capacity that makes performance easy and facilitated, as opposed to merely possible capacity.
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): The capacity that is merely possible, not necessarily easy.
توهم (tawahhum): Presumption or assumption of the existence of capacity, even if not certain.
ثمرة الوجوب (thamarat al-wujub): The practical consequence or fruit of an obligation, such as the obligation of make-up (qada) or sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is presumption (tawahhum) of provisions and mount not considered for the obligation of Hajj, unlike prayer?
A) Because Hajj is not obligatory on the poor.
B) Because considering it would cause great hardship and the fruit of such presumption (make-up) does not apply to Hajj.
C) Because provisions and mount are not required for Hajj.
D) Because prayer is more important than Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Facilitated capacity is the basis for most financial obligations in the Hanafi school, ensuring obligations are easy to fulfill.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Division of Capacity: Facilitating vs. Possible
Statement of principle and its application to zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between facilitating capacity (qudra muyassara) and possible capacity (qudra mumkina) and explain why financial acts of worship require the former according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Financial ibadat require facilitating capacity; bodily ibadat need only possible capacity.

In this passage from a Hanafi usul commentary, the author explains a key distinction: the capacity (qudra) needed for financial acts of worship like zakat and ushr is of a higher order than that needed for bodily acts. The obligation of these acts is tied to ease (yusr) and normalcy. Let's unpack this principle and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of capacity
From the text, extract the definitions of qudra muyassara (facilitating capacity) and qudra mumkina (possible capacity). Note which one is required for most financial ibadat.
The text explicitly says 'these capacity is a condition in most financial acts of worship without the bodily ones' and glosses it as 'al-muyassara'.
2
Understand the rationale for ease
Why do financial acts require ease? Because wealth is dear to the soul, so requiring it under hardship would contradict the principle of yusr. The text mentions that if capacity ceases, obligation ceases, otherwise ease becomes hardship.
The gloss explains that the obligation was established by ease, so if it remained without capacity, it would become a penalty (ghurm).
3
Note the exception: sadaqat al-fitr
The author says 'most' financial ibadat require facilitating capacity; sadaqat al-fitr is an exception that is established by possible capacity. This shows the principle is not absolute.
The exception is mentioned briefly and will be elaborated later in the source.
4
Apply the principle to zakat
The text then applies this to zakat: the condition of nisab and the annual cycle (hawalan al-hawl) indicate that facilitating capacity is considered. Growth (nama') is effectively replaced by the passage of a year because considering real growth would be burdensome.
The passage uses qiyas: the annual cycle stands in for actual growth due to ease.

وكذا العشر كان واجبًا بالقدرة الميسرة؛ لأن الممكنة فيه كان بنفس الزراعة، فإذا شرط قيام
أي القدرة الممكنة
تسعة الأعشار عنده كان دليلاً على أنه يجب بطريق اليسر ، فإذا هلك الخارج كله أو بعضه
صاحب الأرض
بعد التمكن من التصدق تبطل العشر بحصته؛ لأنه اسم إضافي يقتضي وجود الحصص الباقية.
ما هلك الصغر
إذ لو بقيت أي الزكاة، وهذا يرشدك إلى أن المراد بالسقوط السقوط في الدارين كما اختاره في "مشكاة الأنوار"، وقال صاحب "التقرير ": إن السقوط بالهلاك إنما هو في أحكام الدنيا وأما في المؤاخذة فيأثم بعد التمكن. (القمر) إذ لو بقيت إلخ يعني لو بقيت مقدار الواجب المقدم، فإما أن يجب من حيث الزكاة وذا متعذر؛ لأنها كانت واجبة بالقدرة الميسرة، وقد فاتت فلو وجبت بدونها يلزم قلب الموضوع وعكس المشروع، وإما أن يجب من حيث الضمان والغرم وهذا أيضًا متعذر؛ لأن الضمان يستدعي سبق التعدي، وههنا لم يوجد التعدي و لم يتحقق صنع منه ، بل أخذه صاحب الحق بخلاف الاستهلاك لأنه يصنعه . (السنبلي)
لا تسقط أي الزكاة بهلاك النصاب بعد تمام الحول. (القمر) زجرًا له على التعدي: أي على حق الغير، وذا يوجب الغرم عليه، فالنصاب كأنه باق تقديرًا في حق صاحب الحق. (القمر)
:وهذا أي الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي . (القمر) تبقى أي الزكاة بقسط الباقي. (القمر) للغناء: أي ليصير المكلف به أهلاً للوجوب، فإن المطلوب من الزكاة إغناء الفقير والإغناء بصفة الحسن لا يتحقق من غير الغني كالتمليك لا يتحقق من غير المالك، وأحوال الناس متفاوتة في الغناء، فقدره الشارع بملك النصاب، فالنصاب كالقدرة الممكنة في العبادات البدنية. (القمر)
لا لليسر : إذ الواجب ربع العشر وأداء درهم من أربعين كأداء خمسة دراهم من مائتين في اليسر. (القمر) فإذا شرط إلخ : لأن العشر تعلق بحقيقة الخارج الذي هو نماء الأرض، وهو ما يحصل بالزراعة.(القمر)
The Section on the Specific
139
Statement of the Division of Capacity
And this capacity is a condition in most financial acts of worship without the bodily ones.
(i.e., the facilitating capacity)
And the continuity of this capacity is a condition for the continuity of the obligation, i.e., as long as this capacity remains, the obligation remains, and if capacity ceases, the obligation ceases; because the obligation was established by ease, and if it remains without capacity, ease would change into pure hardship.
So that zakat, ushr, and kharaj become void by destruction of the property, as a branch on his statement: 'And continuity of this capacity' means that
(i.e., the nisab and produce)
Zakat was obligatory by the facilitating capacity because capacity in it is established by ownership of the original asset, so when the annual nisab is stipulated, it is known that there is a facilitating capacity. So if the nisab is destroyed after the completion of the year, zakat falls.
From
most financial acts of worship like zakat and ushr, for financial acts of worship are those whose performance is harder on the soul in the common view than bodily ones, because wealth is beloved to the soul. He only said 'most' because some financial acts of worship like sadaqat al-fitr are established by possible capacity as will come. (Al-Qamar) 'Ease changes to hardship': it is not meant that ease itself becomes hardship, for that is impossible, but rather that the obligation was obligatory by way of ease and facility, so if we were to obligate it on the assumption that capacity does not remain, it would be obligatory by way of penalty and hardship, so the easy becomes difficult. (Al-Qamar)
'Original asset' means the nisab free from primary need and debt, or that nisab which is a possible capacity, not ownership of any amount of wealth, for wealth encumbered by need is non-existent legally and customarily. So when growth is stipulated in the nisab of zakat, this is ease. The commentator alluded to this by his saying: 'When the annual nisab is stipulated, etc.,' for he made the passing of the year take the place of real growth, because the year is possible for growth, containing different seasons in which prices usually vary, and considering real growth would be burdensome. And that the obligation is once after the passing of the year is another ease, and that it is little is another ease. So it is known that what is considered in the obligation of zakat is facilitating capacity. (Al-Qamar) From
something small
After the completion of the year, he only restricted it by that because if the nisab is destroyed before the year, there is no zakat by agreement. (Al-Qamar) 'Zakat fell' in this leads to missing the payment of zakat, for delaying payment is permissible until the end of life, and destruction of nisab in this period is not rare, and after destruction the obligation falls. It may be said: We accept the loss in the case of destruction of wealth, and there is no harm in that, because this delay did not take away anyone's ownership or possession. And the objector may object that considering ease in the obligation of zakat by the mentioned aspects does not require considering another ease beyond what the Lawgiver stipulated, which is the fall of zakat by destruction of nisab after the passing of the year, so reflect. (Al-Qamar)

141
The Section on the Specific
140
Statement of the Division of Capacity
For if it remained on him it would only be a penalty. According to al-Shafi'i: it does not fall because the obligation is established upon him by capacity, contrary to if he consumed it; for it remains upon him as a deterrent for his transgression. This is when the nisab is destroyed entirely; for if some of the nisab is destroyed, it (zakat) remains proportionally, because the condition of nisab initially was only for sufficiency, not for ease; for paying one dirham out of forty is like paying five dirhams out of two hundred in ease. So if sufficiency is found, then some is destroyed, ease remains in the remainder to its extent.
(i.e., in the remaining amount)
Similarly, ushr was obligatory by facilitating capacity, because the capacity in it was by farming itself. So when it is stipulated that nine-tenths remain with him, this is evidence that it is obligatory by way of ease. So if the produce, all or some, is destroyed after he is able to give in charity, the ushr becomes void proportionally, because it is a relative term requiring the existence of remaining shares.
(i.e., what is destroyed is small)
For if it (zakat) remained, etc. This indicates that what is meant by 'fall' is the fall in both realms, as chosen in 'Mishkat al-Anwar'. The author of 'al-Taqrir' said: The fall by destruction is only in worldly rulings, but regarding accountability in the afterlife, one sins after having the ability. (Al-Qamar) 'For if it remained, etc.' means if the amount of the obligation remained, then either it would be obligatory as zakat, which is impossible because it was obligatory by facilitating capacity and that capacity has now ceased, so if it were obligatory without it, it would invert the subject and reverse the legislation; or it would be obligatory as compensation and penalty, which is also impossible because compensation requires prior transgression, and here there is no transgression nor any act from him, rather the right-holder took it. (Al-Sanbali)
'It does not fall' means zakat by destruction of nisab after the completion of the year. (Al-Qamar) 'As a deterrent for his transgression' meaning against the right of another, and that obligates compensation upon him, so the nisab is as if it remains virtually in respect of the right-holder. (Al-Qamar)
'And this' means the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i. (Al-Qamar) 'It remains' means zakat according to the remaining portion. (Al-Qamar) 'For sufficiency' meaning to make the obligee fit for obligation, for the goal of zakat is to enrich the poor, and enrichment in a good manner is not realized except from the wealthy, just as giving ownership is not realized without the owner. And people's states vary in wealth, so the Lawgiver measured it by ownership of nisab. So the nisab is like possible capacity in bodily acts of worship. (Al-Qamar)
'Not for ease' for the obligation is one-fourth of a tenth, and paying one dirham out of forty is like paying five dirhams out of two hundred in ease. (Al-Qamar) 'When it is stipulated, etc.' because ushr is attached to the actual produce which is the growth of the land, which is obtained by farming. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the division of capacity (qudra) as a condition for acts of worship. It distinguishes between 'facilitating capacity' (qudra muyassara) and 'possible capacity' (qudra mumkina). The key principle is that in financial acts of worship like zakat and ushr, the required capacity is of the facilitating type, meaning that the obligation is contingent upon ease and normal circumstances. This is why if the nisab (minimum threshold) is destroyed after the year elapses, the obligation of zakat falls—because the facilitating capacity no longer exists. The author contrasts this with bodily acts of worship where possible capacity suffices. The passage then delves into the Hanafi position versus the Shafi'i position: Shafi'i holds that once the obligation is established by capacity at the end of the year, destruction does not remove it; rather, it becomes a debt. Hanafi responds that the obligation was conditioned on the continued existence of the property such that payment remains easy; if destroyed, obliging payment would be hardship. The text also covers the case of partial destruction of nisab or produce, where the obligation remains proportionally because the sufficiency for enrichment is still present. The commentary concludes with a note that the fall of obligation applies in this world but there may be sin in the hereafter if one had the ability to pay. Throughout, the reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference), showing the Hanafi method of considering ease and preventing hardship.

Key Terms
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): Facilitating capacity: the ability to perform an act with ease and without undue hardship.
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): Possible capacity: the mere ability to perform an act, even with difficulty.
النصاب الحولي (al-nisab al-hawli): The nisab that has been owned for a full lunar year, a condition for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is sadaqat al-fitr an exception to the rule that financial ibadat require facilitating capacity?
A) It is a bodily act of worship.
B) It is based on possible capacity according to the text.
C) It is not a financial act of worship.
D) It is obligatory only for the wealthy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions the obligation of most financial acts of worship on the presence of facilitating capacity, which must continue for the obligation to persist; if destroyed, the obligation falls.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Zakat After Nisab Destruction: The Hanafi-Stafi'i Dispute
Ruling on zakat after nisab destruction with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of facilitating capacity to the case of nisab destruction after the year, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zakat falls when nisab is destroyed after the year because the obligation was contingent on continued facilitation, not a fixed debt.

This passage delves into the specific ruling of zakat when the nisab is destroyed after the year elapses. It presents the Hanafi position that the obligation falls, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view that it remains as a debt. The Hanafi response relies on the principle of facilitating capacity and the fact that no transgression occurred.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi ruling
The text states that zakat falls (sāqitah) if the entire nisab is destroyed after the year. This is derived from the principle that the obligation was conditioned on facilitating capacity, which no longer exists.
The destruction must be after the year; before the year, there is no zakat by agreement.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat does not fall; it remains as a debt (dayn) because the obligation was confirmed at the end of the year when capacity existed. The destruction does not cancel the debt.
The text says 'و عند الشافعي لا تسقط' (according to al-Shafi'i, it does not fall).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that making it a debt would turn ease into hardship, and there was no transgression (ta'addi) on the part of the owner, unlike if he consumed the wealth.
The text contrasts destruction (halak) with consumption (istihlak): consumption involves a deliberate act, so it remains a debt as a deterrent.
4
Examine the partial destruction case
If only part of the nisab is destroyed, the obligation remains proportionally on the remaining part. This is because the condition of nisab initially was for sufficiency (ghina'), not ease. The ease of paying a small amount remains.
Paying 1 dirham from 40 is as easy as paying 5 from 200, so partial destruction does not break the ease entirely.

بيان تقسيم القدرة
وهذه القدرة شرط في أكثر العبادات المالية دون البدنية.
أي الميسرة
ودوام هذه القدرة شرط لدوام الواجب أي ما دامت هذه القدرة باقية يبقى الواجب، وإذا انتفى القدرة انتفى الواجب؛ لأن الواجب كان ثابتا باليسر، فإن بقي بدون القدرة يتبدل اليسر إلى العسر الصرف.
حتى تبطل الزكاة والعشر والخراج بهلاك المال تفريع على قوله: ودوام هذه القدرة يعني أن
أي النصاب والخارج
الزكاة كانت واجبة بالقدرة الميسرة؛ لأن التمكن فيه يثبت بملك أصل المال، فإذا اشترط
أي القدرة الممكنة
النصاب الحولي عُلم أن فيه قدرةً ميسرة فإذا هلك النصاب بعد تمام الحول سقطت الزكاة؛
من
أكثر العبادات المالية كالزكاة والعشر، فإن العبادات المالية هي التي أداؤها أشق على النفس عند العامة البدنية؛ لأن المال محبوب النفس، وإنما قال أكثر ؛ لأن بعض العبادات المالية كصدقة الفطر تثبت بالقدرة الممكنة على ما سيجيء. (القمر) يتبدل اليسر إلى العسر : ليس المراد أن نفس اليسر يصير عسرا، فإنه محال، بل المراد أن الواجب كان واجبًا بطريق اليسر والسهولة، فلو أو جبناه على تقدير عدم بقاء القدرة لوجب بطريق الغرامة والعسر، فيتبدل اليسير إلى العسير. (القمر)
أصل المال المراد منه النصاب الفارغ عن الحاجة الأصلية والدين، أو تلك النصاب الكذائي قدرة ممكنة لا ملك أي قدر كان من المال، فإن المال المشغول بالحاجة منعدم شرعًا وعرفًا، فإذا اشترط في نصاب الزكاة النماء كان هذا يسيرًا، وإليه أشار الشارح بقوله: فإذا اشترط النصاب الحولي إلخ فإنه أقيم حولان الحول مقام النماء الحقيقي، لأن الحول ممكن من الاستمناء، لاشتماله على الفصول المختلفة التي يختلف فيها الأسعار غالبًا بحسب العادة وفي اعتبار حقيقة النماء ضرب حرج، وكون الواجب مرة واحدة بعد حولان الحول يسر آخر، وكونه الكثير يسر آخر، فعلم أن المعتبر في وجوب الزكاة قدرة ميسرة. (القمر) من
شيئًا قليلا
بعد تمام الحول إنما قيد به؛ لأنه لو هلك النصاب قبل الحول فلا زكاة بالاتفاق . (القمر) سقطت الزكاة فيه أن هذا يؤدي إلى تفويت أداء الزكاة، فإن تأخير الأداء جائز إلى آخر العمر، وهلاك النصاب في هذه المدة غير نادر وبعد الهلاك سقط الوجوب ويمكن أن يقال: إنا نلتزم الفوات في صورة هلاك المال، ولا محذور في ذلك؛ لأنه ما فوت بهذا التأخير على أحد ملكًا ولا يدًا، وللمناقش أن يناقش بأنه لا يلزم من اعتبار اليسر في وجوب الزكاة بالوجوه المذكورة اعتبار يسر أخر ما نص الشارع عليه، وهو سقوط الزكاة بهلاك النصاب بعد حولان الحول فتدبر . (القمر)

For if it (zakat) remained, etc. This indicates that what is meant by 'fall' is the fall in both realms, as chosen in 'Mishkat al-Anwar'. The author of 'al-Taqrir' said: The fall by destruction is only in worldly rulings, but regarding accountability in the afterlife, one sins after having the ability. (Al-Qamar) 'For if it remained, etc.' means if the amount of the obligation remained, then either it would be obligatory as zakat, which is impossible because it was obligatory by facilitating capacity and that capacity has now ceased, so if it were obligatory without it, it would invert the subject and reverse the legislation; or it would be obligatory as compensation and penalty, which is also impossible because compensation requires prior transgression, and here there is no transgression nor any act from him, rather the right-holder took it. (Al-Sanbali)
'It does not fall' means zakat by destruction of nisab after the completion of the year. (Al-Qamar) 'As a deterrent for his transgression' meaning against the right of another, and that obligates compensation upon him, so the nisab is as if it remains virtually in respect of the right-holder. (Al-Qamar)
'And this' means the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i. (Al-Qamar) 'It remains' means zakat according to the remaining portion. (Al-Qamar) 'For sufficiency' meaning to make the obligee fit for obligation, for the goal of zakat is to enrich the poor, and enrichment in a good manner is not realized except from the wealthy, just as giving ownership is not realized without the owner. And people's states vary in wealth, so the Lawgiver measured it by ownership of nisab. So the nisab is like possible capacity in bodily acts of worship. (Al-Qamar)
'Not for ease' for the obligation is one-fourth of a tenth, and paying one dirham out of forty is like paying five dirhams out of two hundred in ease. (Al-Qamar) 'When it is stipulated, etc.' because ushr is attached to the actual produce which is the growth of the land, which is obtained by farming. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary explains the division of capacity (qudra) as a condition for acts of worship. It distinguishes between 'facilitating capacity' (qudra muyassara) and 'possible capacity' (qudra mumkina). The key principle is that in financial acts of worship like zakat and ushr, the required capacity is of the facilitating type, meaning that the obligation is contingent upon ease and normal circumstances. This is why if the nisab (minimum threshold) is destroyed after the year elapses, the obligation of zakat falls—because the facilitating capacity no longer exists. The author contrasts this with bodily acts of worship where possible capacity suffices. The passage then delves into the Hanafi position versus the Shafi'i position: Shafi'i holds that once the obligation is established by capacity at the end of the year, destruction does not remove it; rather, it becomes a debt. Hanafi responds that the obligation was conditioned on the continued existence of the property such that payment remains easy; if destroyed, obliging payment would be hardship. The text also covers the case of partial destruction of nisab or produce, where the obligation remains proportionally because the sufficiency for enrichment is still present. The commentary concludes with a note that the fall of obligation applies in this world but there may be sin in the hereafter if one had the ability to pay. Throughout, the reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference), showing the Hanafi method of considering ease and preventing hardship.

Key Terms
الغرم (al-ghurm): Penalty or compensation; in this context, if zakat remained after destruction, it would be a penalty rather than an act of worship.
التعدي (al-ta'addi): Transgression or wrongful act; here, destroying one's own wealth is transgression, whereas natural destruction is not.
الغناء (al-ghina'): Sufficiency or wealth that makes one eligible for obligation; the nisab condition is for sufficiency, not ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, what happens to zakat if only part of the nisab is destroyed after the year?
A) Zakat falls entirely.
B) Zakat remains proportionally on the remaining nisab.
C) Zakat becomes a debt that must be paid from other wealth.
D) Zakat is waived only if the owner did not intend to pay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that zakat falls upon total destruction of the nisab after the year due to loss of facilitating capacity; partial destruction leads to proportional obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Performance Establishes Permissibility: The Hanafi Rational Argument
Dispute over whether performance of a commanded act proves its permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether performing a commanded act establishes its permissibility and explain the rational proof (dalil al-istihsan) used, including the response to the mutakallimun's counterexample.

Core Idea
Performing a commanded act establishes its permissibility provisionally; otherwise, an impossible burden (taklif ma la yutaq) would arise.

This lesson examines a foundational dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: does merely performing a commanded act (al-ma'mur bihi) with its conditions and pillars automatically prove its permissibility (jawaz)? The Hanafi school answers affirmatively, relying on rational reasoning and rebutting the counterargument based on the invalid hajj case. Understanding this principle is essential for evaluating the validity of religious acts without requiring external verification for every performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question: When a person performs a commanded act observing all conditions and pillars, can we immediately judge it as permissible (ja'iz) without external evidence of validity?
This is about the attribute of jawaz, which Hanafis define as falling of the obligation to repeat (suqut al-qada').
2
State the mutakallimun's objection
Some mutakallimun (Mu'tazila) argue that performance alone does not prove permissibility, using the example of a pilgrim who invalidates hajj by intercourse before 'Arafah: he is commanded to continue the rites yet his performance is not deemed valid, requiring repetition the next year.
The objection claims that performance can be commanded even when the act is not permissible, so performance cannot be evidence of permissibility.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the pilgrim's continued performance is not a valid analogy because it is based on a new command (amr mubtada') independent of the original obligation. The initial performance, done with conditions and pillars, establishes permissibility provisionally; if later evidence shows a defect, the act is invalidated retroactively, but that does not negate the initial establishment.
The rational proof: if permissibility were not established upon performance, it would amount to an impossible burden (taklif ma la yutaq), because the believer cannot know with certainty all hidden conditions.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
According to the Hanafi position, once a person performs a wajib act, we judge it as valid (ja'iz) without further scrutiny, unless independent evidence of invalidity emerges. The mutakallimun require external verification of all conditions before deeming the act valid.
This practical difference affects how judges and muftis evaluate the validity of acts.

Source Text

Topic of the Specific: Statement of the establishment of the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and its negation. By way of appropriateness and consistency, he said: 'And does the attribute of permissibility become established for the commanded act when it is performed?' Some mutakallimun said no. That is, they differed concerning whether when one performs the commanded act while observing the conditions and pillars, we can judge it as permissible merely by his performance, or we suspend judgment until an external evidence appears indicating the purity of water and the rest of the conditions. So some mutakallimun said: We do not judge it until we know externally that it comprises the conditions and pillars. Do you not see that one who invalidates his hajj by intercourse before standing at 'Arafah is commanded to continue the rites by law, yet his performance is not permissible, and he must repeat it the next year? ... The correct view according to the jurists is that the attribute of permissibility and absence of dislike becomes established by it. That is, the sound school with us is that merely bringing the act into existence establishes the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act, and it means obtaining compliance with what one was obligated to do. Otherwise an impossible burden would be entailed. Then if invalidity appears by an independent evidence afterward, he repeats it. As for hajj, he performed it with this consecration and finished it, and the command to perform a valid hajj in the coming year is a new command... And when the attribute of obligation is absent from the commanded act, the attribute of permissibility does not remain according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. This is another discussion related to what has passed: that the necessitation of the command is obligation, meaning the obligation established by the command. So does the attribute of permissibility remain after abrogation of the obligation? For al-Shafi'i, he says that when it is abrogated...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses two key issues in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: (1) The relationship between performing a commanded act (al-ma'mur bihi) and establishing its permissibility (jawaz), and (2) the effect of abrogation (naskh) of obligation on permissibility. The first issue is a dispute with some mutakallimun (theologians, reportedly Mu'tazila) who argue that merely performing an act does not prove its permissibility; rather, external evidence is needed to verify conditions and pillars. They support their view with the example of one who invalidates his hajj by intercourse before 'Arafah: he is commanded to continue the rites (mudiyy) and yet his performance is not considered valid, requiring repetition the next year. The Hanafi response is twofold: (a) The earlier performance is considered an act of compliance (imtithal) with the original command, establishing permissibility provisionally. If later independent evidence shows a defect, the act is invalidated, but initial permissibility is not contradicted. (b) The command to continue in the invalid hajj case is a new independent command (amr mubtada'), not a continuation of the original obligation. The Hanafi school also relies on the rational principle that without establishing permissibility upon performance, an impossible burden (taklif ma la yutaq) would result. The second issue concerns abrogation: when the obligation (wujub) of an act is removed (e.g., by naskh), does permissibility (jawaz) remain? Hanafis hold that permissibility does not remain, because the command's direct entailment is obligation, and permissibility is derivative. Al-Shafi'i is reported to hold that permissibility can remain even after abrogation. The Hanafi position is grounded in the understanding that the act's legal characterization depends entirely on the command; once the command is lifted, no trace remains unless another command exists.

Key Terms
الجواز (al-jawāz): Attribute of the commanded act meaning its validity and that it fulfills the command, with the fall of the obligation to repeat (sūqūṭ al-qadā').
الوجوب (al-wujūb): Attribute of obligation entailed by the command (amr).
المأمور به (al-ma'mūr bihi): The commanded act, which is the object of the command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the text, what is the logical consequence if performing a commanded act did not establish its permissibility?
A) The act would be automatically invalid.
B) The act would still be valid but require repetition.
C) An impossible burden (taklif ma la yutaq) would arise.
D) The command would be considered abrogated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, performing a commanded act with its conditions establishes its permissibility provisionally, supported by the rational principle of avoiding impossible burden.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
