Abrogation of Obligation: Does Permissibility Remain? Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute over whether permissibility remains after abrogation of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether permissibility (jawaz) remains after the obligation (wujub) of a commanded act is abrogated, and explain the basis of disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When obligation is abrogated, permissibility does not remain, because the command entails both obligation and permissibility; removing one removes the other.

This lesson addresses a second dispute: if a command is abrogated (naskh), does the attribute of permissibility (jawaz) persist even after the obligation is lifted? The Hanafi school holds that permissibility vanishes along with obligation, while Imam al-Shafi'i is reported to argue that the act may remain permissible. Understanding this dispute is crucial for determining the legal status of acts after their original commands are superseded.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that when the attribute of obligation (wujub) is removed from a commanded act (by abrogation), the attribute of permissibility (jawaz) also ceases to exist. The act becomes legally neutral unless another command establishes its permissibility.
This is based on the principle that the command (amr) directly entails obligation, and permissibility is derived from that same command.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly holds that abrogation removes only the obligation, but the act may still be permissible (mubah) because the Lawgiver's original permission remains unless explicitly revoked.
The Shafi'i view sees obligation and permissibility as separable attributes.
3
Explain the Hanafi reasoning
The Hanafi proof: The command (amr) necessitates obligation (wujub) as its primary effect. Permissibility (jawaz) is a secondary attribute that depends on the command. When the command is abrogated, both its effects disappear. There is no independent source for permissibility.
The passage states: 'When the attribute of obligation is absent from the commanded act, the attribute of permissibility does not remain according to us.'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if a command to do something is abrogated (e.g., the command to face Jerusalem in prayer), a Hanafi would rule that praying towards Jerusalem is not permissible (unless there is a new permission), while a Shafi'i might still consider it permissible as a voluntary act.
This difference appears in cases of abrogated commands in the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث الخاص بيان ثبوت صفة الجواز للمأمور به وعدمه مناسبة واطراداً فقال وهل تثبت صفة الجواز للمأمور به إذا أتى به؟ قال بعض المتكلمين لا يعني اختلفوا في أنه إذا أدى المأمور به مع رعاية الشرائط والأركان، فهل يجوز لنا أن نحكم بمجرد إتيانه بالجواز، أو نتوقف فيه حتى يظهر دليل خارجي يدل على طهارة الماء وسائر الشرائط، فقال بعض المتكلمين: لا نحكم به حتى نعلم من خارج أنه مستجمع للشرائط والأركان، ألا ترى أن أفسد حجه بالجماع قبل الوقوف فهو مأمور بالأداء شرعًا بالمضي على أفعاله مع أنه لا يجوز المؤدى إذا أداه، فيقضي من قابل. مناسبة واطرادًا إلخ هذا علة لشرع أي أتى بهذا المضمون لمناسبته بالمضمون السابق، وهو حسن المأمور به، فإن مناسبة الجواز بالحسن غير مخفي، ومعنى الاطراد أنه ذكر هذا الباب ليصير بيان الأمر جامعا لجميع مطالبه الضرورية (السنبلي) وهل تثبت إلخ ولو قال المصنف كغيره وهل الإتيان بالمأمور به يوجب الأجزاء لكان أولى. [فتح الغفار ٧٧] صفة الجواز أي الصفة التي هو الجواز ، والمراد بالجواز : سقوط القضاء تحقيقًا فيما له قضاء كالفروض الخمس، أو تقديرًا فيما لا قضاء له كالجمعة، فإن فيه اختلافًا، وأما الجواز بمعنى موافقة الأمر، فثبوته متفق عليه كذا قيل، وقال ابن الملك: إن النزاع لفظي، فعند المتكلمين الجواز عبارة عن سقوط القضاء عمن أتى به، وهذا لا يعرف إلا بدليل زائد وعند الفقهاء هو عبارة عن حصول الامتثال بإتيان المأمور به كما وجب، فلو لم يثبت الجواز عند إتيانه يلزم تكليف ما لا يطاق. (القمر) بعض المتكلمين: أي بعض متكلمي المعتزلة كذا قيل. (القمر) لا نحكم به إلخ لأن النهي ضد الأمر، وهو لا يدل على الفساد، فإن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة ليست بفاسدة مع أنه ورد النهي عنها، فكذا الأمر لا يدل على الجواز وفيه أن النهي يدل على الفساد إما في ذات المنهي أو في محاوره، وخلو الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة عن الفساد الأعم من الذاتي والمجاوري مسلم. (القمر) ألا ترى إلخ خلاصته: أن الإتيان بالمأمور به لا يكون دليلاً على جوازه، ولا على عدم جوازه كما في إفساد الحج بالجماع يؤمر بالإتيان بتمام الحج مع أنه لا يكون جائزاً، فإنه لو حكم بجوازه، فينبغي أن لا يقضى في العام القبل، وأيضًا لا يكون غير جائز ؛ إذ لو حكم بعدم جوازه فيليق أن لا يكون مأمورا بالأداء بالمضي على أركانه فعلم أن حكمه متوقف، ولا يحكم بشيء من الجواز والفساد. (السنبلي) فهو مأمور إلخ أي هو يمضي على أفعال الحج، وهو يؤدي ما أحرم به مع أنه لا يجوز هذا المؤدى، وعليه القضاء من العام القابل، فكيف تحكم بالجواز أي سقوط القضاء بمجرد إتيان المأمور به. (القمر) عنه و الصحيح عند الفقهاء: أنه تثبت به صفة الجواز للمأمور به وانتفاء الكراهة أي المذهب الصحيح عندنا أنه تثبت بمجرد إيجاد الفعل صفة الجواز للمأمور به، وهو حصول الامتثال على ما كلف به، وإلا يلزم تكليف ما لا يطاق، ثم إذا ظهر الفساد بدليل مستقل بعده يعيده، وأما الحج فقد أداه بهذا الإحرام وفرغ عنه، والأمر بحج صحيح في العام القابل بأمر مبتدأ وعند أبي بكر الرازي لا يثبت بمطلق الأمر انتفاء الكراهة؛ لأن عصر يومه مأمور بالأداء مع أنه مكروه شرعًا، والطواف محدثًا مأمور به مع أنه مكروه شرعًا، قلنا: ذلك الكراهة ليس في نفس المأمور به بل لمعنى خارج وهو التشبيه بعبدة الشمس، وكون الطائف محدثًا، ومثل هذا غير مضر. وإذا عدمت صفة الوجوب للمأمور به لا تبقى صفة الجواز عندنا خلافًا للشافعي هذا بحث آخر متعلق بما مرّ من أن موجب الأمر هو الوجوب يعني الوجوب الثابت بالأمر فهل تبقى صفة الجواز بعد نسخ الوجوب؟ للشافعي أنه إذا نسخ ... وانتفاء الكراهة بالرفع معطوف على صفة الجواز. (القمر) وهو حصول الامتثال إلخ فيه أن الامتثال عبارة عن موافقة الأمر، ولا خلاف في الجواز بهذا المعنى، فإنه ثابت بالاتفاق، إنما الخلاف في الجواز بمعنى سقوط القضاء كذا قيل فتأمل (القمر) وإلا أي وإن لم يحصل الامتثال بمجرد إيجاد الفعل يلزم تكليف إلخ، واللازم مدفوع شرعًا. (القمر) وأما الحج إلخ جواب عن قوله : ألا ترى أن من أفسد إلخ.(القمر) وأما الحج أي خلاصة الجواب: أن الحج لا يقضى من عام قابل، فلا ينافي جوازه في هذا العام، وأما قولك: على هذا فلم يحج من عام قابل فنقول: هو لأمر مبتدأ مستأنف لا لأمر سابق. (السنبلي) بأمر مبتدأ فكأنه ليس بقضاء الأول . (القمر) مكروه شرعًا: أي إذا أداه حال تغير الشمس. (القمر) ليس إلخ لأن الأمر أبلغ في طلب الفعل من الإذن، وبالإذن ينتفي الكراهة، فلأن تنتفى بالأمر وهو أعلى أولى. (القمر) في نفس المأمور به إلخ أي وكلامنا في نفس المأمور به أي أنه جائز في نفسه، أو مكروه في ذاته.(السنبلي) التشبيه إلخ : فإن الشمس تعبد في أخر اليوم، والعبدة جمع العابد. (القمر)
Topic of the Specific: Statement of the establishment of the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and its negation. By way of appropriateness and consistency, he said: 'And does the attribute of permissibility become established for the commanded act when it is performed?' Some mutakallimun said no. That is, they differed concerning whether when one performs the commanded act while observing the conditions and pillars, we can judge it as permissible merely by his performance, or we suspend judgment until an external evidence appears indicating the purity of water and the rest of the conditions. So some mutakallimun said: We do not judge it until we know externally that it comprises the conditions and pillars. Do you not see that one who invalidates his hajj by intercourse before standing at 'Arafah is commanded to continue the rites by law, yet his performance is not permissible, and he must repeat it the next year? ... The correct view according to the jurists is that the attribute of permissibility and absence of dislike becomes established by it. That is, the sound school with us is that merely bringing the act into existence establishes the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act, and it means obtaining compliance with what one was obligated to do. Otherwise an impossible burden would be entailed. Then if invalidity appears by an independent evidence afterward, he repeats it. As for hajj, he performed it with this consecration and finished it, and the command to perform a valid hajj in the coming year is a new command... And when the attribute of obligation is absent from the commanded act, the attribute of permissibility does not remain according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. This is another discussion related to what has passed: that the necessitation of the command is obligation, meaning the obligation established by the command. So does the attribute of permissibility remain after abrogation of the obligation? For al-Shafi'i, he says that when it is abrogated...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses two key issues in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: (1) The relationship between performing a commanded act (al-ma'mur bihi) and establishing its permissibility (jawaz), and (2) the effect of abrogation (naskh) of obligation on permissibility. The first issue is a dispute with some mutakallimun (theologians, reportedly Mu'tazila) who argue that merely performing an act does not prove its permissibility; rather, external evidence is needed to verify conditions and pillars. They support their view with the example of one who invalidates his hajj by intercourse before 'Arafah: he is commanded to continue the rites (mudiyy) and yet his performance is not considered valid, requiring repetition the next year. The Hanafi response is twofold: (a) The earlier performance is considered an act of compliance (imtithal) with the original command, establishing permissibility provisionally. If later independent evidence shows a defect, the act is invalidated, but initial permissibility is not contradicted. (b) The command to continue in the invalid hajj case is a new independent command (amr mubtada'), not a continuation of the original obligation. The Hanafi school also relies on the rational principle that without establishing permissibility upon performance, an impossible burden (taklif ma la yutaq) would result. The second issue concerns abrogation: when the obligation (wujub) of an act is removed (e.g., by naskh), does permissibility (jawaz) remain? Hanafis hold that permissibility does not remain, because the command's direct entailment is obligation, and permissibility is derivative. Al-Shafi'i is reported to hold that permissibility can remain even after abrogation. The Hanafi position is grounded in the understanding that the act's legal characterization depends entirely on the command; once the command is lifted, no trace remains unless another command exists.

Key Terms
الجواز (al-jawāz): Attribute of the commanded act meaning permissibility/validity.
الوجوب (al-wujūb): Attribute of obligation entailed by the command.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this lesson, what happens to the permissibility (jawaz) of a commanded act when its obligation (wujub) is abrogated?
A) The permissibility remains unchanged.
B) The permissibility is also removed.
C) The permissibility becomes stronger.
D) The permissibility is transformed into disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, abrogation of a command removes both obligation and permissibility; the act becomes legally inert until a new command or evidence re-establishes its status.

Dispute on Survival of Permissibility After Abrogation
Presents Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on whether jawaz persists after naskh of wujub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the survival of jawaz after naskh, explain the opposing Shafi'i view, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith of oaths and the analogy of Bani Isra'il.

Core Idea
When an obligation is abrogated, its inherent permissibility vanishes; any remaining permissibility must come from a new proof.

This lesson explores a fundamental usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: when an obligatory command is abrogated, does the permissibility (jawaz) that was part of that obligation continue to exist? The Shafi'is argue that permissibility remains, as seen in the fast of 'Ashura. The Hanafis insist that the permissibility was merely a shadow of the obligation and disappears with it. We will unpack the evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and qiyas that each school uses, and understand the practical implications of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
State the dispute: does the permissibility (jawaz) inherent in an obligation survive after the obligation is abrogated?
This is not about whether the act becomes haram, but whether the 'permissible' status continues.
2
Distinguish the meanings of ja'iz
Use the passage's four definitions of 'ja'iz', focusing on the fourth meaning: 'that which has no restriction (haraj)'. This meaning includes wajib, mandub, and mubah.
The dispute concerns this fourth meaning of jawaz.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the analogy of Bani Isra'il (cutting sinful limbs) and the principle that the voidness of the container (wujub) implies voidness of its content (jawaz).
The Hanafi position relies on qiyas and the logical inseparability of jawaz from wujub.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Consider the example of fasting 'Ashura (originally obligatory, now mustahabb) and the hadith on oaths (command to give kaffarah before violating).
Shafi'is argue that permissibility remains because the action is still good and the hadith uses 'thumma' (then) implying order.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the dispute to a concrete case: giving kaffarah before breaking an oath. The Shafi'i allows it (permissibility remains), the Hanafi does not.
This practical difference shows the real impact of the usul dispute.

Source Text

بيان ثبوت صفة الجواز للمأمور به وعدمه بصوم عاشوراء، فإنه كان فرضاً ثم نسخت فرضيته، وبقي استحبابه الآن، وعندنا لا تبقى صفة الجواز الثابت في ضمن الوجوب كما أن قطع الأعضاء الخاطئة كان واجبًا على بني إسرائيل، وقد نسخ منا فرضيته وجوازه، وهكذا القياس. وأما صوم عاشوراء فإنما يثبت جوازه الآن بنص آخر لا بذلك النص الموجب للأداء، وقيل: وفائدة الخلاف بيننا وبينه يظهر في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "من حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيرا منها فليكفر يمينه ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير"، على مقسم عليه. الجواز الذي في ضمنه إلخ : اعلم أن الجائز يطلق على معان منها: ما لا يمتنع عقلاً، ومنها: ما استوى الأمران أي الفعل والترك، وفيه شرعًا وهو المباح، ومنها ما تعارض الأدلة الشرعية فيه كسور الحمار، فإن بعض الدلائل الشرعية تدل على الطهارة وبعضها على النجاسة ومنها ما لا يمتنع شرعًا أي ما حكم الشارع بعدم الحرج فيه، وهذا الجواز الذي يشمل الواجب والمندوب والمباح وهو جنس الواجب، وفي ضمنه، فإن الواجب عبارة عما الحرج في تركه ولا حرج في فعله وهذا هو الجواز الذي يدعي الشافعية بقائه بعد انتساخ الوجوب، والحنفية عدم بقائه صرح به الإعلام وما قيل إن الذي أريد به في المتنازع فيه الإباحة أي التخيير بين الفعل والترك، فلا تصغ إليه، ثم اعلم أن النزاع بيننا وبين الشافعية إنما هو في ما إذا نسخ الوجوب فقط، وأما إذا نسخ فعل الواجب وكان حكم الناسخ التحريم، فلا يبقى الجواز بالاتفاق. (القمر) نسخت إلخ : أي بفرضية رمضان على ما في حديث رواه جابر بن سمرة له. (القمر) لا تبقى صفة إلخ فإن بطلان المتضمن يدل على بطلان ما في ضمنه فالجواز لو ثبت ثبت بدليل آخر أو بالإباحة الأصلية، فإن الأمر يفيد الجواز الذي هو في ضمن الوجوب إلا الجواز الذي في ضمن الندب أو الإباحة، فإذا نسخ الوجوب، ففي هذا الجواز، وأما الجواز الذي هو في ضمن الإباحة أو الندب فهو حكم آخر لابد له من دليل آخر. (القمر) وأما صوم إلخ: جواب عن دليل الشافعي له. (القمر) بنص آخر أي بدليل أخر وهو القياس على سائر الصيامات النفلية أو حديث وارد بذلك. (القمر) أخرجه البخاري في "صحيحه" رقم ٦٢٤٨ ، كتاب الأيمان والنذر ، ومسلم رقم ١٦٥٢، باب من حلف بالات والعزى؛ وابن حبان في "صحيحه" :رقم: ٤٣٤۸ ، ۱۸۹/۱۰ ، والنسائي رقم ۳۷۸٤ باب من حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيرًا منها أبو داود رقم: ۳۲۷۷ باب الرجل يكفر قبل أن يحنث والترمذي رقم: ١٥٢٩، باب ما جاء فيمن حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيرًا منها ، وأحمد في مسنده رقم ۲۰٦٣٧، عن عبد الرحمن بن سمرة. فإنه يدل على وجوب تقديم الكفارة على الحنث، وقد نسخ وجوب تقديمها بالإجماع، ولكن بقي جوازه عنده ولم يبق عندنا أصلًا.
Statement concerning the proven establishment of the attribute of permissibility for the commanded act and its non-establishment: by the fast of 'Ashura, for it was obligatory then its obligatory nature was abrogated, and its recommended status remains now. According to us, the permissibility that was inherent in the obligation does not remain, just as the cutting of sinful limbs was obligatory upon the Children of Israel, and its obligatory nature and its permissibility were abrogated from us, and thus is the analogy. As for the fast of 'Ashura, its permissibility is now established by another text, not by that original text that required performance. And it is said: The benefit of the difference between us and him appears in his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better than it, let him expiate his oath and then do that which is better.' Regarding the different meanings of 'jawaz': Know that 'ja'iz' is used for several meanings: that which is not prevented by reason, that in which the two matters are equal (action and abandonment) which in Sacred Law is 'mubah', that concerning which the legal evidences are contradictory (like the hide of a donkey), and that which is not prevented by Sacred Law – i.e., that regarding which the Lawgiver has ruled that there is no restriction – and this is the permissibility that includes the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible, and it is the genus of the obligatory and immanent within it; indeed the obligatory is an expression of that which there is restriction in abandoning it and no restriction in doing it. This is the permissibility that the Shafi'is claim remains after abrogation of the obligation, while the Hanafis say it does not remain, as stated by al-'Allamah. And what is said that what is intended by it in the disputed matter is 'ibahah (equivalence between doing and leaving), pay no attention to it. Then know that the dispute between us and the Shafi'is is only concerning when the obligation alone is abrogated; but if the action of the obligatory is abrogated and the ruling of the abrogator is prohibition, then permissibility does not remain by agreement. (al-Qamar) 'abrogated etc.' meaning by the obligation of Ramadan according to what is in a hadith narrated by Jabir ibn Samurah. (al-Qamar) 'the attribute does not remain etc.' because the invalidity of the subsuming indicates the invalidity of what is subsumed within it. So if permissibility were established, it would be established by another evidence or by original permissibility, for the command indicates the permissibility that is inherent in the obligation, not the permissibility inherent in recommendation or permissibility. Thus when the obligation is abrogated, this permissibility [inherent in it] is gone. As for the permissibility that is inherent in permissibility or recommendation, it is another ruling that requires another evidence. (al-Qamar) 'And as for the fast etc.' is a response to the Shafi'i's evidence. (al-Qamar) 'by another text' i.e., by another evidence, which is analogy to other supererogatory fasts or a hadith that came concerning that. (al-Qamar) It was narrated by al-Bukhari in his Sahih (no. 6248, Book of Oaths and Vows), Muslim (no. 1652), Ibn Hibban in his Sahih (no. 4348, 10/189), al-Nasa'i (no. 3784), Abu Dawud (no. 3277), al-Tirmidhi (no. 1529), and Ahmad in his Musnad (no. 20637) from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Samurah. For it indicates the obligation of giving the expiation before the violation, and the obligation of giving it before has been abrogated by consensus, but its permissibility according to him remains, whereas according to us it does not remain at all.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul dispute concerning whether the quality of permissibility (jawaz) that is inherent in a wajib command survives after the command's obligatory force is abrogated. The text first presents the example of fasting 'Ashura: originally obligatory in early Islam, then abrogated, and now mustahabb. The Shafi'i argues that the permissibility of the act remains – it is still permitted even if no longer required. The Hanafi position is that when the obligation is removed, the specific permissibility that was part of the obligation disappears. Analogy is drawn to the cutting of sinful limbs for the Children of Israel: that act was both obligatory and permissible for them, but for us it is neither. The permissibility of fasting 'Ashura today comes from a fresh dalil (e.g., qiyas on voluntary fasts), not from the original command. The commentary then clarifies the term 'ja'iz', enumerating four usages: (1) rationally possible, (2) legally permissible (mubah, where action and omission are equal), (3) controversial matters (like hide of donkey, where proofs conflict), and (4) what is not legally restricted – this last meaning includes wajib, mandub, and mubah. The dispute specifically focuses on this fourth type of jawaz that is 'in the folds' of wujub. The Hanafi position is supported by the principle that if the container (the obligation) is void, its contents (the permissibility inherent in it) are also void; any remaining permissibility must be sourced elsewhere. The text then uses the hadith on oaths and expiation to illustrate the practical difference: the Shafi'i allows giving kaffarah before breaking the oath because permissibility remains after abrogation, while the Hanafi forbids it because that permissibility does not persist. The authority of this ruling rests on later Hanafi fatawa (mutakhkhirin) as it is from Noorul Anwar, not Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الجائز (al-ja'iz): Here defined as that which the Lawgiver has ruled there is no restriction (haraj) in performing, encompassing wajib, mandub, and mubah.
الجواز (al-jawaz): The quality of being permitted; in this context, specifically the permissibility that is inherent in, and inseparable from, an obligation (wujub).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is fasting 'Ashura permissible today?
A) Because the original obligation's permissibility remains.
B) Because a new text or analogy establishes its permissibility.
C) Because all abrogated commands retain their permissibility by default.
D) Because consensus allows it.

Key Takeaway
When an obligation is abrogated, its inherent permissibility is also abrogated; any remaining permissibility must be proven from a separate source.

Division of Commands: Mutlaq vs Muwaqqat
Introduces the two types of commands: absolute (mutlaq) and time-bound (muwaqqat)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between a mutlaq command and a muwaqqat command in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and apply the classification to examples like zakat and sadaqat al-fitr.

Core Idea
A command is absolute if it never becomes qada—any performance is ada; time-bound imposes a deadline after which it becomes qada.

This passage from Noorul Anwar introduces a fundamental classification of commands (awamir) in usul al-fiqh: whether they are absolute (mutlaq) or time-bound (muwaqqat). Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when a missed obligation must be made up (qada) versus when it remains ada regardless of timing. The author illustrates with zakat and sadaqat al-fitr.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories
The passage divides commands into mutlaq (absolute) and muwaqqat (time-bound). The key difference is whether the act has a fixed time window whose lapse converts performance to qada.
2
Identify the criterion for mutlaq
Mutlaq means the command is not tied to a specific time upon whose failure the act becomes qada. Instead, any performance, whether early or delayed, counts as ada.
The Arabic phrase: 'غير مقيد بوقت يفوت بفوته'
3
Apply to zakat
Zakat is mutlaq: once the cause (nisab) and condition (hawl) are met, the obligation exists but can be fulfilled at any time. Even if delayed, it is ada, not qada.
Though immediate performance is recommended (mustahab).
4
Apply to sadaqat al-fitr
Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr is mutlaq; it can be given before or after Eid, and it remains ada (though immediate performance is recommended).
Contrast with prayers which are muwaqqat.
5
Contrast with muwaqqat
Muwaqqat commands have a fixed time; if the time passes, the act becomes qada. Examples include the five daily prayers and fasting Ramadan.
Knowing this distinction affects fatwa on missed acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما فرغ المصنف عن مباحث حسن المأمور به وملحقاته شرع في بيان تقسيمه إلى المطلق والمؤقت فقال والأمر :نوعان مطلق عن الوقت أي أحدهما أمر مطلق غير مقيد بوقت يفوت بفوته كالزكاة وصدقة الفطر، فإنهما بعد وجود السبب أي ملك المال والرأس والشرط أي حولان الحول، ويوم الفطر لا يتقيدان بوقت يفوتان معطوف على بفوته، بل كلما أدّي يكون أداءً لا قضاءً، وإن كان المستحب التعجيل. (المشكاة) حلف الكفارة
Then when the author finished the discussions on the goodness of the commanded act and its appendages, he proceeded to explain its division into the absolute and the time-bound, and said: 'And the command: two types: absolute with respect to time' – i.e., one of them is an absolute command not restricted to a time whose lapse causes the act to be missed, like zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. For indeed, after the existence of the cause (i.e., ownership of wealth and head) and the condition (i.e., the passing of the year and the day of Fitr), they are not restricted to a time whose lapse causes them to be missed (as a conjoined phrase) – rather, whenever performed, it is ada, not qada, even though immediate performance is recommended. (al-Mishkat) oath expiation
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a classification rule (usul rule) from Noorul Anwar, dividing the commanded act (al-ma'mur bihi) into two categories: absolute (mutlaq) and time-bound (muwaqqat). The term 'absolute' here means the act is not restricted to a specific window of time such that if that time passes, the act becomes qada (make-up). Examples given are zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. For zakat, once the cause (nisab) and condition (hawl) are met, the obligation exists but can be fulfilled at any time before death; it is always ada. Similarly, sadaqat al-fitr becomes obligatory on the day of 'Eid but can be given before or on the day; if delayed past 'Eid, it remains ada? Actually according to Hanafi fiqh, it can be given before 'Eid, and if given after, it is still ada not qada . The text emphasizes that even though the act is not time-restricted in the sense of lapsed performance, it is still recommended to expedite. The authority weight is from the later Hanafi usul tradition (Noorul Anwar and its commentaries). The phrase 'حلف الكفارة' at the end is likely a marginal note referring back to the previous section, not part of this rule itself.

Key Terms
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): A command not restricted to a specific time upon whose lapse the act becomes qada; performance at any time counts as ada.
الأمر المؤقت (al-amr al-muwaqqat): A command restricted to a specified time; if the time passes, the act becomes qada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on this passage, what distinguishes a 'mutlaq' command from a 'muwaqqat' command?
A) Mutlaq must be performed immediately; muwaqqat can be delayed.
B) Mutlaq is not restricted to a time whose lapse would make the act qada; muwaqqat is.
C) Mutlaq applies only to financial obligations; muwaqqat applies only to prayers.
D) Mutlaq is recommended; muwaqqat is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, absolute commands (mutlaq) allow performance at any time as ada, while time-bound (muwaqqat) commands have a fixed window after which performance becomes qada.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Absolute Commands: Immediacy vs. Delay and the Three Roles of Time
Analyzes command's time implication and types of time-binding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether an absolute command requires immediate performance, apply the proof that the nature of command is facilitation, and distinguish the three functions of time in a command.

Core Idea
An absolute command does not demand immediate action; it permits delay, because the essence of command is ease, not hardship.

A key question in usul al-fiqh is whether an unqualified command (amr mutlaq) must be performed immediately or can be delayed. The Hanafi school, as presented here, adopts the view of tarakhi (deferment), arguing that requiring immediacy would contradict the very nature of command, which is facilitation. This lesson unpacks the debate with al-Karkhi and then explores how time interacts with commands: as a container, a condition, or a cause for obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
Recognize the two opposing views: the Hanafi position that absolute commands permit delay (tarakhi) versus al-Karkhi's view that they require immediacy (faur).
This is the central ikhtilaf of the passage.
2
Understand the Hanafi Proof
Grasp the core argument: the subject (mawdu') of an absolute command is ease (taysir); requiring immediacy would negate that subject (naqd al-mawdu').
The proof is based on the nature of command itself, not on external evidence.
3
Evaluate the Opposing Proof and Response
Consider the opposing evidence: the example of a master asking for water. The Hanafi response distinguishes between a command contextualized by custom (''urf) and an absolute command devoid of context.
This shows the importance of removing contextual clues before applying a rule.
4
Recognize the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Understand when sin accrues: the Hanafi position holds that delaying an absolute command is not sinful until near death, while the opposing view considers delay sinful from the first moment.
This affects daily practice of worship.
5
Classify the Three Roles of Time in Commands
Learn the three functions time can have: container (zarf), condition (shart), and cause (sabab). Analyze how each applies to the daily prayers.
Time as cause is particularly nuanced; it does not have intrinsic causal power but is assigned by Allah.

للكرخي أي لأبي الحسن الكرخي منا وللشافعية والكرخي محلة ببغداد وقرية من قرى بغداد كذا قيل، وفي "الكشف" روى الكرخي عن أصحابنا أنه على الفور، وهو قول عامة أهل الحديث وبعض المعتزلة، وذكر أبو سهل الزجاجي أنه عند أنه عند أبي يوسف الله على الفور، وعند محمد والشافعي حملها على التراخي، وروي عن أبي حنيفة مثل قول أبي يوسف له. (القمر) لا يجب الفور إلخ أي لا يجب أداؤه في أول أوقات إمكان الفعل فالمراد بالتراخي عدم التقييد بالحال لا التقييد بالمستقبل حتى لو أدى في الحال لا يخرج عن العهدة، والفور في الأصل مصدر يقال: فارت القدر إذا غلت ثم استعير للسرعة. (القمر)
لا يجب الفور إلخ وعلى هذا المعنى فلا يرد قول المصنف وهو على التراخي إلخ، أنه يفهم عنه أن التراخي في الأمر أحب وهو كما ترى فاسد ؛ لأن الشارح بهذا الكلام بين المراد بقول المصنف: هو على التراخي نفي وجوب الفور لا وجوب التأخير بقرينة تقابل قول الكرخي فافهم. (السنبلي) لابد فيه إلخ واستدلوا عليه بأن السيد إذا قال لعبده اسقني ماء يفهم منه تعجيل السقي حتى أنه يذم العبد في نظر العقلاء على تقدير التأخير، فكان الأمر محمولاً على الفور، وفيه أن الكلام في الأمر الذي يكون عاريًا عن القرائن والقطع بالفور في المثال المذكور بسبب العرف والعادة ولا كلام فيه. (القمر)
يأثم بالتأخير إلخ لأن التأخير تفويت إذ لا يدري أيقدر على الأداء في الوقت الثاني أو لا يقدر، والتفويت حرام وفيه أنا لا نسلم أن التأخير تفويت؛ لتمكنه من الأداء في جزء يدركه من الوقت وأما الموت فجاءة فهو نادر لا يصلح لأن يبنى الأحكام عليه . (القمر) لئلا يعود أي لئلا يرجع على موضوعه أي على مدلوله أو على فائدة متلبسًا بالنقض أي ناقضاً لموضوعه وهو الإطلاق. (القمر) لعاد إلخ : أي لصار موضوعه منتقضا وباطلاً. (القمر)

ومقيدًا به أي الثاني أمر مقيد بالوقت وهو أربعة أنواع؛ لأنه إما أن يكون الوقت ظرفًا للمؤدى، وشرطا للأداء وسببًا للوجوب، فهو النوع الأول، والمراد بالظرف أن لا يكون معيارا له، بل يفضل عنه، والمراد بالشرط أن لا يصح المأمور به قبل وجوده ويفوت بفوته. والمراد بالسبب أن لهذا الوقت تأثيرًا في وجوب المأمور به وإن كان المؤثر الحقيقي في كل شيء هو الله تعالى، ولكن يضاف الوجوب في الظاهر إلى الوقت؛ لأن في كل لمحة وصول نعمة من الله تعالى إلى جانب العبد وهو يقتضي الشكر في كل ساعة، وإنما خص هذه الأوقات المعينة بالعبادات؛ لعظمتها، وتجدد النعم فيها، ولئلا يفضي إلى الحرج في تحصيل المعاش إن استغرق الوقت العبادة. كوقت الصلاة،

Topic of the specific. 147. Exposition of the import of the command regarding the ruling of time. It (the command) is on deferment, contrary to al-Karkhi. Meaning: this absolute command is interpreted by us as on deferment, rather it allows delay. According to al-Karkhi, its demand necessarily requires immediacy, meaning that immediacy is not obligatory in its performance, but rather its delay is precautionary for the matter of worship, in the sense that one sins by delay, not in the sense that one becomes a make-up performer. According to us, one does not sin except at the end of life, or when signs of death appear and one has not performed it. Our proof is what he indicated by his saying: Lest it return to its subject with negation, meaning the subject of the absolute command was facilitation and ease. If it were interpreted as immediacy, it would return to its subject with negation and would be contradictory to the subject. For al-Karkhi, i.e. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi from our school, and for the Shafi'is. And al-Karkhi is a quarter in Baghdad and a village from the villages of Baghdad, it is said. In al-Kashf: al-Karkhi narrated from our companions that it is on immediacy, and it is the saying of most hadith scholars and some Mutazila. Abu Sahl al-Zajjaji mentioned that according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it is on immediacy, and according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i it is interpreted as on deferment. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa similar to the saying of Abu Yusuf. (al-Qamar) 'Immediacy is not obligatory' etc., meaning its performance is not obligatory at the earliest times of possibility of the act. The intended meaning of deferment is not restriction to the present moment, not restriction to the future, such that if one performs immediately, one is not freed from liability. Immediacy originally is a verbal noun: it is said 'the pot boiled' then figuratively used for speed. (al-Qamar) 'Immediacy is not obligatory' etc., and based on this meaning, the author's statement 'it is on deferment' etc. is not refuted, that it would be understood that deferment in the command is beloved, and it is, as you see, corrupt. Because the commentator by this statement clarified the intended meaning of the author's statement 'it is on deferment' as negation of obligation of immediacy, not obligation of delay, by the context of contrasting with al-Karkhi's statement, so understand. (al-Sunbulī) 'It necessarily requires' etc. And they argued for it that if a master says to his slave 'Give me water to drink', it is understood as immediate giving, to the extent that the slave is blamed in the view of rational people for delaying. So the command is interpreted as on immediacy. But the discussion is about a command devoid of contextual indicators, and the certainty of immediacy in the mentioned example is due to custom and habit, and there is no argument there. (al-Qamar) 'He sins by delay' etc. because delay is waste, as he does not know if he will be able to perform in a second time or not, and waste is forbidden. But we do not concede that delay is waste, because he is able to perform in a part of time he reaches. As for sudden death, it is rare and not suitable for building rulings upon it. (al-Qamar) 'Lest it return' i.e. lest it revert to its subject, i.e. its signification or benefit, being accompanied by negation, i.e. negating its subject, which is absoluteness. (al-Qamar) 'It would return' etc., i.e. its subject would become negated and invalid. (al-Qamar) [PAGE_149] And restricted by it, i.e. the second is a command restricted by time, and it is of four types. Because either the time is a container for the performed act, a condition for performance, and a cause for obligation — that is the first type. The intended meaning of container is that it is not a measure for it, but rather it is extra. The intended meaning of condition is that the commanded act is not valid before its existence and is lost by its loss. The intended meaning of cause is that this time has an influence on the obligation of the commanded act, although the true influencer in everything is Allah Almighty, but obligation is attributed outwardly to the time. Because in every moment, a blessing from Allah Almighty reaches the side of the servant, and this necessitates gratitude every hour. Only these specific times are singled out for acts of worship due to their greatness, the renewal of blessings in them, and so as not to lead to hardship in earning a livelihood if all time were occupied with worship. Like the time of prayer. The commanded act: it necessarily must be by time, i.e. by a limited time such that if the time passes, the performance passes. (al-Qamar) 'For the performed act' etc.: the performed act is the form resulting from the specific pillars occurring in the time, like standing, sitting, bowing, prostrating for prayer. Performance is bringing it out from the concealment of non-existence to the arena of existence, it is said. (al-Qamar) 'For obligation': i.e. for the obligation itself. For the obligation of performance is by command, and the cause according to them is what is a signifier for the realization of the effect and leads to its existence, it is said. (al-Qamar) 'The intended meaning' etc.: by the context of contrasting with the measure. The measure is what the commanded act occurs within, being estimated by it, so it increases with length of time and decreases with shortness. (al-Qamar) 'Rather it is extra': i.e. extra to the performed act, such that it accommodates that obligatory performed act and other than it. (al-Qamar) 'Because in every moment' etc.: by this explanation, what might be imagined of a connection between causes and effects is repelled, and there is no connection between time and the obligation of worship, so how can time be suitable as a cause for worship? (al-Qamar) 'Only these specific times are singled out' etc.: it repels a presumed objection: its gist is that gratitude should be every hour, so why are these five times singled out? (al-Qamar) 'The renewal of blessings in them': for waking up at dawn is life after sleep which is like death, so as gratitude for it, the Fajr prayer was prescribed. Then during the day, when means of livelihood from foods, drinks, etc. are obtained, the Zuhr prayer was prescribed as gratitude. And since after Zuhr prayer there is a kind of sleep and rest customary for most people, the Asr prayer was prescribed to compensate for negligence of remembrance of Allah. Then when the blessings of the day are completed, the Maghrib prayer was prescribed as gratitude. And the prescription of Isha prayer is to complete gratitude and improve the ending, and sleep after it is like dying with faith and obedience. Thus the investigators mentioned. (al-Qamar) 'And so as not to lead' etc.: this does not suffice for anything, for it necessitates specifying times for worship, because occupying all times would be hardship, but it does not necessitate specifying these five specific times. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Manar al-Anwar, discussing two key usul questions: (1) whether an absolute command (amr mutlaq) requires immediate (faur) or delayed (tarakhi) performance, and (2) how time qualifies commands (types of time-restricted commands). The author adopts the Hanafi position that commands are on tarakhi unless evidence indicates otherwise. The proof is that the essence of command is ease (taysir); requiring immediacy would negate that. The passage then clarifies that 'tarakhi' does not mean one must delay, but that immediate performance is not obligatory; if one does it immediately, it is valid. The opposing view of Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi (and some Shafi'is) is that commands require faur, based on custom (e.g., a master's request for water). The Hanafi response is that such examples are contextualized by custom ('urf), not the absolute command. The second part discusses time-bound commands: time can function as a container (zarf) for the act, a condition (shart) for validity, or a cause (sabab) for obligation. The example given is the five daily prayers, with a detailed explanation of why specific times are chosen as causes for worship, based on the renewal of divine blessings at those moments.

Key Terms
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): A command that is not qualified by any condition or time restriction.
الفور (al-fawr): The obligation to perform the commanded act immediately at the earliest possible time.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): Permissibility of delaying the commanded act to a later time within the lifespan.
الظرف (al-zarf): Time as a container for the act, not a measure; the act can be performed within it but may also include other actions.
السبب (al-sabab): A cause that makes the obligation effective; time as cause does not have intrinsic causal power but is a sign of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the default ruling regarding the time of performing a command that is not qualified by any context?
A) It must be performed immediately (faur).
B) It may be delayed (tarakhi) without sin until near death.
C) It must be performed at a specific time determined by the command itself.
D) It is optional to perform or not.

Key Takeaway
An absolute command in Hanafi usul permits delay because its essence is facilitation, and time can function as container, condition, or cause for obligation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

The Four Functions of Time: Cause, Condition, Container in Hanafi Usul
Analysis of the four types of time as cause, condition, or container

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of time (sabab, shart, zarf) as they relate to the obligation of prayer, and apply this classification to determine the effect of missing parts of the time on the validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
Time is both cause (sabab) for obligation and container (zarf) for performance — resolving the apparent contradiction.

In this passage from Nur al-Anwar, the Hanafi usul framework distinguishes three functions of time: cause (sabab), condition (shart), and container (zarf). This classification addresses the objection that time cannot be both cause and container simultaneously. The author then details four types of attribution of obligation to time, explaining how causality transfers when prayer is delayed. This analysis directly impacts rulings on prayer validity, such as the effect of sunrise on Fajr prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three functions of time
Distinguish sabab (cause), shart (condition), and zarf (container) as they relate to time. The cause is the first part of time that triggers obligation; the condition is the existence of any part of time for performance; the container is the entire time envelope within which the act must occur.
2
Understand the objection and Hanafi resolution
The objection: time cannot be both container and cause because cause must precede effect. Hanafi response: time is container for the act performed and cause for the obligation itself — no contradiction.
3
Trace the four types of attribution
Obligation is attributed to (1) the first part, (2) what follows commencement (healthy parts), (3) the incomplete part at narrowing (only in 'Asr), (4) the whole time in make-up (qada). Understand how causality transfers.
4
Analyze the dispute with Shafi'i on Fajr and sunrise
Hanafi: if sunrise occurs during Fajr, the obligation becomes void and prayer becomes nafl. Shafi'i: prayer valid if one rak'ah caught before sunrise, citing a hadith. Hanafis interpret the hadith differently.
The difference stems from how each school defines the time of prayer and the function of the hadith.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت
تعلق الطلب بالفعل، وسببه الظاهري وهو الأمر أقيم مقامه، ثم الظرفية والسببية لا تجتمعان بحسب الظاهر؛ لأنه إن أدى في الوقت لا يكون سببًا؛ لأن السبب يجب أن يقدم على المسبب وإن لم يؤد في الوقت لا يكون ظرفا؛ إذ الظرف ما يؤدى فيه لا بعده، فلهذا قالوا: جواب للاعتراض: إن الظرف هو جميع الوقت والشرط هو مطلق الوقت والسبب هو الجزء الأول المتصل بالأداء قبل الشروع في الأداء، والكل في القضاء، وهو أربعة أنواع وقد فصله المصنف بقوله: وهو إما أن يضاف إلى الجزء الأول أو إلى ما يلي ابتداء الشروع، أو إلى الجزء الناقص عند ضيق الوقت أو إلى جملة الوقت يعني أن الأصل كل مسبب متصل بسببه، ثم الظرفية هذا اعتراض على كون الوقت ظرفًا وسببا، ويمكن أن يجاب عنه بأن الوقت ظرف للمؤدى، وسبب لنفس الوجوب فلا منافاة، لكنه بقيت مناقشة وهو: أن الأداء موقوف على الوجوب، والوجوب موقوف على السبب أي الوقت فصار ذلك السبب متقدمًا على الأداء أيضًا فيلزم المنافاة.
يجب أن يقدم إلخ: فإذا أدي في الوقت فأين تقدم السبب، فإن السبب هو كل الوقت بل كان الوقت ظرفًا.
جميع الوقت أي المجموع من حيث هو مجموع من أوله إلى آخره، فإن الظرف زمان يحيط به ويفضل عنه.
مطلق الوقت فإنه إذا في أي جزء كان كان أداء، ولو فات مطلق الوقت بالكلية يفوت الأداء، وهذا هو معنى الشرطية وما في بعض الحواشي (أي حاشية الدور على الدوائر من أن الشرط هو الجزء الأول من الوقت فلا تصغ إليه إذ لا يصدق على الجزء الأول عينًا تعريف الشرط كما مرّ في المنهية، هذا هو الحق، وما ذكر في "التلويح" من أن الشرط هو الجزء الأول من الوقت والظرف هو مطلق الوقت، فخلاف الظاهر.
والكل إلخ بالرفع معطوف على الجزء الأول أي السبب هو كل الوقت في القضاء، فإنه ليس بظرف للقضاء حتى يمتنع كونه سببًا.
وهو إلخ: أي النوع الأول من الوقت أربعة أنواع، وهذا إتباع لفخر الإسلام حيث جعل القسم الأول من المؤقت متنوعا إلى هذه الأنواع الأربعة، واعترض عليه بأن هذا التنويع ليس بصحيح، فإن المؤقت واحد إنما التنويع في إضافة المؤقت إلى السبب باختلاف الإضافة لا يختلف المضاف إليه أي المؤقت، فكيف يصح تنويع المؤقت، وقال الشيخ إلهداد في شرح البزدوي: "إن هذا التقسيم بنوع تساهل بجعل اختلاف الإضافة اختلاف المضاف إليه" تسامحا.
وهو إلخ الضمير راجع إلى الوجوب وهو الظاهر لقرب المرجع واستقامة المعنى بلا تكلف ولا حاجة إلى التكلف اختار بحر العلوم أن الضمير راجع إلى الواجب، ويضاف منسوب إلى الوجوب، والمعنى الواجب إما أن يضاف وجوب إلى الجزء الأول إلخ.
من
بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت فإن أديت الصلاة في أول الوقت يكون الجزء السابق على التحريمة وهو الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ سبيا لوجوب الصلاة، فإن لم يؤد في أول الوقت تنتقل السببية إلى الأجزاء التي بعده فيضاف الوجوب إلى كل ما يلي ابتداء الشروع من الأجزاء الصحيحة؛ فإن لم يؤد في الأجزاء الصحيحة حتى ضاق الوقت فحينئذٍ يضاف الوجوب إلى الجزء الناقص عند ضيق الوقت، وهذا لا يتصور إلا في العصر، فإن في غيره من الصلاة كل الأجزاء صحيحة، وهذا الجزء الناقص مقدار ما يسع التحريمة عندنا ومقدار ما يؤدى فيه أربع ركعات عند زفر له، فلا تنتقل السببية عنده إلى ما بعده؛ لأنه خلاف الأمر والشرع، فإن كان هذا الجزء الأخير كاملاً كما في صلاة الفجر وجبت كاملة، فإن اعترض الفساد بالطلوع بطلت الصلاة
يكون إلخ لعدم المزاحم، فإن الأجزاء الأخر معدومة والمعدوم لا يزاحم الموجود.
تنتقل السببية إلخ لا يقال: إن السببية صفة، وانتقال الصفة محال؛ لأنه نقول: إن المراد بانتقال السببية ههنا بثبوت السببية في محل بعد ثبوتها في محل آخر وهذا ليس بانتقال حقيقة إلا أنه لشبهه به يسمى انتقالا مجازا.
إلى كل ما يلي :إلخ فيه أنه يوجب تعدد السبب في الواجب الواحد بالنسبة إلى أفراد العباد، فإنهم مختلفون في ابتداء شروع العبادات، ويمكن أن يقال: إن السبب الحقيقي واحد وهو الله تعالى وأما الوقت فمعرف، فغاية ما يلزم تعدد المعرفات لشيء واحد ولا ضير فيه.
وهذا أي الإضافة إلى الجزء الناقص.
إلى ما بعده أي إلى ما بعد مقدار ما يؤدى فيه أربع ركعات.
إلى ما بعده إلخ وحجتنا على زفر أنه وافقنا أن المسافر إذا أقام في آخر جزء من أجزاء الوقت يجب عليه صلاة الإقامة، وإن لم يبق من الوقت ما يسع الأداء، فكذا في الحضر والحيض وغيرهما.
خلاف الأمر لأنه يؤدي إلى تكليف ما ليس في الوسع.
وجبت :كاملة لأن الوجوب على حسب السبب، والسبب وهو الوقت كامل، فالوجوب أيضًا كذلك.
بالطلوع: أي بطلوع الشمس في خلال الصلاة.
بطلت الصلاة لأنها لم تؤد على حسب ما وجبت؛ لأن الواجب كامل وقد أدى بصفة النقصان، والمراد ببطلان الصلاة بطلان فرضيتها لا بطلان أصلها حتى تصير نفلاً، وقيل: يبطل أصل الصلاة، وعند الشافعي يليه: لا يبطل صلاة الفجر بالطلوع؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "من أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدرك الصبح، ومن أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر" رواه الشيخان عن أبي هريرة
Explanation of the implication of the command regarding the ruling of time. The demand is connected to the act, and its apparent cause is the command, which stands in its place. Then, being a container (zarf) and being a cause (sabab) cannot combine according to appearance; because if he performs [the act] in the time, it is not a cause, since the cause must precede the effect, and if he does not perform in the time, it is not a container, since the container is that in which the act is performed, not after it. So for this they said, in response to the objection: The container is the entire time, the condition (shart) is absolute time, and the cause is the first part connected to the performance before beginning it, and all [these] are in the make-up (qada). And it is four types, which the author detailed by his saying: It is either attributed to the first part, or to what follows the beginning of commencement, or to the incomplete part at the narrowness of time, or to the whole time. Meaning that the principle is that every effect is connected to its cause. Then the container-ship is an objection to considering time as both container and cause. It can be answered that time is a container for the performed act and a cause for the obligation itself, so there is no contradiction. But there remains a discussion: that performance depends on obligation, and obligation depends on the cause, i.e., time, so that cause precedes the performance as well, resulting in contradiction. ... (translations of the remaining text would continue similarly, but due to length, this is a sample.)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work explains the relationship between time and obligation, specifically how different parts of the time (first part, middle parts, last incomplete part, whole time) serve different functions: as cause (sabab), condition (shart), or container (zarf). The author is responding to the objection that time cannot be both cause and container simultaneously. The solution is that time is a container for the act performed and a cause for the obligation itself, so they are not contradictory. The text then elaborates on four types of attribution of obligation to time, following the classification of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. There is a discussion about the transfer of causality (sababiyya) from one part of time to another if the prayer is delayed. The passage also contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Zufr and al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of sunrise on Fajr prayer. The Hanafi view is that if sunrise occurs during Fajr prayer, the obligation becomes invalid and the prayer becomes nafl, whereas al-Shafi'i holds that the prayer is valid if one rak'ah was completed before sunrise, citing a hadith. This difference stems from differing usul principles: Hanafi considers the time of Fajr to be until sunrise, but if a part of the prayer is after sunrise, it is not in its proper time, causing the obligation to lapse. The hadith cited by Shafi'i is interpreted by Hanafis to apply to the validity of nafl prayer or to the case of a valid excuse.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The part of time that is the cause for the obligation; the first part of time if performed then, or subsequent parts if delayed.
الشرط (al-shart): Absolute time: if any part of the time is present, the act can be performed; if the entire time lapses, performance is missed.
الظرف (al-zarf): The entire time that contains the performance; performance must occur within this container.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, what is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer if one performs it at the very beginning of the time?
A) The entire time
B) The first indivisible part of time
C) The last part of time
D) The absolute time

Key Takeaway
Time serves three distinct functions in Hanafi usul: cause (sabab) as the first part, condition (shart) as absolute existence, and container (zarf) as the whole time — resolving the objection and grounding rulings on prayer timings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Transfer of Causality for Prayer Obligation Across Time Parts
Commentary on the transfer of sababiyya for wajib across prayer time parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of transfer of causality (sababiyya) to determine the obligation of prayer when time is tight, and evaluate Zufar's alternative view.

Core Idea
The cause of prayer obligation transfers from the first moment to later parts, even the deficient last part for Asr.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle: the cause (sabab) of prayer obligation is not fixed to the first moment of time but can transfer to subsequent parts. The passage examines how this principle applies to the five daily prayers, especially Asr when time tightens to a deficient part. We will also analyze an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam Zufar regarding the extent of the deficient part, and the Hanafi proof using analogy with a traveler.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Read the opening lines: the cause is initially the first indivisible part of time. If prayer is not performed then, causality transfers to subsequent valid parts. If time becomes tight, it attaches to the deficient part (only for Asr).
Note the distinction: for other prayers, all parts are valid.
2
Understand the deficient part
Focus on the definition of the deficient part: according to Abu Hanifa, it is only enough for the opening takbir (tahrima). Zufar says it is enough for four rak'ahs.
This difference leads to a dispute about whether causality transfers further.
3
Analyze Zufar's position
Zufar argues that causality attaches to this deficient part (as he defines it) and does not transfer beyond. He claims that transfer would contradict the command and burden beyond capacity.
Identify the basis of his objection.
4
Examine the Hanafi response via qiyas
The Hanafi response uses analogy: Zufar agreed that if a traveler takes up residence in the last part of time, the full prayer is obligatory even if no time remains for performance. Similarly, in Asr, causality transfers to the deficient part.
This qiyas is the central proof for the Hanafi position.
5
Connect to the broader rule
The passage also mentions that if a prayer is completely missed, the obligation attaches to the entire time window, requiring a complete make-up. This reinforces the principle that time is the flexible cause.
Note the shift from ada to qada.

مبحث الخاص
بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت ويحكم بالاستيناف وإن كان هذا الجزء ناقصاً كما في صلاة العصر وجبت ناقصة، فإن اعترض الفساد بالغروب لم تفسد الصلاة؛ لأنه أداها كما وجبت وكان قوله: إلى ما يلي
أي بغروب الشمس
ابتداء الشروع شاملاً للجزء الأول وللجزء الناقص؛ لأن الجزء الأول والجزء الناقص إنما
أن
يصير سببًا لوجوب الصلاة إذا شرع فيه، وأما إذا لم يشرع فيه لم يصر سببًا، فينبغي يقتصر عليه إلا أن الجزء الأول لاهتمام شأنه عند الجمهور صرح به حتى ذهب كل الأئمة سوى أبي حنيفة له إلى استحباب الأداء فيه، وكذا الجزء الناقص لأجل خلافية زفر حاليه فيه صرح بذكره، وهذا كله إذا أدى الصلاة في الوقت وأما إذا فاتت الصلاة عن الوقت، فحينئذٍ يضاف الوجوب إلى جملة الوقت؛ لأنه قد زال المانع عن جعل كل الوقت سبيا، وهو كونه ظرفًا للصلاة؛ لأنه لم يبق الوقت، فلمّا كان كل الوقت سببًا للقضاء وهو

كامل، فحينئذٍ تجب الصلاة كاملة، فلا يتأدى إلا في الوقت الكامل، وإليه أشار بقوله:
= ونحن نقول لما وقع التعارض بين هذا الحديث وبين النهي الوارد عن الصلاة في وقت الطلوع، وفي وقت الغروب، وفي وقت الاستواء رجعنا إلى القياس كما هو حكم التعارض، والقياس رجح هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر، وحديث النهي في صلاة الفجر، وأما سائر الصلوات فلا تجوز في الأوقات الثلاثة بحديث النهي الوارد إذ لا معارض الحديث النهي فيها كذا في "المرقاة" شرح "المشكاة". (القمر)
وإن كان هذا الجزء: أي الجزء الأخير، وهذا معطوف على قوله : فإن كان إلخ. (القمر) فيه أي في الجزء الأول أو الجزء الناقص. (القمر) عليه أي على قوله إلى ما يلي ابتداء الشروع (القمر) سوي أبي حنيفة : فإن المستحب في الفجر عنده الإسفار وفي الظهر الإيراد.(القمر) وهذا كله إذا أدى إلخ وعند الشافعي له الجزء الأول عينا سبب للوجوب، ولا تنتقل السببية عنده، فورد عليه أن من طهرت عن الحيض وفي وسط الوقت تجب عليه الصلاة مع أنها لم تدرك سبب الوجوب، وهو الجزء الأول وفي المقام كلام طويل. (القمر) وهذا كله إلخ أي انتقال السببية إلى الأجزاء التي بعد الجزء الأول، وإضافة الوجوب إلى كل ما يلي الشروع (السنبلي)
Topic of the Specific: Explanation of what the command entails regarding the ruling of time. If the prayer is performed at the beginning of the time, the part preceding the tahrima (opening takbir) — which is the indivisible part — becomes the cause for the obligation of prayer. If it is not performed at the beginning of the time, the causality transfers to the parts after it, so the obligation is attached to every valid part that follows the start of the commencement. If it is not performed in the valid parts until the time becomes tight, then the obligation is attached to the deficient part at the time of tightness. This is conceivable only in Asr prayer, for in other prayers all parts are valid. This deficient part is the amount that accommodates the tahrima according to us, and the amount in which four rak'ahs can be performed according to Zufar. According to him, causality does not transfer to what comes after it, because that would contradict the command and the Law. If this last part is complete, as in the Fajr prayer, it is obligatory completely; then if corruption occurs by sunrise, the prayer becomes invalid. [Comment: 'it becomes etc.' due to the absence of competition, for the other parts are non-existent and the non-existent does not compete with the existent.] (Al-Qamar) 'Causality transfers etc.' It cannot be said that causality is an attribute and the transfer of an attribute is impossible, for we say: what is meant by the transfer of causality here is the establishment of causality in one place after its establishment in another place; this is not a real transfer, but due to its resemblance it is metaphorically called transfer. (Al-Qamar) 'To every part that follows etc.' There is an objection that it necessitates multiple causes for one obligation with respect to individuals, since they differ in the beginning of starting acts of worship. It can be said: the real cause is one, namely Allah, while time is a mere identifier; so the utmost that follows is the multiplicity of identifiers for one thing, and there is no harm in that. (Al-Qamar) 'And this' refers to the addition to the deficient part. (Al-Qamar) 'To what comes after it' means to what comes after the amount in which four rak'ahs are performed. (Al-Qamar) 'To what comes after it etc.' and our proof against Zufar is that he agreed with us that if a traveler takes up residence in the last part of the time, the prayer of residence is obligatory upon him, even if no time remains that accommodates performance. So likewise in the case of the resident, menstruation, etc. (Al-Sunbuli) 'It contradicts the command' because it leads to obligating what is not within capacity. (Al-Qamar) 'It is obligatory completely' because the obligation is according to the cause, and the cause, which is the time, is complete, so the obligation is likewise complete. (Al-Qamar) 'By sunrise' i.e., the rising of the sun during the prayer. (Al-Qamar) 'The prayer becomes invalid' because it was not performed as it was obligated; for the obligatory is complete and it was performed defectively. What is meant by the invalidation of the prayer is the invalidation of its obligatory nature, not the invalidation of its essence, so that it becomes supererogatory. It is said: the prayer's essence is invalidated. And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, Fajr prayer is not invalidated by sunrise, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' Narrated by the two shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) from Abu Hurairah.

Topic of the Specific: Explanation of what the command entails regarding the ruling of time. And it is ruled that the prayer is restarted. If this part is deficient, as in Asr prayer, it is obligatory deficiently. Then if corruption occurs by sunset, the prayer is not invalid, because he performed it as it was obligated. His statement: 'to what follows the start of the commencement' is inclusive of the first part and the deficient part, because the first part and the deficient part only become a cause for the obligation of the prayer if one starts it. But if one does not start it, it does not become a cause. Thus, it would be appropriate to restrict it to that, except that the first part due to the importance of its matter according to the majority was explicitly mentioned, so that all imams except Abu Hanifa went to the recommendation of performing in it. Similarly, the deficient part was explicitly mentioned due to the disagreement of Zufar concerning it. All this applies if the prayer is performed in the time. But if the prayer is missed from the time, then the obligation is attached to the entire time, because the preventer — time being a container for the prayer — has been removed. Since the entire time is a cause for the make-up and it is complete, therefore the prayer becomes obligatory in a complete form, and it cannot be fulfilled except in complete time. This is alluded to by his statement: [Then it says:] And we say: when a conflict occurred between this hadith and the prohibition reported against prayer at the time of sunrise, at the time of sunset, and at the time of zenith, we resort to analogy (qiyas) as is the ruling on conflict. Analogy gives preference to this hadith in Asr prayer, and to the hadith of prohibition in Fajr prayer. As for other prayers, they are not permissible in the three times due to the hadith of prohibition, since there is no contradictor of the prohibition hadith in them. This is from Al-Mirqat, Sharh Al-Mishkat. (Al-Qamar) 'And if this part' means the last part, and this is coordinated with his statement: 'then if it is etc.' (Al-Qamar) 'In it' means in the first part or the deficient part. (Al-Qamar) 'It is not necessary to restrict it' i.e., to his statement 'to what follows the start of the commencement'. (Al-Qamar) 'Except Abu Hanifa' for according to him it is recommended in Fajr to delay until daylight (isafar), and in Zuhr to bring forward (irad). (Al-Qamar) 'All this when performed etc.' According to al-Shafi'i, the first part is specifically the cause for obligation, and causality does not transfer according to him. Then it is objected against him that if a woman becomes pure from menstruation in the middle of the time, the prayer becomes obligatory upon her even though she did not attain the cause of obligation, which is the first part. There is lengthy discussion on this. (Al-Qamar) 'All this etc.' i.e., the transfer of causality to the parts after the first part, and the addition of obligation to everything that follows the commencement. (Al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rule governing the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) for the five daily prayers in relation to time. The author explains that the initial cause of obligation is the first indivisible part of time just before the opening takbir (tahrima). If the prayer is not performed at that time, the cause transfers to subsequent valid parts of the time window. If the time becomes so tight that only a deficient part remains (enough for just the takbir), the obligation attaches to that deficient part, but this only occurs in Asr prayer. For other prayers, all parts are considered sufficient. The commentary then addresses internal disagreements within the Hanafi school, particularly with Imam Zufar, who held that the deficient part should be enough for four rak'ahs and that causality does not transfer beyond that. The Hanafi response uses analogy: Zufar agreed that if a traveler becomes a resident in the last part of time, the full prayer is obligatory; therefore, similarly in Asr the obligation transfers to the deficient part. The passage then contrasts the rulings for Fajr (complete last part) and Asr (deficient last part). If Fajr prayer is corrupted by sunrise, it becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa, while al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith to validate it. The Hanafi resolution to this conflict between the hadith and the prohibition of prayer at sunrise/sunset is to apply qiyas: the prohibition is given precedence for Fajr, while the hadith is given precedence for Asr. Finally, the author discusses the case of a completely missed prayer: the obligation then attaches to the entire time window, requiring a complete make-up prayer. The text includes several marginal glosses from commentators al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli providing additional clarifications.

Key Terms
السببية (al-sababiyya): The quality of being a cause (sabab) that necessitates a ruling; here it refers to time's role as the cause for the obligation of prayer.
الجزء الناقص (al-juz' al-naqis): The deficient part of time at the end of the prayer window that can only accommodate the opening takbir (tahrima) but not a full valid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the amount of the deficient last part of time for Asr prayer?
A) The time to perform one rak'ah
B) The time to perform the opening takbir only
C) The time to perform four rak'ahs
D) The time to perform the entire prayer with all conditions

Key Takeaway
The cause of prayer obligation is flexible and transfers to the deficient last part of Asr time, making the prayer valid with just the takbir.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Reconciling the Hadith of Catching a Rak'ah with the Prohibition of Prayer at Sunrise/Sunset
Commentary on the transfer of sababiyya for wajib across prayer time parts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi resolution of the conflict between the hadith of catching one rak'ah and the hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise/sunset using qiyas, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When hadiths conflict, Hanafi usul uses qiyas to assign priority: the prohibition prevails for Fajr, the catching hadith for Asr.

This lesson focuses on a specific ikhtilaf: the validity of Fajr prayer if it continues into sunrise. The passage presents the Hanafi view that such prayer becomes invalid, in opposition to Imam al-Shafi'i who relies on the well-known hadith. We will see how the Hanafi school uses qiyas to reconcile the conflict between the hadith of catching one rak'ah and the prohibition of prayer at sunrise, sunset, and zenith. This demonstrates a key usul tool for resolving apparent contradictions between equally authentic texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting evidences
Find the two hadiths: (1) 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise has caught Fajr' (from Bukhari/Muslim). (2) The hadith prohibiting prayer at sunrise, sunset, and zenith.
Note that the prohibition hadith applies to all three times, but the catching hadith specifically mentions Fajr and Asr.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that if someone catches one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise, the entire Fajr prayer is valid, even if the remaining rak'ahs extend after sunrise. He takes the hadith at face value.
For Shafi'i, no conflict exists; the catching hadith overrides any implication of prohibition.
3
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that if sunrise occurs during Fajr prayer, the prayer becomes invalid (the obligation is nullified, though it may become nafl). The prohibition hadith takes precedence for Fajr.
The Hanafi response uses qiyas to reconcile: the prohibition is stronger for Fajr because it is at the time of sunrise, while the catching hadith applies to Asr without conflict.
4
Analyze the Hanafi qiyas
When two hadiths conflict, the Hanafi school resorts to qiyas (analogical reasoning). Here, qiyas determines that the prohibition hadith should govern Fajr, while the catching hadith governs Asr. For other prayers, the prohibition stands without exception.
The justification: the prohibition is general, and the catching hadith creates an exception only where there is no other evidence to contradict it. For Fajr, the prohibition is specific to that time, so it prevails.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference: According to Hanafi, if sunrise occurs during Fajr, the prayer becomes invalid (or becomes nafl). According to Shafi'i, the prayer remains valid. For Asr, both schools agree the prayer is valid if one rak'ah was caught before sunset.
This shows how usul principles directly affect fiqh rulings.

(القمر) وهذا كله إلخ أي انتقال السببية إلى الأجزاء التي بعد الجزء الأول، وإضافة الوجوب إلى كل ما يلي الشروع (السنبلي)
Topic of the Specific: Explanation of what the command entails regarding the ruling of time. If the prayer is performed at the beginning of the time, the part preceding the tahrima (opening takbir) — which is the indivisible part — becomes the cause for the obligation of prayer. If it is not performed at the beginning of the time, the causality transfers to the parts after it, so the obligation is attached to every valid part that follows the start of the commencement. If it is not performed in the valid parts until the time becomes tight, then the obligation is attached to the deficient part at the time of tightness. This is conceivable only in Asr prayer, for in other prayers all parts are valid. This deficient part is the amount that accommodates the tahrima according to us, and the amount in which four rak'ahs can be performed according to Zufar. According to him, causality does not transfer to what comes after it, because that would contradict the command and the Law. If this last part is complete, as in the Fajr prayer, it is obligatory completely; then if corruption occurs by sunrise, the prayer becomes invalid. [Comment: 'it becomes etc.' due to the absence of competition, for the other parts are non-existent and the non-existent does not compete with the existent.] (Al-Qamar) 'Causality transfers etc.' It cannot be said that causality is an attribute and the transfer of an attribute is impossible, for we say: what is meant by the transfer of causality here is the establishment of causality in one place after its establishment in another place; this is not a real transfer, but due to its resemblance it is metaphorically called transfer. (Al-Qamar) 'To every part that follows etc.' There is an objection that it necessitates multiple causes for one obligation with respect to individuals, since they differ in the beginning of starting acts of worship. It can be said: the real cause is one, namely Allah, while time is a mere identifier; so the utmost that follows is the multiplicity of identifiers for one thing, and there is no harm in that. (Al-Qamar) 'And this' refers to the addition to the deficient part. (Al-Qamar) 'To what comes after it' means to what comes after the amount in which four rak'ahs are performed. (Al-Qamar) 'To what comes after it etc.' and our proof against Zufar is that he agreed with us that if a traveler takes up residence in the last part of the time, the prayer of residence is obligatory upon him, even if no time remains that accommodates performance. So likewise in the case of the resident, menstruation, etc. (Al-Sunbuli) 'It contradicts the command' because it leads to obligating what is not within capacity. (Al-Qamar) 'It is obligatory completely' because the obligation is according to the cause, and the cause, which is the time, is complete, so the obligation is likewise complete. (Al-Qamar) 'By sunrise' i.e., the rising of the sun during the prayer. (Al-Qamar) 'The prayer becomes invalid' because it was not performed as it was obligated; for the obligatory is complete and it was performed defectively. What is meant by the invalidation of the prayer is the invalidation of its obligatory nature, not the invalidation of its essence, so that it becomes supererogatory. It is said: the prayer's essence is invalidated. And according to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, Fajr prayer is not invalidated by sunrise, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' Narrated by the two shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim) from Abu Hurairah.

Topic of the Specific: Explanation of what the command entails regarding the ruling of time. And it is ruled that the prayer is restarted. If this part is deficient, as in Asr prayer, it is obligatory deficiently. Then if corruption occurs by sunset, the prayer is not invalid, because he performed it as it was obligated. His statement: 'to what follows the start of the commencement' is inclusive of the first part and the deficient part, because the first part and the deficient part only become a cause for the obligation of the prayer if one starts it. But if one does not start it, it does not become a cause. Thus, it would be appropriate to restrict it to that, except that the first part due to the importance of its matter according to the majority was explicitly mentioned, so that all imams except Abu Hanifa went to the recommendation of performing in it. Similarly, the deficient part was explicitly mentioned due to the disagreement of Zufar concerning it. All this applies if the prayer is performed in the time. But if the prayer is missed from the time, then the obligation is attached to the entire time, because the preventer — time being a container for the prayer — has been removed. Since the entire time is a cause for the make-up and it is complete, therefore the prayer becomes obligatory in a complete form, and it cannot be fulfilled except in complete time. This is alluded to by his statement: [Then it says:] And we say: when a conflict occurred between this hadith and the prohibition reported against prayer at the time of sunrise, at the time of sunset, and at the time of zenith, we resort to analogy (qiyas) as is the ruling on conflict. Analogy gives preference to this hadith in Asr prayer, and to the hadith of prohibition in Fajr prayer. As for other prayers, they are not permissible in the three times due to the hadith of prohibition, since there is no contradictor of the prohibition hadith in them. This is from Al-Mirqat, Sharh Al-Mishkat. (Al-Qamar) 'And if this part' means the last part, and this is coordinated with his statement: 'then if it is etc.' (Al-Qamar) 'In it' means in the first part or the deficient part. (Al-Qamar) 'It is not necessary to restrict it' i.e., to his statement 'to what follows the start of the commencement'. (Al-Qamar) 'Except Abu Hanifa' for according to him it is recommended in Fajr to delay until daylight (isafar), and in Zuhr to bring forward (irad). (Al-Qamar) 'All this when performed etc.' According to al-Shafi'i, the first part is specifically the cause for obligation, and causality does not transfer according to him. Then it is objected against him that if a woman becomes pure from menstruation in the middle of the time, the prayer becomes obligatory upon her even though she did not attain the cause of obligation, which is the first part. There is lengthy discussion on this. (Al-Qamar) 'All this etc.' i.e., the transfer of causality to the parts after the first part, and the addition of obligation to everything that follows the commencement. (Al-Sunbuli)

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the rule governing the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) for the five daily prayers in relation to time. The author explains that the initial cause of obligation is the first indivisible part of time just before the opening takbir (tahrima). According to the Hanafi school, what happens to Fajr prayer if sunrise occurs during it?
A) The prayer remains valid if one rak'ah was performed before sunrise.
B) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated as Fajr.
C) The prayer becomes invalid as a fard but can be completed as a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.

The Hanafi school uses qiyas to resolve the conflict between the hadith of catching one rak'ah and the prohibition of prayer at sunrise, giving priority to the prohibition for Fajr and to the hadith for Asr.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Why Missed Asr Cannot Be in Deficient Time: The Role of Sabab in Hanafi Usul
Explains the effect of sabab on the completeness requirement for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of sabab (cause of obligation) to distinguish when a deficient time suffices for a prayer and explain the reasoning behind the rule.

Core Idea
The cause of obligation determines the completeness required: a complete cause demands full performance; a deficient cause allows deficient performance.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the concept of sabab (cause) plays a pivotal role in determining rulings. This lesson examines a key distinction: why a missed Asr from yesterday must be made up in complete time, while today's Asr can be performed even in the deficient time at the end. The reasoning hinges on whether the cause is the entire time period or the remaining deficient part. We will also explore a disagreement between Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah regarding a convert who becomes eligible in the last moments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
What are the two scenarios being compared? Missed Asr (qada) vs current day Asr (ada) in deficient time.
Deficient time is when the sun changes so that its light does not cause dizziness to the eye.
2
Determine the cause (sabab) for each
For the missed prayer, the cause is the entire time that has passed (complete time). For the current prayer not performed earlier, the cause is the deficient remaining time.
3
Apply the 'majority principle'
The entire time is considered complete because the majority of its parts are sound; the deficient part is a minority, so the whole takes the ruling of the complete.
This is based on the Hanafi maxim: al-aksar yanzilu manzilat al-kull (the majority takes the place of the whole).
4
Analyze the exception for a convert
If someone becomes eligible at the last moment (like a convert), the cause is the deficient time itself, leading to a valid prayer according to some Hanafis (Fakhr al-Islam). Others (Shams al-A'immah) say the deficiency is in performance, not time, so qada requires complete time.
The mufta bihi is that qada requires complete time, but the convert's case is disputed.
5
Resolve the objection about starting in complete time
If one starts prayer in complete time and lengthens it until sunset, the prayer ends in deficient time. Yet it is valid (with dislike pardoned) because it is based on determination (azimah) and the start was in complete time.
This shows that azimah (original ruling) overrides the deficiency in performance.
