مبحث الخاص
بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت
فلهذا لا يتأدى عصر أمسه في الوقت الناقص بخلاف عصر يومه يعني فلأجل أن وجوب عصر اليوم هو الوقت الناقص إذا لم يؤده في الأجزاء الصحيحة، وسبب وجوب عصر الأمس هو كل الوقت الفائت الكامل، قلنا: لا يتأدى عصر الأمس في الوقت الناقص؛ لأنه لما فاتت الصلاة عن الوقت كان كل الوقت سببا وهو كامل باعتبار كل الوقت أكثر أجزائه وإن كان يشتمل على الوقت الناقص فلا يصح قضاؤه إلا في الوقت الكامل ويتأدى عصر يومه في الوقت الناقص؛ لأنه لما لم يؤده في الوقت الأول واتصل شروعه في الجزء الناقص كان هو سببًا لوجوبه فيؤدي ناقصا كما وجب، ولا يقال: إن من شرع صلاة العصر في أول الوقت ثم مدّها بالتعديل والتطويل إلى أن غربت الشمس، فإن هذه الصلاة قد تمت ناقصة وكان شروعها في الوقت الكامل؛ لأنا نقول: إنما يلزم هذا ضرورة.
الوقت الناقص: أي وقت تغير قرص الشمس بحيث يصير ضوؤها بحال لا يحصل للبصر بالنظر إليه حيرة كذا قيل.(القمر) الفائت الكامل: أي باعتبار أكثر الأجزاء، وللأكثر حكم الكل، فلا تصغ إلى من قال: إن السبب وهو كل الوقت ناقص بنقصان بعض الأجزاء. (القمر) لا يتأدى إلخ هذا في حق من كان أهلاً في جميع وقت عصر الأمس، وأما من حديث أهلية في آخر الوقت كمن كان كافرًا، وأسلم في آخر وقت عصر الأمس، فالسبب له الأمس في الوقت الآخر من اليوم كذا ذكره أعظم العلماء آخر الوقت وهو ناقص، فيصح منه أداء عصر ه تبعا لفخر الإسلام، وأما شمس الأئمة فجزم بعدم الصحة وقال إنه لا نقصان في الوقت نفسه، بل في الأداء في ذلك الوقت الأخير فيتحمل هذا النقصان في الأداء لشرف الأداء، ولا يتحمل في القضاء، فيجب القضاء في الوقت الكامل. (القمر) كان هو إلخ: أي كان الجزء الناقص سببًا لوجوب عصر اليوم.(القمر) كما وجب لأنه وجب ناقصًا لنقصان سببه . (القمر) ولا يقال إلخ اعتراض على ما تقرر من أن ما وجب كاملاً لا يتأدى بصفة النقصان. (القمر) إلى أن غربت الشمس: أي قبل الفراغ من صلاة العصر. (القمر) وكان شروعها إلخ أي ومع هذا يقولون إنه لا يفسد صلاته، فأجاب بأنه إنما يلزم هذا ضرورة ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن العزيمة في كل الصلاة أداؤها في جميع الوقت؛ لأن كون العبد مشغولا بخدمة المولى في جميع الأوقات هو الأصل لاسيما في أوقات الصلاة. (السنبلي) فجعل هذا القدر من الكراهة عفوًا.
Discussion of the specific. Explanation of the effect of the command in the ruling of time. For this reason, yesterday's Asr is not performed in the deficient time, unlike today's Asr. That is because the obligation of today's Asr is the deficient time if not performed in the sound parts, while the cause of yesterday's Asr obligation is the entire complete time. So we say: yesterday's Asr is not performed in the deficient time because when the prayer was missed from its time, the entire time became the cause and it is complete considering the majority of parts, even if it includes the deficient time. So it is not valid to make it up except in complete time. And today's Asr is performed in the deficient time because when he did not perform it in the first time and his beginning connected in the deficient part, that part became the cause for its obligation, so he performs it deficient as it was obligated. And it is not said: whoever begins Asr at the beginning of time and extends it slowly until sunset, this prayer ended deficient while its start was in complete time because we say: this is necessitated by determination. Deficient time: meaning the time when the sun's disc changes so that its light is such that the eye cannot look at it without dizziness. (Al-Qamar) The complete missed time: meaning by consideration of the majority of parts, and the majority has the ruling of the whole, so do not listen to those who say that the cause, which is the entire time, is deficient due to deficiency of some parts. (Al-Qamar) 'Not performed' etc. applies to one who was eligible for the entire time of yesterday's Asr. But regarding one who becomes eligible at the end of the time, like a disbeliever who converts to Islam at the end of yesterday's Asr time, the cause for him is the last part of the day, which is deficient. So it is valid for him to perform it, following Fakhr al-Islam. But Shams al-A'immah definitely ruled it invalid, saying there is no deficiency in the time itself, but in performance at that last time, so this deficiency in performance is tolerated for the honor of performance but not for making up, so making up must be in complete time. (Al-Qamar) 'That part became' etc.: meaning the deficient part became the cause for the obligation of today's Asr. (Al-Qamar) 'As it was obligated' because it was obligated deficient due to deficiency of its cause. (Al-Qamar) 'And it is not said' etc. is an objection to what was established: that what is obligated completely is not performed with deficiency. (Al-Qamar) 'Until sunset' meaning before finishing Asr prayer. (Al-Qamar) 'And its start' etc. meaning despite this they say his prayer is not invalid, and he answered that this is necessitated by it being based on determination, for determination in every prayer is to perform it in all the time; because the slave being busy with the master's service all times is the original, especially in prayer times. (Al-Sunbuli) So this amount of dislike is pardoned.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the discussion of 'specific' (al-khas) in usul al-fiqh, explaining the effect of the command on the ruling of time for prayer. It addresses why the missed Asr of yesterday cannot be performed in the deficient time (when the sun has changed), while the current day's Asr can. The reasoning is based on the cause (sabab) of obligation: for the missed prayer, the cause is the entire complete time (the whole time period, considered complete by majority), so it must be made up in complete time. For the current day's Asr, if not performed at the start, the deficient part itself becomes the cause, so it is performed deficient. The text also addresses a potential objection: if one starts prayer in complete time and extends it into deficient time, the prayer is valid because it is based on determination (azimah), and a slight dislike is pardoned. Also, a dispute between Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'immah is noted for a convert: Fakhr al-Islam holds that the last part of time is the cause and is deficient, so the prayer is valid; Shams al-A'immah says the deficiency is in performance, not time, so it is not valid for making up.

Key Terms
الوقت الناقص (al-waqt al-naqis): The deficient time: the time when the sun's disc changes so that its light does not cause dizziness to the eye.
الوقت الكامل (al-waqt al-kamil): The complete time: the entire time period, considered complete by the majority of parts, with the majority taking the ruling of the whole.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause of obligation; here, the time itself is the cause for prayer obligation.
العزيمة (al-azimah): Determination: the original ruling without consideration of excuses; performing the prayer in the entire time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can the missed Asr prayer from yesterday not be performed in the deficient time (when the sun has changed)?
A) Because the deficient time is not valid for any prayer.
B) Because the cause of obligation for the missed prayer is the entire complete time, and a complete cause requires a complete performance.
C) Because the person was not eligible for the deficient time.
D) Because the deficient time is only for voluntary prayers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the cause (sabab) determines the performance requirement: a missed prayer is caused by the entire complete time, so it requires complete time to make up; a current prayer can be performed in deficient time because its cause is the deficient part.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Specific Intention Required When Time is Common
Ruling with talil on specific intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) for obligatory prayer when the time is shared with voluntary prayers, and apply the talil (rationale) that the time's capacity for multiple prayers necessitates specification.

Core Idea
Specify your prayer intention when the time fits multiple prayers; general intention is invalid because the time is a 'container' for both obligation and supererogation.

This lesson presents the Hanafi usul rule that specific intention is required for the obligatory prayer when the time is suitable for both the timely obligation and other prayers. The text explains why absolute intention (mutaq al-niyyah) is not valid, and how the ruling is derived from the nature of time as a common container. Understanding this rule helps you grasp how the Hanafi school uses the concept of 'capacity of time' to determine the conditions of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying an obligatory prayer in a time that is ṣāliḥ (suitable) for both the obligatory prayer (waqtī) and other prayers like nafl or qaḍā. The ruling is that one must specify the intention (niyyat al-ta'yīn).
e.g., 'I intend to pray the noon prayer of today'.
2
Determine the underlying cause (ʿilla)
The cause for requiring specific intention is that the time is a container (ẓarf) that can accommodate multiple types of prayer. Without specification, the intention remains ambiguous, which invalidates the prayer.
The text says: 'لما كان الوقت ظرفًا صالحًا للوقتي وغيره'.
3
Understand the talīl (rationale)
The ruling is based on talīl: the condition is attached to the capacity of time. When capacity exists, specification is needed. This is a rational derivation (istidlāl) from the nature of prayer and time.
This is a Hanafi usul method: deriving 'illa from the text.
4
Distinguish from absolute intention
Absolute intention (mutaq al-niyya) is not sufficient because it does not indicate which prayer is intended when multiple prayers could be performed in that time.
The text says: 'ولا يصح مطلق النية'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكمه: اشتراط نية التعيين أي من حكم هذا القسم الذي هو ظرف اشتراط نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت أن أصلي ظهر اليوم ، ولا يصح مطلق النية؛ لأنه لما كان الوقت ظرفًا صالحًا للوقتي وغيره من النوافل، والقضاء يجب أن يعين النية. أي للصلاة الوقتية ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت أي إذا ضاق الوقت عن التوسعة بسبب تقصيره إلى آخر الوقت، أو بسبب نومه أو نسيانه لا يسقط التعيين عن ذمته؛ لأنه إنما جاء الضيق بسبب العارض، وفي الأصل كان سعة. كالنوم وأخواته. مجموعي: وجبت كاملة على العزيمة: اعلم أن الأحكام المشروعة على نوعين عزيمة وهي: اسم لما هو أصل غير متعلق بالعوارض، ورخصة وهو ما يكون شرعه باعتبار العارض. (القمر) في كل صلاة: الكل ههنا إفرادي، ومن فهم أن الكل فقد شطط تأمل. (القمر) أن يؤدي إلخ لتوارد نعم الله تعالى على العبد، وقد جعل له ولاية صرف بعض الأوقات إلى حوائج نفسه رخصته. (القمر) عفوًا لكن بقيت مناقشة وهو: أنه إذا شرع العصر في الوقت الكامل ومدها إلى أن دخل الوقت الناقص، وفرغ قبل آخر الوقت فإن هذه الصلاة جائزة مع أنها لكمال سببها، وقد أديت بصفة النقصان وليس ههنا بناء على العزيمة كما هو الظاهر فتأمل. (القمر) الذي هو ظرف فيه مسامحة، والأولى أن يقال: الذي وقته ظرف (القمر) بأن يقول إلخ: أو ينوي بقلبه معينًا.(القمر) ظهر اليوم فيه إيماء إلى أن المراد بالتعيين تعيين فرض الوقت، ولو نوى فرض الظهر لا يكفي، لأن فرض الظهر يكون أداء وقضاء، فلا يتعين الأداء إلا بذكر فرض الوقت كذا قال ابن الملك، وفي "مشكاة الأنوار": أن نية الظهر المقرون باليوم تعيين وإن خرج الوقت وكذا المقرون بالوقت إن لم يخرج الوقت وفرض الوقت كظهر الوقت، وإن نوى فرض الظهر ففي فتاوى العتابي الأصح أنه يجزئه؛ لأن كون الفائتة عليه محتمل ولا اعتبار به (القمر) ولا يسقط إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أنه لما كان اشتراط نية التعيين لعلّة كون الوقت صالحا للوقتي وغيره، فيلزم منه أن لا يكون نية التعيين شرطًا إذا ضاق الوقت؛ لأن العلة المذكورة هناك مفقود، فأجاب بأن هذا الضيق لا يعتد به لكونه عارضا؛ لأن الوقت في الأصل متوسع فيشترط نية التعيين في صورة الضيق أيضا باعتبار أصل الوقت. (السنبلي) إذا ضاق الوقت أي بحيث لا يسع إلا هذا الفرض (القمر)
Its ruling: The condition of specific intention. That is, from the ruling of this category which is a container, the condition of specific intention is that he says: 'I intend to pray the noon of today', and absolute intention is not valid because the time is a container suitable for the timely prayer and other voluntary prayers, and making up requires specifying the intention. For the timely prayer. And it does not fall due to narrowness of time: i.e., if time becomes too narrow for expansion due to his shortcoming until the end of time, or due to his sleep or forgetfulness, the specification does not fall from his responsibility; because the narrowness came only due to an incidental cause, while originally there was capacity. Like sleep and its likes. Totality: it was obligated complete upon determination. Know that the prescribed rulings are of two types: determination, which is the name for what is original not connected to incidental causes; and concession, which is what is legislated due to incidental causes. (Al-Qamar) In every prayer: 'every' here is individual, and whoever understands 'every' as all has gone far, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'That he perform' etc. because of the succession of Allah's blessings upon the slave, and He has given him the authority to spend some times for his own needs as a concession. (Al-Qamar) 'Pardoned' but there remains a discussion: that if one begins Asr in complete time and extends it until the deficient time enters, and finishes before the last time, this prayer is permissible even though for its complete cause it was performed with deficiency, and here there is no building on determination as is apparent, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'Which is a container' there is looseness, and it is better to say: whose time is a container. (Al-Qamar) 'That he says' etc.: or he intends with his heart specifically. (Al-Qamar) 'Noon of today' indicates that the intended specification is the specification of the obligatory prayer of the time. And if he intends 'the noon obligatory prayer', it is insufficient, because 'the noon obligatory prayer' can be both performance and makeup, so performance is not specified except by mentioning the obligatory prayer of the time. Thus said Ibn al-Malik. And in Mishkat al-Anwar: that the intention of noon coupled with 'today' is specification even if the time has left, and similarly coupled with 'time' if the time has not left, and 'obligatory prayer of the time' like 'the noon of the time'. And if he intends 'the noon obligatory prayer', in the Fatawa of al-Atabi, the soundest is that it suffices him; because the possibility of it being a missed prayer is merely probable and not considered. (Al-Qamar) 'And it does not fall' etc.: repelling an anticipated objection, its gist: since the condition of specific intention is due to the time being suitable for the timely and other prayers, it would follow that specific intention is not a condition when time is narrow, because the mentioned cause is absent. He answered that this narrowness is not regarded because it is incidental; for time originally is capacious, so specific intention is still required in the case of narrowness as well, by consideration of the original time. (Al-Sunbuli) 'When time becomes narrow': i.e., to the extent that it cannot hold except this obligatory prayer. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) for the obligatory prayer when the time is common to both the obligatory and voluntary prayers. The text states that one must explicitly intend, for example, 'I intend to pray the noon prayer of today', and a general intention is not valid. This is because the time is a container that can host both the timely obligation and voluntary prayers. The ruling also clarifies that this requirement does not fall away even if the time becomes so narrow that it only accommodates the obligatory prayer; because the narrowness is incidental, and the original ruling (capacity) is considered. The passage engages with various scholarly opinions: Ibn al-Malik holds that specifying the time (e.g., 'today') is necessary, while in Mishkat al-Anwar, coupling with 'today' or 'time' suffices; the Fatawa of al-Atabi considers intending 'the noon obligatory prayer' as sufficient. The commentary resolves a potential objection: if the condition of specific intention is because the time is common, then in narrow time when only one prayer fits, why is it still required? The answer: narrowness is incidental and does not change the original ruling.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Specific intention: to specify which prayer one intends, e.g., 'I intend to pray the noon prayer of today'.
الوقت الصالح (al-waqt al-salih): A time that is suitable for both the obligatory prayer of that time and other voluntary prayers or missed prayers.
ضيق الوقت (diq al-waqt): Narrowness of time: when the remaining time is barely enough for the obligatory prayer with its conditions.
العزيمة (al-azimah): Determination: the original ruling without concession

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is absolute intention (مطلق النية) not valid in a time that is ṣāliḥ (suitable) for both the timely prayer and other prayers?
A) Because the time is specific for the obligatory prayer only.
B) Because the time is a container that can hold multiple prayers, so specification is needed.
C) Because absolute intention is always invalid in any time.
D) Because the prayer must be offered with specific intention for it to be a valid obligation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions specific intention for obligatory prayer in common time because the time's capacity for multiple acts of worship necessitates specification; this condition does not fall due to incidental narrowness of time.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Narrow Time Does Not Lift the Requirement of Specific Intention
Expansion on the narrow time ruling and subsidiary discussions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school maintains the requirement of specific intention even in narrow time, distinguishing between original capacity and incidental narrowness, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences on the wording of intention.

Core Idea
Narrowness of time is incidental; the original capacity of time governs the ruling on intention specification.

This lesson builds on the previous one by examining the scenario when time becomes so narrow that only one prayer can fit. Some might argue that the requirement for specific intention drops because the cause (common time) is absent. The Hanafi response is that the narrowness is secondary and the original ruling (azimah) remains. This lesson also delves into the exact wording of intention and scholarly differences on what suffices, including views of Ibn al-Malik and al-Atabi.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection: if the condition of specific intention is due to the time being common, then when time is narrow (only one prayer fits), the condition should drop because the cause is gone.
2
Hanafi response: incidental narrowness
The narrowness is an accidental state (āriḍ) caused by the person's delay, sleep, or forgetfulness. The original time was capacious, so the original ruling (azimah) applies.
The text says: 'لأنه إنما جاء الضيق بسبب العارض، وفي الأصل كان سعة'.
3
Examine the azimah/rukhsah distinction
The text introduces the concept of azimah and rukhsah. Azimah is the original ruling without concessions; rukhsah is due to incidental causes. The narrowness does not create a rukhsah to drop specification.
The marginal note: 'وجبت كاملة على العزيمة'.
4
Review the specific wording of intention
The text discusses whether 'فرض الظهر' suffices or if one must say 'ظهر اليوم'. Ibn al-Malik requires mention of the time (today), while Mishkat al-Anwar considers coupling with 'today' or 'time' as sufficient. al-Atabi holds that intending the obligatory prayer of the time suffices.
These are ikhtilafat within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(السنبلي) إذا ضاق الوقت أي بحيث لا يسع إلا هذا الفرض (القمر)
Its ruling: The condition of specific intention. That is, from the ruling of this category which is a container, the condition of specific intention is that he says: 'I intend to pray the noon of today', and absolute intention is not valid because the time is a container suitable for the timely prayer and other voluntary prayers, and making up requires specifying the intention. For the timely prayer. And it does not fall due to narrowness of time: i.e., if time becomes too narrow for expansion due to his shortcoming until the end of time, or due to his sleep or forgetfulness, the specification does not fall from his responsibility; because the narrowness came only due to an incidental cause, while originally there was capacity. Like sleep and its likes. Totality: it was obligated complete upon determination. Know that the prescribed rulings are of two types: determination, which is the name for what is original not connected to incidental causes; and concession, which is what is legislated due to incidental causes. (Al-Qamar) In every prayer: 'every' here is individual, and whoever understands 'every' as all has gone far, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'That he perform' etc. because of the succession of Allah's blessings upon the slave, and He has given him the authority to spend some times for his own needs as a concession. (Al-Qamar) 'Pardoned' but there remains a discussion: that if one begins Asr in complete time and extends it until the deficient time enters, and finishes before the last time, this prayer is permissible even though for its complete cause it was performed with deficiency, and here there is no building on determination as is apparent, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'Which is a container' there is looseness, and it is better to say: whose time is a container. (Al-Qamar) 'That he says' etc.: or he intends with his heart specifically. (Al-Qamar) 'Noon of today' indicates that the intended specification is the specification of the obligatory prayer of the time. And if he intends 'the noon obligatory prayer', it is insufficient, because 'the noon obligatory prayer' can be both performance and makeup, so performance is not specified except by mentioning the obligatory prayer of the time. Thus said Ibn al-Malik. And in Mishkat al-Anwar: that the intention of noon coupled with 'today' is specification even if the time has left, and similarly coupled with 'time' if the time has not left, and 'obligatory prayer of the time' like 'the noon of the time'. And if he intends 'the noon obligatory prayer', in the Fatawa of al-Atabi, the soundest is that it suffices him; because the possibility of it being a missed prayer is merely probable and not considered. (Al-Qamar) 'And it does not fall' etc.: repelling an anticipated objection, its gist: since the condition of specific intention is due to the time being suitable for the timely and other prayers, it would follow that specific intention is not a condition when time is narrow, because the mentioned cause is absent. He answered that this narrowness is not regarded because it is incidental; for time originally is capacious, so specific intention is still required in the case of narrowness as well, by consideration of the original time. (Al-Sunbuli) 'When time becomes narrow': i.e., to the extent that it cannot hold except this obligatory prayer. (Al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of specific intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) for the obligatory prayer when the time is common to both the obligatory and voluntary prayers. The text states that one must explicitly intend, for example, 'I intend to pray the noon prayer of today', and a general intention is not valid. This is because the time is a container that can host both the timely obligation and voluntary prayers. The ruling also clarifies that this requirement does not fall away even if the time becomes so narrow that it only accommodates the obligatory prayer; because the narrowness is incidental, and the original ruling (capacity) is considered. The passage engages with various scholarly opinions: Ibn al-Malik holds that specifying the time (e.g., 'today') is necessary, while in Mishkat al-Anwar, coupling with 'today' or 'time' suffices; the Fatawa of al-Atabi considers intending 'the noon obligatory prayer' as sufficient. The commentary resolves a potential objection: if the condition of specific intention is because the time is common, then in narrow time when only one prayer fits, why is it still required? The answer: narrowness is incidental and does not change the original ruling.

Key Terms
العزيمة (al-azimah): Determination: the original ruling without concession
الرخصة (al-rukhsah): Concession: a ruling legislated due to incidental causes
عارض (arid): Incidental cause that does not change the original ruling
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer of the current time (e.g., Fajr, Dhuhr, etc.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does the narrowness of time not lift the requirement of specific intention?
A) Because the weak (da'if) have special dispensations.
B) Because the narrowness is incidental, and the original capacity of time is considered.
C) Because narrowness never occurs in prayer times.
D) Because the prayer becomes invalid if intention is not specific.

Key Takeaway
The requirement of specific intention for obligatory prayer is based on the original capacity of time, not the current incidental narrowness; thus it remains even in tight situations.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
The Obligation of Specifying Intention in Expansive Time Prayers
Commentary on the ruling of time for prayers and specification of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that specifying intention is required for timed prayers and distinguish between time as container (zarf) and time as measure (mi'yar).

Core Idea
Specifying intention is required when time is a container; tightness does not drop the requirement.

In this commentary passage, the author establishes that for obligatory prayers like Zuhr, the devotee must specify the intention by saying 'I intend to pray Zuhr today'. This is because the time for such prayers is a 'container' that can accommodate both the obligation and supererogatory acts, as well as make-up prayers. Moreover, this specification is not waived even when time becomes tight due to personal negligence, as the original time is inherently expansive. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the Hanafi classification of time-bound obligations into 'container' and 'measure' categories, which directly affects the necessity of specifying intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Intention
Locate the statement in the Arabic that says 'اشتراط نية التعيين' (the condition of specifying intention). This is the core ruling for prayers whose time is a container.
The text specifies that absolute intention (مطلق النية) is invalid.
2
Understand the Reason: Time as Container
The passage explains that specification is needed because the time is 'ظرف' (a container) that can hold both the timed obligation and other prayers. Without specification, one does not know which prayer is intended.
Contrast with time as 'معيار' (measure) where no specification is needed, as in Ramadan fasting.
3
Analyze the Effect of Time Tightness
The text argues that tightness of time due to one's own fault, sleep, or forgetfulness does not drop the requirement of specifying intention. The original spaciousness of time is the basis.
This is because the tightness is 'عارض' (accidental) and does not change the original nature of the time.
4
Distinguish between 'Azima' and 'Rukhsah'
The passage defines 'azima (determination) as the foundational ruling not attached to accidents, and 'rukhsah (concession) as a ruling due to an accident. The specification requirement is part of 'azima.
This distinction helps in understanding why some concessions (like excusing slight dislike) do not affect the specification requirement.

بيان موجب الأمر في حكم الوقت ابتنائه على العزيمة، فإن العزيمة في كل صلاة أن يؤدي في تمام الوقت، فالاحتراز عن الكراهة مع الإقبال على العزيمة مما لا يجتمع قط، فجعل هذا القدر من الكراهة عفوًا. حكمه: اشتراط نية التعيين أي من حكم هذا القسم الذي هو ظرف اشتراط نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت أن أصلي ظهر اليوم ، ولا يصح مطلق النية؛ لأنه لما كان الوقت ظرفًا صالحًا للوقتي وغيره من النوافل، والقضاء يجب أن يعين النية.
ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت أي إذا ضاق الوقت عن التوسعة بسبب تقصيره إلى آخر الوقت، أو بسبب نومه أو نسيانه لا يسقط التعيين عن ذمته؛ لأنه إنما جاء الضيق بسبب العارض، وفي الأصل كان سعة.
مجموعي: وجبت كاملة على العزيمة: اعلم أن الأحكام المشروعة على نوعين عزيمة وهي: اسم لما هو أصل غير متعلق بالعوارض، ورخصة وهو ما يكون شرعه باعتبار العارض. (القمر) في كل صلاة : الكل ههنا إفرادي، ومن فهم أن الكل فقد شطط تأمل. (القمر) أن يؤدي إلخ لتوارد نعم الله تعالى على العبد، وقد جعل له ولاية صرف بعض الأوقات إلى حوائج نفسه رخصته. (القمر) عفوًا لكن بقيت مناقشة وهو: أنه إذا شرع العصر في الوقت الكامل ومدها إلى أن دخل الوقت الناقص، وفرغ قبل آخر الوقت فإن هذه الصلاة جائزة مع أنها لكمال سببها، وقد أديت بصفة النقصان وليس ههنا بناء على العزيمة كما هو الظاهر فتأمل. (القمر) الذي هو ظرف فيه مسامحة، والأولى أن يقال: الذي وقته ظرف (القمر) بأن يقول إلخ : أو ينوي بقلبه معينًا.(القمر) ظهر اليوم فيه إيماء إلى أن المراد بالتعيين تعيين فرض الوقت، ولو نوى فرض الظهر لا يكفي، لأن فرض الظهر يكون أداء وقضاء، فلا يتعين الأداء إلا بذكر فرض الوقت كذا قال ابن الملك، وفي "مشكاة الأنوار": أن نية الظهر المقرون باليوم تعيين وإن خرج الوقت وكذا المقرون بالوقت إن لم يخرج الوقت وفرض الوقت كظهر الوقت،
وإن نوى فرض الظهر ففي فتاوى العتابي الأصح أنه يجزئه؛ لأن كون الفائتة عليه محتمل ولا اعتبار به (القمر) ولا يسقط إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره أنه لما كان اشتراط نية التعيين لعلّة كون الوقت صالحا للوقتي وغيره، فيلزم منه أن لا يكون نية التعيين شرطًا إذا ضاق الوقت؛ لأن العلة المذكورة هناك مفقود، فأجاب بأن هذا الضيق لا يعتد به لكونه عارضا؛ لأن الوقت في الأصل متوسع فيشترط نية التعيين في صورة الضيق أيضا باعتبار أصل الوقت. (السنبلي) إذا ضاق الوقت أي بحيث لا يسع إلا هذا الفرض (القمر)
ولا يتعين بالتعيين إلا بالأداء أي إن عيّن أحد أول الوقت أو أوسطه، أو آخره لا يتعين بتعيينه اللساني أو القصدي إلا إذا أدى، ففي أي وقت أدى يكون ذلك الوقت متعينًا، وإن لم يؤد فيما عينه بل في جزء آخر لا يسمى قضاء.
كالحانث في اليمين، فإنه يتخير في كفارتها بين ثلاثة أشياء: إطعام عشرة مساكين، أو كسوتهم، أو تحرير رقبة، فإن عين واحدا منها باللسان أو بالقلب لا يتعين عند الله تعالى ما لم يؤده، فإذا أدى صار متعينًا، وإن أدى غير ما عينه أو لا يكون مؤديا.
لا يسمى قضاء: فإن الواجب في الموسع هو الأداء في جزء من الوقت وما قال بعض الشافعية: من أن الجزء الأول متعين للأداء، وفي غير الجزء الأول قضاء، وبعض الحنفية من أن الجزء الأخير متعين للأداء، فإن أدى في الأول يكون نفلاً يسقط به الفرض فخطأ، فإن الأمر وسع فكل جزء من أجزاء الوقت وقت لامتثال الأمر، فالتعيين بالأول أو بالأخير تضييق، وخلاف الأمر فتدبر. (القمر) فإنه يتخير في كفارتها إلخ وإذا لم يجد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة، فعليه صيام ثلاثة أيام كما ينطق به القرآن المجيد، فالخيار إنما هو في هذه الثلاثة لا فيها مع الصوم، فما في مسير" "الدائر" من أن الحانث مخير بين الإطعام والكسوة والتحرير والصوم، فليس بصحيح تأمل. (القمر) وإن أدى غير إلخ كما أنه عين أن يطعم عشرة مساكين، ثم بدأ له أن يحرر رقبة فهذا التحرير يكون أداء، وهذا بناء على أن الواجب في الواجب المخير أحد الأمور كما هو مقتضى كلمة "أو" . (القمر) إلا بكون إلخ في العبارة مسامحة والأولى أن يقول: إلا بكون الوقت في الأول ظرفا، وفي هذا الثاني معياراً . (القمر) فيطول : أي المؤقت بطول الوقت كما في الصيف. (القمر)
أو يكون الوقت معيارا له وسببًا لوجوبه کشهر رمضان عطف على قوله: إما أن يكون ظرفا وهو النوع الثاني من الأنواع الأربعة للمؤقت، ولا فرق بينه وبين القسم الأول إلا
بكون الأول ظرفا، وهذا معياراً والمعيار هو الذي استوعب المؤقت ولا يفضل عنه، فيطول
Topic of the Specific: Explanation of the imperative's implication regarding the ruling of time, built upon determination. Indeed, determination in every prayer is to perform it at the complete time. So avoiding dislike while focusing on determination can never combine. Thus this amount of dislike is made excusable. Its ruling: the condition of specifying intention, meaning from the ruling of this category which is a container, specifying intention is required, such that one says: 'I intend to pray Zuhr today', and absolute intention is not valid; because since time is a container suitable for the timely and other supererogatory prayers, and for make-up, intention must be specified. And it is not dropped due to tightness of time, meaning if time becomes tight for expansion due to his negligence until the end of time, or due to sleep or forgetfulness, specification is not dropped from his liability; because the tightness only came due to an accidental cause, and originally there was spaciousness. Al-Majmu'i: It became obligatory completely upon determination: Know that legislated rulings are of two types: determination, which is a name for that which is foundational, not attached to accidents; and concession, which is what is legislated considering an accident. (Al-Qamar) 'in every prayer': the word 'every' here is individual, and whoever understands 'every' as general has gone far, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'to perform' etc. due to the succession of Allah's blessings upon the servant, and He has given him authority to spend some times for his own needs as a concession. (Al-Qamar) 'excusable' but a discussion remains: if one begins Asr at the complete time and prolongs it until the deficient time enters, and finishes before the last time, then this prayer is permissible even though its cause is complete and it was performed in a deficient manner, and there is no building upon determination as apparent, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'which is a container' has some imprecision, and better to say: 'whose time is a container'. (Al-Qamar) 'by saying' etc.: or he intends in his heart a specific one. (Al-Qamar) 'Zuhr of today' indicates that the intended specification is specification of the obligation of the time, and if he intends 'obligation of Zuhr' it is not sufficient, because the obligation of Zuhr can be performance or make-up, so performance is not specified except by mentioning the obligation of the time. Thus said Ibn al-Malik. And in Mishkat al-Anwar: that the intention of Zuhr coupled with 'today' is specification even if time has exited, and likewise coupled with 'time' if time has not exited, and 'obligation of the time' is like 'Zuhr of the time'. If he intends 'obligation of Zuhr', then in Fatawa al-Atabi the soundest is that it suffices him; because the possibility of a missed prayer upon him is only probable and not considered. (Al-Qamar) 'and it is not dropped' etc.: repelling an anticipated objection, its formulation: since the requirement of specifying intention is due to the cause that time is suitable for the timely and other prayers, it would follow that specifying intention is not a condition when time is tight, because the mentioned cause is absent. So he replied that this tightness is not considered because it is accidental; since time originally is expansive, so specifying intention is required in the case of tightness also considering the original time. (Al-Sunbuli) 'when time becomes tight' i.e., such that it does not accommodate except this obligatory prayer. (Al-Qamar) And it is not specified by specification except by performance: i.e., if one specifies the beginning, middle, or end of time, it is not specified by his verbal or intentional specification until he performs. So in whatever time he performs, that time becomes specified, and if he does not perform in the time he specified but in another part, it is not called make-up. Like the one who breaks an oath: he has a choice in its expiation among three things: feeding ten poor, or clothing them, or freeing a slave. If he specifies one of them verbally or in intent, it is not specified in the sight of Allah until he performs it. When he performs, it becomes specified, and if he performs other than what he specified, he is not considered performing. It is not called make-up: for the obligation in the expansive time is performance in any part of the time. And what some Shafi'is said that the first part is specified for performance and in other than the first part it is make-up, and some Hanafis that the last part is specified for performance, that if one performs in the first it becomes supererogatory by which the obligation is dropped, is incorrect. For the command was expansive, so every part of the time is a time for complying with the order. So specification of the first or last is a restriction and contrary to the command, so reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'he has a choice in its expiation' etc. And if he does not find these three things, then upon him is fasting three days as the Quran declares. So the choice is only among these three, not including fasting. So what is in the circulating statement that the breaker of oath is given choice between feeding, clothing, freeing, and fasting is not correct, reflect. (Al-Qamar) 'and if he performs other than' etc. For example, if he specified that he would feed ten poor, then it occurred to him to free a slave, this freeing is considered performance. This is based on the fact that the obligation in a categorized obligation is one of the things as required by the word 'or'. (Al-Qamar) 'except by being' etc. There is imprecision in the phrasing; better to say: except that in the first category time is a container, and in this second category it is a measure. (Al-Qamar) 'it prolongs' i.e., the time-bound obligation prolongs with the length of time as in summer. Or time is a measure for it and a cause for its obligation, like the month of Ramadan, coordinated with his saying: 'either it is a container' which is the second type of the four types for the time-bound. There is no difference between it and the first category except that the first is a container and this is a measure. The measure is that which encompasses the time-bound and does not exceed it, so it lengthens.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the section regarding the 'specific' topic in usul al-fiqh, focusing on the ruling of time for prayers and the requirement of specifying intention (ta'yin al-niyyah). The author begins by establishing that the ruling for obligatory prayers is built upon 'azima (determination) meaning one should perform the prayer at its complete optimal time. However, to avoid hardship, a slight degree of makruh (dislike) is excused. The key ruling discussed is that for time-bound prayers like Zuhr, one must specify the intention by saying 'I intend to pray Zuhr today' because the time is a container that can accommodate both the obligatory prayer and supererogatory prayers, as well as make-up prayers. Without specification, the intention is general and insufficient. This specification is not dropped even if time becomes tight due to one's own negligence, sleep, or forgetfulness, because the original time is expansive. The commentary then defines 'azima and rukhsah: 'azima is the foundational ruling not attached to accidental circumstances, while rukhsah is a ruling legislated considering an accident. The commentator Al-Qamar raises a subtle issue about performing Asr in the complete time but extending it into the deficient time—this is still valid despite being performed in a deficient manner, which shows the ruling is not strictly built on 'azima. Next, the passage clarifies that specification of intention does not become binding upon the specified part of time until one actually performs the prayer. This is analogous to the expiation for breaking an oath: one may choose between feeding, clothing, or freeing a slave, but the choice becomes binding only upon actual performance. Therefore, if a person intends to pray at the beginning of the time but ends up praying at the end, it is still considered ada (timely performance), not qada (make-up). The commentary then rejects the views of some Shafi'is (that the first part is specified for performance) and some Hanafis (that the last part is specified) as incorrect, because the command is expansive and any part of the time is valid for compliance. Finally, the passage introduces the classification of time-bound obligations into two categories: time as a container (zarf) for obligations like daily prayers where the time extends beyond the act, and time as a measure (mi'yar) for obligations like Ramadan fasting where the time exactly encompasses the act. The difference is that in the first category, the time is a container and the act may be shorter, while in the second, the act fills the entire time.

Key Terms
عزيمة (azima): A foundational legal rule not attached to accidental circumstances; the original strict ruling.
رخصة (rukhsa): A ruling legislated due to an accidental circumstance, providing concession.
ظرف (zarf): A container; time that extends beyond the act itself, allowing flexibility.
معيار (mi'yar): A measure; time that exactly encompasses the obligated act, leaving no room for delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following statements is correct regarding the specification of intention for the Zuhr prayer?
A) A general intention like 'I intend to pray the obligatory prayer' is sufficient because the time is a container.
B) The intention must specify 'Zuhr' because the time can also accommodate supererogatory and make-up prayers.
C) Specification is only required if one is praying at the last part of the time.
D) If time becomes tight due to negligence, specification is not required.

Key Takeaway
For prayers whose time is a container, specifying the prayer by name in intention is obligatory, and this obligation is not affected by temporal tightness, as the ruling is based on the original expansive nature of time.
